### Running the Example Application

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/packages/angular/README.md

Instructions for setting up and running the example application, which combines Angular and Express.js. It covers navigating to the example directory, setting up environment variables (like API keys), and starting the development servers.

```bash
# Navigate to example
cd examples/angular-chat

# Set up environment
echo "OPENAI_API_KEY=your_key_here" > .env

# Start development (Angular + Express)
pnpm start

# Starts:
# - Angular dev server: http://localhost:4200
# - Express API server: http://localhost:3000
# - Proxy routes /api/* to Express
```

```bash
# Create .env file with your OpenAI API key

# Start the app
pnpm start
```

### Computer Tool Setup with Anthropic

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/05-computer-use.mdx

Defines a computer tool for the AI SDK using the Anthropic provider. This tool includes display dimensions and custom logic for executing actions like taking screenshots or performing other computer interactions. It also specifies how to convert tool results back into a model-understandable format.

```typescript
import { anthropic } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { getScreenshot, executeComputerAction } from '@/utils/computer-use';

const computerTool = anthropic.tools.computer_20250124({
  displayWidthPx: 1920,
  displayHeightPx: 1080,
  execute: async ({ action, coordinate, text }) => {
    switch (action) {
      case 'screenshot': {
        return {
          type: 'image',
          data: getScreenshot(),
        };
      }
      default: {
        return executeComputerAction(action, coordinate, text);
      }
    }
  },
  toModelOutput(result) {
    return typeof result === 'string'
      ? [{ type: 'text', text: result }]
      : [{ type: 'image', data: result.data, mediaType: 'image/png' }];
  },
});
```

### Generate Text with OpenAI o3-mini

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/24-o3.mdx

Demonstrates how to call the `generateText` function from the AI SDK to interact with the OpenAI o3-mini model. It shows the basic setup for sending a prompt and receiving a text response.

```typescript
import { generateText } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: openai('o3-mini'),
  prompt: 'Explain the concept of quantum entanglement.',
});
```

### Prompt Engineering Examples

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/06-advanced/01-prompt-engineering.mdx

Demonstrates various prompt engineering techniques for LLMs, including simple instructions, specific instructions, and few-shot learning with examples. These examples illustrate how to guide LLM responses for tasks like slogan generation.

```APIDOC
APIDOC:
  Prompting Techniques:

  1. Simple Instruction:
    Input: "Create a slogan for a coffee shop."
    Description: Basic prompt to generate a slogan.

  2. Specific Instruction:
    Input: "Create a slogan for an organic coffee shop."
    Description: Adds specificity to the prompt to influence the output.

  3. Instruction with Detail:
    Input: "Create three slogans for a coffee shop with live music."
    Description: Includes more details in the prompt, though the model might miss nuances.

  4. Few-Shot Learning with Examples:
    Input: "Create three slogans for a business with unique features.\n\nBusiness: Bookstore with cats\nSlogans: \"Purr-fect Pages\", \"Books and Whiskers\", \"Novels and Nuzzles\"\nBusiness: Gym with rock climbing\nSlogans: \"Peak Performance\", \"Reach New Heights\", \"Climb Your Way Fit\"\nBusiness: Coffee shop with live music\nSlogans:"
    Description: Provides examples of desired input-output pairs to guide the model towards generating similar, high-quality outputs. This technique is known as few-shot learning.
```

### RAG Input/Output Example (No Context)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/01-rag-chatbot.mdx

Demonstrates a basic interaction with an LLM where it cannot answer a personal question due to lack of external information. This highlights the need for RAG.

```txt
**input**
What is my favorite food?

**generation**
I don't have access to personal information about individuals, including their
favorite foods.

```

### RAG Input/Output Example (With Context)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/01-rag-chatbot.mdx

Illustrates how providing relevant context to an LLM, alongside the user's prompt, augments its generation capabilities and allows it to answer specific questions accurately.

```txt
**input**
Respond to the user's prompt using only the provided context.
user prompt: 'What is my favorite food?'
context: user loves chicken nuggets

**generation**
Your favorite food is chicken nuggets!

```

### Build Chat Interface with useChat Hook

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/24-o3.mdx

Example of a root page component (`app/page.tsx`) using the `useChat` hook from AI SDK UI. It manages chat messages, user input, and submission, rendering the conversation and a form for user interaction.

```tsx
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';

export default function Page() {
  const { messages, input, handleInputChange, handleSubmit, error } = useChat();

  return (
    <>
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id}>
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.content}
        </div>
      ))}
      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit}>
        <input name="prompt" value={input} onChange={handleInputChange} />
        <button type="submit">Submit</button>
      </form>
    </>
  );
}
```

### Call Llama 3.1 with DeepInfra

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/21-llama-3_1.mdx

Demonstrates how to use the AI SDK to call the Llama 3.1 405B Instruct model via the DeepInfra provider. This example uses the `generateText` function to retrieve a text response for a given prompt.

```typescript
import { deepinfra } from '@ai-sdk/deepinfra';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: deepinfra('meta-llama/Meta-Llama-3.1-405B-Instruct'),
  prompt: 'What is love?',
});
```

### Migrate AI Models with Unified API

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/21-llama-3_1.mdx

This example showcases the AI SDK's unified API for generating text, illustrating how to switch between different AI models and providers with minimal code modifications. The core `generateText` function remains consistent, abstracting away provider-specific details.

```tsx
import { generateText } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-4.1'),
  prompt: 'What is love?',
});
```

```tsx
import { generateText } from 'ai';
import { deepinfra } from '@ai-sdk/deepinfra';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: deepinfra('meta-llama/Meta-Llama-3.1-70B-Instruct'),
  prompt: 'What is love?',
});
```

```javascript
const result = streamText({

  prompt: 'Open the browser and navigate to vercel.com',
  tools: { computer: computerTool },

for await (const chunk of result.textStream) {
  console.log(chunk);
}
```

### Node.js Braintrust Span Processor Setup

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/05-observability/braintrust.mdx

Configures the OpenTelemetry Node.js SDK with the BraintrustSpanProcessor for tracing LLM applications. Installs necessary packages and starts the SDK. Requires `ai`, `@ai-sdk/openai`, `braintrust`, `@opentelemetry/sdk-node`, `@opentelemetry/sdk-trace-base`, and `zod`.

```bash
npm install ai @ai-sdk/openai braintrust @opentelemetry/sdk-node @opentelemetry/sdk-trace-base zod
```

```typescript
import { NodeSDK } from '@opentelemetry/sdk-node';
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';
import { BraintrustSpanProcessor } from 'braintrust';

const sdk = new NodeSDK({
  spanProcessors: [
    new BraintrustSpanProcessor({
      parent: 'project_name:your-project-name',
      filterAISpans: true,
    }),
  ],
});

sdk.start();

async function main() {
  const result = await generateText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o-mini'),
    messages: [
      {
        role: 'user',
        content: 'What are my orders and where are they? My user ID is 123',
      },
    ],
    tools: {
      listOrders: tool({
        description: 'list all orders',
        parameters: z.object({ userId: z.string() }),
        execute: async ({ userId }) =>
          `User ${userId} has the following orders: 1`,
      }),
      viewTrackingInformation: tool({
        description: 'view tracking information for a specific order',
        parameters: z.object({ orderId: z.string() }),
        execute: async ({ orderId }) =>
          `Here is the tracking information for ${orderId}`,
      }),
    },
    experimental_telemetry: {
      isEnabled: true,
      functionId: 'my-awesome-function',
      metadata: {
        something: 'custom',
        someOtherThing: 'other-value',
      },
    },
    maxSteps: 10,
  });

  await sdk.shutdown();
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

### Configure Multi-Step Generations with stopWhen

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/05-computer-use.mdx

Configures the `streamText` function to allow multi-step agentic generations by using the `stopWhen` parameter with `stepCountIs`. This enables the model to perform multiple actions sequentially without explicit user intervention between steps.

```javascript
import { stepCountIs } from 'ai';

const stream = streamText({
  model: anthropic('claude-sonnet-4-20250514'),
  prompt: 'Open the browser and navigate to vercel.com',
  tools: { computer: computerTool },
  stopWhen: stepCountIs(10), // experiment with this value based on your use case
});
```

### Helicone Proxy vs. OpenTelemetry Setup

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/05-observability/helicone.mdx

Compares the minimal code required for Helicone's proxy integration against a more complex OpenTelemetry (OTEL) setup for observability. Helicone's approach avoids multiple package installations and extensive SDK configuration.

```javascript
const openai = createOpenAI({
  baseURL: "https://oai.helicone.ai/v1",
  headers: { "Helicone-Auth": `Bearer ${process.env.HELICONE_API_KEY}` },
});
```

```javascript
// Install multiple packages
// @vercel/otel, @opentelemetry/sdk-node, @opentelemetry/auto-instrumentations-node, etc.

// Create exporter
const exporter = new OtherProviderExporter({
  projectApiKey: process.env.API_KEY
});

// Setup SDK
const sdk = new NodeSDK({
  traceExporter: exporter,
  instrumentations: [getNodeAutoInstrumentations()],
  resource: new Resource({...}),
});

// Start SDK
sdk.start();

// Enable telemetry on each request
const response = await generateText({
  model: openai("gpt-4o-mini"),
  prompt: "Hello world",
  experimental_telemetry: { isEnabled: true }
});

// Shutdown SDK to flush traces
await sdk.shutdown();
```

### Gemini 2.5 Tool Calling with AI SDK

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/17-gemini-2-5.mdx

Demonstrates how to use tool calling with Gemini 2.5 models via the AI SDK. This example defines a 'weather' tool using Zod for schema validation and an `execute` function, allowing the LLM to interact with external systems. It also shows optional `stopWhen` for multi-step execution.

```typescript
import { z } from 'zod';
import { generateText, tool, stepCountIs } from 'ai';
import { google } from '@ai-sdk/google';

const result = await generateText({
  model: google('gemini-2.5-flash'),
  prompt: 'What is the weather in San Francisco?',
  tools: {
    weather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => ({
        location,
        temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10,
      }),
    }),
  },
  stopWhen: stepCountIs(5), // Optional, enables multi step calling
});

console.log(result.text);

console.log(result.steps);
```

### Next.js Chat API Route Handler with Gemini

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/17-gemini-2-5.mdx

Example of a Next.js API route handler (`app/api/chat/route.ts`) that streams text responses from the Gemini 2.5 Flash model. It processes incoming messages and returns a UI message stream.

```tsx
import {
  google
} from '@ai-sdk/google';
import { streamText, UIMessage, convertToModelMessages } from 'ai';

// Allow streaming responses up to 30 seconds
export const maxDuration = 30;

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: google('gemini-2.5-flash'),
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### Gemini 2.5 Text Generation with Thinking Process

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/17-gemini-2-5.mdx

Illustrates how to enable Gemini 2.5's internal 'thinking process' for improved reasoning and multi-step planning. This snippet shows how to configure `thinkingBudget` and `includeThoughts` within `providerOptions` to get detailed reasoning summaries alongside the text response.

```typescript
import { google } from '@ai-sdk/google';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text, reasoning } = await generateText({
  model: google('gemini-2.5-flash'),
  prompt: 'What is the sum of the first 10 prime numbers?',
  providerOptions: {
    google: {
      thinkingConfig: {
        thinkingBudget: 8192,
        includeThoughts: true,
      },
    },
  },
});

console.log(text); // text response
console.log(reasoning); // reasoning summary
```

### Generate Structured Data with OpenAI GPT-4.5 and Zod

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/22-gpt-4-5.mdx

This example shows how to generate structured JSON data that conforms to a specified Zod schema using GPT-4.5 and the AI SDK. It leverages the 'generateObject' function and requires 'ai', '@ai-sdk/openai', and 'zod'. The output is a type-safe object matching the schema.

```typescript
import { generateObject } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { object } = await generateObject({
  model: openai('gpt-4.5-preview'),
  schema: z.object({
    recipe: z.object({
      name: z.string(),
      ingredients: z.array(z.object({ name: z.string(), amount: z.string() })),
      steps: z.array(z.string()),
    }),
  }),
  prompt: 'Generate a lasagna recipe.',
});
```

--------------------------------

### Computer Tool Setup and Execution

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/16-google-vertex.mdx

Demonstrates how to initialize and use the Computer Tool for interacting with a computer's interface. It includes example logic for handling actions like taking screenshots and executing generic commands.

```typescript
const computerTool = vertexAnthropic.tools.computer_20241022({
  displayWidthPx: 1920,
  displayHeightPx: 1080,
  displayNumber: 0, // Optional, for X11 environments

  execute: async ({ action, coordinate, text }) => {
    // Implement your computer control logic here
    // Return the result of the action

    // Example code:
    switch (action) {
      case 'screenshot': {
        // multipart result:
        return {
          type: 'image',
          data: fs
            .readFileSync('./data/screenshot-editor.png')
            .toString('base64'),
        };
      }
      default: {
        console.log('Action:', action);
        console.log('Coordinate:', coordinate);
        console.log('Text:', text);
        return `executed ${action}`;
      }
    }
  },

  // map to tool result content for LLM consumption:
  toModelOutput(result) {
    return typeof result === 'string'
      ? [{ type: 'text', text: result }]
      : [{ type: 'image', data: result.data, mediaType: 'image/png' }];
  },
});
```

--------------------------------

### Stream UI Components with Server Actions and Tools

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/21-llama-3_1.mdx

Demonstrates how to stream dynamic React components from a Next.js Server Action using AI SDK RSC's `streamUI` function. This example integrates tool usage, allowing the AI to call a `getWeather` tool and yield intermediate UI states (like loading) before returning the final component.

```tsx
'use server';

import { streamUI } from '@ai-sdk/rsc';
import { deepinfra } from '@ai-sdk/deepinfra';
import { z } from 'zod';

export async function streamComponent() {
  const result = await streamUI({
    model: deepinfra('meta-llama/Meta-Llama-3.1-70B-Instruct'),
    prompt: 'Get the weather for San Francisco',
    text: ({ content }) => <div>{content}</div>,
    tools: {
      getWeather: {
        description: 'Get the weather for a location',
        inputSchema: z.object({ location: z.string() }),
        generate: async function* ({ location }) {
          yield <div>loading...</div>;
          const weather = '25c'; // await getWeather(location);
          return (
            <div>
              the weather in {location} is {weather}.
            </div>
          );
        },
      },
    },
  });
  return result.value;
}
```

### OpenAI API Key Configuration

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/examples/next-openai-telemetry/app/README.md

Instructions for setting up the OpenAI API key locally. This involves signing up on the OpenAI platform, generating an API key, and storing it in a `.env.local` file for the application to use.

```APIDOC
OpenAI API Key Setup:

1. Sign up at OpenAI's Developer Platform: https://platform.openai.com/signup
2. Generate an API Key from your OpenAI dashboard: https://platform.openai.com/account/api-keys
3. Create a `.env.local` file in your project root.
4. Set the `OPENAI_API_KEY` environment variable in `.env.local` with your generated API key.
   Example `.env.local` content:
   OPENAI_API_KEY=your_openai_api_key_here

This key is essential for the application to authenticate with OpenAI services.
```

### Call DeepSeek R1 via Groq with Reasoning Middleware

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/25-r1.mdx

Illustrates integrating DeepSeek R1 models via the Groq provider using the AI SDK. It employs `wrapLanguageModel` and `extractReasoningMiddleware` to capture reasoning output identified by the '<think>' tag.

```ts
import { groq } from '@ai-sdk/groq';
import {
  generateText,
  wrapLanguageModel,
  extractReasoningMiddleware,
} from 'ai';

// middleware to extract reasoning tokens
const enhancedModel = wrapLanguageModel({
  model: groq('deepseek-r1-distill-llama-70b'),
  middleware: extractReasoningMiddleware({ tagName: 'think' }),
});

const { reasoningText, text } = await generateText({
  model: enhancedModel,
  prompt: 'Explain quantum entanglement.',
});
```

### Create and Use MCPClient Example

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/01-ai-sdk-core/23-create-mcp-client.mdx

A TypeScript example demonstrating how to initialize the MCPClient with a stdio transport, retrieve available tools, and use them with the generateText function. Includes basic try-finally block for client cleanup.

```typescript
import { experimental_createMCPClient, generateText } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';

try {
  const client = await experimental_createMCPClient({
    transport: {
      type: 'stdio',
      command: 'node server.js',
    },
  });

  const tools = await client.tools();

  const response = await generateText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o-mini'),
    tools,
    messages: [{ role: 'user', content: 'Query the data' }],
  });

  console.log(response);
} finally {
  await client.close();
}
```

### SvelteKit API: Stream GPT-4o Chat with AI SDK

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/04-svelte.mdx

Creates a SvelteKit POST endpoint to handle chat messages. It uses the AI SDK's `createOpenAI` and `streamText` functions to interact with the GPT-4o model, processing `UIMessage` input and returning a streamed response. Requires `@ai-sdk/openai` and `$env/static/private` for API key.

```ts
import { createOpenAI } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { streamText, type UIMessage, convertToModelMessages } from 'ai';

import { OPENAI_API_KEY } from '$env/static/private';

const openai = createOpenAI({
  apiKey: OPENAI_API_KEY,
});

export async function POST({ request }) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await request.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### Instance Synchronization with Context in Svelte

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/04-svelte.mdx

Shows how to achieve instance synchronization in Svelte using `createAIContext`. This allows multiple instances of hooks with the same `id` to share state, mimicking behavior found in other frameworks.

```svelte
<script>
  import { createAIContext } from '@ai-sdk/svelte';

  let { children } = $props();

  createAIContext();
  // all hooks created after this or in components that are children of this component
  // will have synchronized state
</script>

{@render children()}
```

```bash
├── src/
│   ├── example-chat-settings.ts       # Chat model types and settings
│   ├── example-completion-settings.ts # Completion model types and settings

├── tsconfig.json
├── tsup.config.ts                     # Build configuration
└── README.md
```

### Use Google Search Grounding with Gemini AI SDK

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/17-gemini-2-5.mdx

Demonstrates how to enable Gemini models to access the latest information via Google Search using the AI SDK. It shows importing necessary modules, configuring the model with search tools, and accessing grounding metadata and safety ratings from the response.

```ts
import {
  google
} from '@ai-sdk/google';
import { GoogleGenerativeAIProviderMetadata } from '@ai-sdk/google';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text, sources, providerMetadata } = await generateText({
  model: google('gemini-2.5-flash'),
  tools: {
    google_search: google.tools.googleSearch({}),
  },
  prompt:
    'List the top 5 San Francisco news from the past week.' +
    'You must include the date of each article.',
});

// access the grounding metadata. Casting to the provider metadata type
// is optional but provides autocomplete and type safety.
const metadata = providerMetadata?.google as
  | GoogleGenerativeAIProviderMetadata
  | undefined;
const groundingMetadata = metadata?.groundingMetadata;
const safetyRatings = metadata?.safetyRatings;
```

### Provider Registry: Setup

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/03-ai-sdk-core/45-provider-management.mdx

Set up a provider registry to manage multiple AI providers and models centrally. This example registers Anthropic and OpenAI providers, configuring OpenAI with an API key.

```ts
import { anthropic } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { createOpenAI } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { createProviderRegistry } from 'ai';

export const registry = createProviderRegistry({
  // register provider with prefix and default setup:
  anthropic,

  // register provider with prefix and custom setup:
  openai: createOpenAI({
    apiKey: process.env.OPENAI_API_KEY,
  }),
});
```

### API Route: Enable Multi-Step Tool Calls

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/04-svelte.mdx

Configures an API route to handle chat messages, enabling multi-step tool calls by setting `stopWhen` to `stepCountIs(5)`. It defines a 'weather' tool with input validation using Zod and an execution function.

```typescript
import { createOpenAI } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import {
  streamText,
  type UIMessage,
  convertToModelMessages,
  tool,
  stepCountIs,
} from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

import { OPENAI_API_KEY } from '$env/static/private';

const openai = createOpenAI({
  apiKey: OPENAI_API_KEY,
});

export async function POST({ request }) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await request.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
    stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
    tools: {
      weather: tool({
        description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ location }) => {
          const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
          return {
            location,
            temperature,
          };
        },
      }),
    },
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

--------------------------------

### Combine Multiple AI Tools in a Request

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/05-computer-use.mdx

Demonstrates how to define and combine different Computer Use tools (computer, bash, text editor) and pass them to the generateText function for complex task execution. This allows for sequential operations like file creation, modification, and terminal commands within a single AI interaction.

```typescript
const computerTool = anthropic.tools.computer_20250124({
  // ... configuration for computer tool
});

const bashTool = anthropic.tools.bash_20250124({
  execute: async ({ command, restart }) => execSync(command).toString()
});

const textEditorTool = anthropic.tools.textEditor_20250124({
  execute: async ({
    command,
    path,
    file_text,
    insert_line,
    new_str,
    old_str,
    view_range
  }) => {
    // Handle file operations based on command
    switch(command) {
      case 'create':
      case 'write':
      case 'delete':
      case 'insert':
      case 'replace':
      case 'view':
        return executeTextEditorFunction({
          command,
          path,
          fileText: file_text,
          insertLine: insert_line,
          newStr: new_str,
          oldStr: old_str,
          viewRange: view_range
        });
      default:
        throw new Error(`Unknown text editor command: ${command}`);
    }
  }
});


const response = await generateText({
  model: anthropic("claude-sonnet-4-20250514"),
  prompt: "Create a new file called example.txt, write 'Hello World' to it, and run 'cat example.txt' in the terminal",
  tools: {
    computer: computerTool,
    bash: bashTool,
    str_replace_editor: textEditorTool,
  },
});
```

### Svelte UI: Chat Interface with AI SDK

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/04-svelte.mdx

Implements a Svelte chat interface using the AI SDK's `Chat` class. It displays messages and provides an input form for user interaction. The `Chat` class handles sending messages to the API and managing the chat state, abstracting the complexity of UI interactions.

```svelte
<script lang="ts">
  import { Chat } from '@ai-sdk/svelte';

  let input = '';
  const chat = new Chat({});

  function handleSubmit(event: SubmitEvent) {
    event.preventDefault();
    chat.sendMessage({ text: input });
    input = '';
  }
</script>

<main>
  <ul>
    {#each chat.messages as message, messageIndex (messageIndex)}
      <li>
        <div>{message.role}</div>
        <div>
          {#each message.parts as part, partIndex (partIndex)}
            {#if part.type === 'text'}
              <div>{part.text}</div>
            {/if}
          {/each}
        </div>
      </li>
    {/each}
  </ul>
  <form onsubmit={handleSubmit}>
    <input bind:value={input} />
    <button type="submit">Send</button>
  </form>
</main>
```

### Integrate Caching Middleware with AI SDK

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/05-node/80-local-caching-middleware.mdx

Demonstrates integrating a caching middleware into an AI SDK setup using TypeScript. This example shows streaming text generation with a cached model, utilizing the `cached` function for local development. It includes setup with environment variables and processing of streamed output, token usage, and finish reason.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { streamText } from 'ai';
import 'dotenv/config';
import { cached } from '../middleware/your-cache-middleware';

async function main() {
  const result = streamText({
    model: cached(openai('gpt-4o')),
    maxOutputTokens: 512,
    temperature: 0.3,
    maxRetries: 5,
    prompt: 'Invent a new holiday and describe its traditions.',
  });

  for await (const textPart of result.textStream) {
    process.stdout.write(textPart);
  }

  console.log();
  console.log('Token usage:', await result.usage);
  console.log('Finish reason:', await result.finishReason);
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

### Svelte UI: Display Tool Invocations

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/04-svelte.mdx

Updates a Svelte component to display chat messages, including specific handling for 'text' and 'tool-weather' parts. It iterates through messages and their parts, rendering tool results as JSON.

```svelte
<script lang="ts">
  import { Chat } from '@ai-sdk/svelte';

  let input = '';
  const chat = new Chat({});

  function handleSubmit(event: SubmitEvent) {
    event.preventDefault();
    chat.sendMessage({ text: input });
    input = '';
  }
</script>

<main>
  <ul>
    {#each chat.messages as message, messageIndex (messageIndex)}
      <li>
        <div>{message.role}</div>
        <div>
          {#each message.parts as part, partIndex (partIndex)}
            {#if part.type === 'text'}
              <div>{part.text}</div>
            {:else if part.type === 'tool-weather'}
              <pre>{JSON.stringify(part, null, 2)}</pre>
            {/if}
          {/each}
        </div>
      </li>
    {/each}
  </ul>
  <form onsubmit={handleSubmit}>
    <input bind:value={input} />
    <button type="submit">Send</button>
  </form>
</main>
```

### Call DeepSeek R1 via Fireworks with Reasoning Middleware

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/25-r1.mdx

Shows how to use the AI SDK to call DeepSeek R1 through the Fireworks provider. It utilizes `wrapLanguageModel` and `extractReasoningMiddleware` to process reasoning tokens tagged with '<think>'.

```ts
import { fireworks } from '@ai-sdk/fireworks';
import {
  generateText,
  wrapLanguageModel,
  extractReasoningMiddleware,
} from 'ai';

// middleware to extract reasoning tokens
const enhancedModel = wrapLanguageModel({
  model: fireworks('accounts/fireworks/models/deepseek-r1'),
  middleware: extractReasoningMiddleware({ tagName: 'think' }),
});

const { reasoningText, text } = await generateText({
  model: enhancedModel,
  prompt: 'Explain quantum entanglement.',
});
```

### Add Weather Tool to API Route

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/04-svelte.mdx

Updates the API route (`src/routes/api/chat/+server.ts`) to include a weather tool. This tool uses Zod for input schema validation and simulates fetching weather data.

```tsx
import {
  streamText,
  type UIMessage,
  convertToModelMessages,
  tool,
  stepCountIs,
} from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

import { OPENAI_API_KEY } from '$env/static/private';

const openai = createOpenAI({
  apiKey: OPENAI_API_KEY,
});

export async function POST({ request }) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await request.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
    tools: {
      weather: tool({
        description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ location }) => {
          const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
          return {
            location,
            temperature,
          };
        },
      }),
    },
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### Control Reasoning Effort for o3-mini

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/24-o3.mdx

Shows how to control the reasoning effort level (`low`, `medium`, `high`) for the o3-mini model using the `providerOptions` parameter in the `generateText` function. This allows tuning for speed or accuracy.

```typescript
import { generateText } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';

// Reduce reasoning effort for faster responses
const { text } = await generateText({
  model: openai('o3-mini'),
  prompt: 'Explain quantum entanglement briefly.',
  providerOptions: {
    openai: { reasoningEffort: 'low' },
  },
});
```

### AI SDK Tool Integration Concepts

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/06-nodejs.mdx

This documentation outlines the capabilities of the AI SDK for integrating tools, enabling AI models to interact with external systems and real-world data. It details the multi-step process where models can call tools, process results, and use that information for more accurate responses, bridging knowledge gaps and enabling actions.

```APIDOC
AI SDK Tooling:
  Purpose: Extend AI model capabilities by allowing them to access external data, perform actions, and integrate with real-world systems.

  Key Features:
    - Tool Definition: Define tools with descriptions and input schemas (using Zod) to guide the model.
    - Multi-step Execution: Models can chain tool calls to gather information sequentially.
    - Real-time Data Access: Bridge the gap between the model's knowledge cutoff and current information.
    - Action Execution: Enable models to perform actions beyond text generation.

  Interaction Flow Example:
    1. User Query: User asks a question requiring external data (e.g., weather).
    2. Model Tool Call: The AI model identifies the need for a tool and calls it with appropriate parameters (e.g., `weather` tool with `location`).
    3. Tool Execution: The defined tool function executes, fetching or calculating the required data (e.g., temperature in Fahrenheit).
    4. Result Logging: Tool results are often logged or made available for further processing.
    5. Subsequent Tool Calls: The model may use the result of one tool to inform another (e.g., convert Fahrenheit to Celsius).
    6. Natural Language Response: The model synthesizes all gathered information into a coherent, natural language response.

  Benefits:
    - Increased Accuracy: Access to up-to-date information.
    - Enhanced Functionality: Ability to perform tasks and interact with services.
    - Contextual Responses: More relevant and informative answers.

  Example Scenario:
    - User asks: "What's the weather in New York in celsius?"
    - Model calls `weather` tool for 'New York', gets Fahrenheit temperature.
    - Model calls `convertFahrenheitToCelsius` tool with the received Fahrenheit temperature.
    - Model provides a response like: "The weather in New York is X degrees Celsius."
```

--------------------------------

### Implementing Agents for Multi-Step Reasoning

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/21-llama-3_1.mdx

Shows how to build agents that can perform multiple steps and tool calls to solve complex problems. By setting `maxSteps`, the LLM can reason, choose tools, and execute them iteratively, as demonstrated with a math problem solver.

```typescript
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { deepinfra } from '@ai-sdk/deepinfra';
import * as mathjs from 'mathjs';
import { z } from 'zod';

const problem =
  'Calculate the profit for a day if revenue is $5000 and expenses are $3500.';

const { text: answer } = await generateText({
  model: deepinfra('meta-llama/Meta-Llama-3.1-70B-Instruct'),
  system:
    'You are solving math problems. Reason step by step. Use the calculator when necessary.',
  prompt: problem,
  tools: {
    calculate: tool({
      description: 'A tool for evaluating mathematical expressions.',
      inputSchema: z.object({ expression: z.string() }),
      execute: async ({ expression }) => mathjs.evaluate(expression),
    }),
  },
  maxSteps: 5,
});

// 'answer' will contain the result of the agent's step-by-step calculation.
```

### Use Tool Calling for External System Interaction

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/24-o3.mdx

Illustrates how to enable AI models to interact with external systems by defining tools. The `tool` function, combined with `generateText`, allows the model to call predefined functions with specified input schemas, enhancing its ability to provide real-time information.

```ts
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: openai('o3-mini'),
  prompt: 'What is the weather like today in San Francisco?',
  tools: {
    getWeather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => ({
        location,
        temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10,
      }),
    }),
  },
});
```

### Full Image Generation Example

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/04-azure.mdx

A complete example demonstrating image generation with Azure OpenAI, including necessary imports and logging the result.

```ts
import { azure } from '@ai-sdk/azure';
import { experimental_generateImage as generateImage } from 'ai';

const { image } = await generateImage({
  model: azure.image('your-dalle-deployment-name'),
  prompt: 'A photorealistic image of a cat astronaut floating in space',
  size: '1024x1024', // '1024x1024', '1792x1024', or '1024x1792' for DALL-E 3
});

// image contains the URL or base64 data of the generated image
console.log(image);
```

### Instrument Node.js App with Langfuse

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/05-observability/langfuse.mdx

Provides a Node.js example for integrating Langfuse tracing using OpenTelemetry. It sets up the `NodeSDK` with `getNodeAutoInstrumentations` and the `LangfuseExporter`, then starts the SDK and sends traces.

```ts
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { generateText } from 'ai';
import { NodeSDK } from '@opentelemetry/sdk-node';
import { getNodeAutoInstrumentations } from '@opentelemetry/auto-instrumentations-node';
import { LangfuseExporter } from 'langfuse-vercel';

const sdk = new NodeSDK({
  traceExporter: new LangfuseExporter(),
  instrumentations: [getNodeAutoInstrumentations()],
});

sdk.start();

async function main() {
  const result = await generateText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    maxOutputTokens: 50,
    prompt: 'Invent a new holiday and describe its traditions.',
    experimental_telemetry: {
      isEnabled: true,
      functionId: 'my-awesome-function',
      metadata: {
        something: 'custom',
        someOtherThing: 'other-value',
      },
    },
  });

  console.log(result.text);

  await sdk.shutdown(); // Flushes the trace to Langfuse
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

### Example Links Component

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/01-ai-sdk-core/01-generate-text.mdx

This snippet shows how to define and pass an array of example links to a component. It includes titles and URLs for various AI functionalities in Next.js and Node.js.

```jsx
import React from 'react';

// Assuming ExampleLinks is a component that renders links based on the prop
// const ExampleLinks = ({ examples }) => (
//   <div>
//     {examples.map((example, index) => (
//       <div key={index}>
//         <a href={example.link}>{example.title}</a>
//       </div>
//     ))}
//   </div>
// );

<ExampleLinks
  examples={[
    {
      title: 'Learn to generate text using a language model in Next.js',
      link: '/examples/next-app/basics/generating-text',
    },
    {
      title:
        'Learn to generate a chat completion using a language model in Next.js',
      link: '/examples/next-app/basics/generating-text',
    },
    {
      title: 'Learn to call tools using a language model in Next.js',
      link: '/examples/next-app/tools/call-tool',
    },
    {
      title:
        'Learn to render a React component as a tool call using a language model in Next.js',
      link: '/examples/next-app/tools/render-interface-during-tool-call',
    },
    {
      title: 'Learn to generate text using a language model in Node.js',
      link: '/examples/node/generating-text/generate-text',
    },
    {
      title:
        'Learn to generate chat completions using a language model in Node.js',
      link: '/examples/node/generating-text/generate-text-with-chat-prompt',
    },
  ]}
/>
```

### Enable Extended Reasoning with Claude 4 Sonnet via AI SDK

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/18-claude-4.mdx

Shows how to enable Claude 4's extended reasoning capabilities using the AI SDK. It includes enabling the `thinking` provider option with a budget and using the `interleaved-thinking` beta header for more complex problem-solving scenarios.

```typescript
import { anthropic, AnthropicProviderOptions } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text, reasoningText, reasoning } = await generateText({
  model: anthropic('claude-sonnet-4-20250514'),
  prompt: 'How will quantum computing impact cryptography by 2050?',
  providerOptions: {
    anthropic: {
      thinking: { type: 'enabled', budgetTokens: 15000 },
    } satisfies AnthropicProviderOptions,
  },
  headers: {
    'anthropic-beta': 'interleaved-thinking-2025-05-14',
  },
});

console.log(text); // text response
console.log(reasoningText); // reasoning text
console.log(reasoning); // reasoning details including redacted reasoning
```

### Instrument Next.js App with Langfuse

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/05-observability/langfuse.mdx

Guides on setting up OpenTelemetry instrumentation for a Next.js application to send traces to Langfuse. It involves installing necessary packages and configuring the `LangfuseExporter` within the `instrumentation.ts` file.

```bash
npm install @vercel/otel langfuse-vercel @opentelemetry/api-logs @opentelemetry/instrumentation @opentelemetry/sdk-logs
```

```ts
import { registerOTel } from '@vercel/otel';
import { LangfuseExporter } from 'langfuse-vercel';

export function register() {
  registerOTel({
    serviceName: 'langfuse-vercel-ai-nextjs-example',
    traceExporter: new LangfuseExporter(),
  });
}
```

### Initialize Laminar with Sentry (Standalone)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/05-observability/laminar.mdx

Provides a code example for initializing both Sentry and Laminar, emphasizing that Laminar should be initialized after Sentry. This setup ensures that Sentry captures its traces and Laminar captures AI SDK traces.

```javascript
const Sentry = await import('@sentry/node');
const { Laminar } = await import('@lmnr-ai/lmnr');

Sentry.init({
  dsn: process.env.SENTRY_DSN,
});

Laminar.initialize({
  projectApiKey: process.env.LMNR_PROJECT_API_KEY,
});
```

```typescript
import { anthropic } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
```

```ts
const { text, reasoning, reasoningDetails } = await generateText({
  model: anthropic('claude-3-7-sonnet-20250219'),
  prompt: 'How many people will live in the world in 2040?',
});
```

### DeepSeek R1 Model Provider Details

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/25-r1.mdx

This entry details various AI SDK providers that support the DeepSeek R1 model. It includes the specific model ID required for each provider and notes on token reasoning capabilities or middleware requirements.

```APIDOC
Provider Comparison for DeepSeek R1:

- DeepSeek:
  - Model ID: `deepseek-reasoner`
  - Reasoning Tokens: Check size
  - Documentation: /providers/ai-sdk-providers/deepseek
  - Model Docs: https://api-docs.deepseek.com/guides/reasoning_model

- Fireworks:
  - Model ID: `accounts/fireworks/models/deepseek-r1`
  - Reasoning Tokens: Requires Middleware
  - Documentation: /providers/ai-sdk-providers/fireworks
  - Model Docs: https://fireworks.ai/models/fireworks/deepseek-r1

- Groq:
  - Model ID: `deepseek-r1-distill-llama-70b`
  - Reasoning Tokens: Requires Middleware
  - Documentation: /providers/ai-sdk-providers/groq
  - Model Docs: https://huggingface.co/deepseek-ai/DeepSeek-R1-Distill-Llama-70B

- Azure:
  - Model ID: `DeepSeek-R1`
  - Reasoning Tokens: Requires Middleware
  - Documentation: /providers/ai-sdk-providers/azure
  - Model Docs: https://ai.azure.com/explore/models/DeepSeek-R1/version/1/registry/azureml-deepseek#code-samples

- Together AI:
  - Model ID: `deepseek-ai/DeepSeek-R1`
  - Reasoning Tokens: Requires Middleware
  - Documentation: /providers/ai-sdk-providers/togetherai
  - Model Docs: https://www.together.ai/models/deepseek-r1

- FriendliAI:
  - Model ID: `deepseek-r1`
  - Reasoning Tokens: Requires Middleware
  - Documentation: /providers/community-providers/friendliai
  - Model Docs: https://huggingface.co/deepseek-ai/DeepSeek-R1

- LangDB:
  - Model ID: `deepseek/deepseek-reasoner`
  - Reasoning Tokens: Requires Middleware
  - Documentation: /providers/community-providers/langdb
  - Model Docs: https://docs.langdb.ai/guides/deepseek
```

### Advanced Provider Registry Configuration

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/03-ai-sdk-core/45-provider-management.mdx

An example demonstrating advanced provider management, including custom providers, model aliases, default settings, provider limitations, and custom separators. This setup allows for flexible configuration of AI models.

```typescript
import { anthropic, AnthropicProviderOptions } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { createOpenAICompatible } from '@ai-sdk/openai-compatible';
import { xai } from '@ai-sdk/xai';
import { groq } from '@ai-sdk/groq';
import {
  createProviderRegistry,
  customProvider,
  defaultSettingsMiddleware,
  wrapLanguageModel,
} from 'ai';

export const registry = createProviderRegistry(
  {
    // pass through a full provider with a namespace prefix
    xai,

    // access an OpenAI-compatible provider with custom setup
    custom: createOpenAICompatible({
      name: 'provider-name',
      apiKey: process.env.CUSTOM_API_KEY,
      baseURL: 'https://api.custom.com/v1',
    }),

    // setup model name aliases
    anthropic: customProvider({
      languageModels: {
        fast: anthropic('claude-3-haiku-20240307'),

        // simple model
        writing: anthropic('claude-3-7-sonnet-20250219'),

        // extended reasoning model configuration:
        reasoning: wrapLanguageModel({
          model: anthropic('claude-3-7-sonnet-20250219'),
          middleware: defaultSettingsMiddleware({
            settings: {
              maxOutputTokens: 100000, // example default setting
              providerOptions: {
                anthropic: {
                  thinking: {
                    type: 'enabled',
                    budgetTokens: 32000,
                  },
                } satisfies AnthropicProviderOptions,
              },
            },
          }),
        }),
      },
      fallbackProvider: anthropic,
    }),

    // limit a provider to certain models without a fallback
    groq: customProvider({
      languageModels: {
        'gemma2-9b-it': groq('gemma2-9b-it'),
        'qwen-qwq-32b': groq('qwen-qwq-32b'),
      },
    }),
  },
  { separator: ' > ' },
);

// usage:
const model = registry.languageModel('anthropic > reasoning');

```

--------------------------------

### Next.js Page with useChat Hook

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/25-r1.mdx

Implements a client-side Next.js page that uses the `useChat` hook from AI SDK UI. It manages user input, sends messages to the API, and displays chat history, including model reasoning.

```typescript
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { useState } from 'react';

export default function Page() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat();

  const handleSubmit = (e: React.FormEvent<HTMLFormElement>) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    if (input.trim()) {
      sendMessage({ text: input });
      setInput('');
    }
  };

  return (
    <>
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id}>
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.parts.map((part, index) => {
            if (part.type === 'reasoning') {
              return <pre key={index}>{part.text}</pre>;
            }
            if (part.type === 'text') {
              return <span key={index}>{part.text}</span>;
            }
            return null;
          })}
        </div>
      ))}
      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit}>
        <input
          name="prompt"
          value={input}
          onChange={e => setInput(e.target.value)}
        />
        <button type="submit">Submit</button>
      </form>
    </>
  );
}
```

--------------------------------

### Create Interactive AI Chatbot with Streaming

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/06-nodejs.mdx

Implements a command-line AI chatbot using the AI SDK. It handles user input, maintains conversation history, streams responses from the OpenAI GPT-4o model, and prints them to the terminal.

```ts
import {
  openai
} from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { ModelMessage, streamText } from 'ai';
import 'dotenv/config';
import * as readline from 'node:readline/promises';

const terminal = readline.createInterface({
  input: process.stdin,
  output: process.stdout,
});

const messages: ModelMessage[] = [];

async function main() {
  while (true) {
    const userInput = await terminal.question('You: ');

    messages.push({ role: 'user', content: userInput });

    const result = streamText({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      messages,
    });

    let fullResponse = '';
    process.stdout.write('\nAssistant: ');
    for await (const delta of result.textStream) {
      fullResponse += delta;
      process.stdout.write(delta);
    }
    process.stdout.write('\n\n');

    messages.push({ role: 'assistant', content: fullResponse });
  }
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

### Example Provider API and Implementation

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/02-openai-compatible-providers/01-custom-providers.mdx

Defines the structure for custom AI providers, including settings, model interfaces, and a factory function to create provider instances. It leverages compatible OpenAI SDK components and provider utilities.

```APIDOC
ExampleProviderSettings:
  apiKey?: string
    Example API key.
  baseURL?: string
    Base URL for the API calls.
  headers?: Record<string, string>
    Custom headers to include in the requests.
  queryParams?: Record<string, string>
    Optional custom url query parameters to include in request urls.
  fetch?: FetchFunction
    Custom fetch implementation. You can use it as a middleware to intercept requests,
or to provide a custom fetch implementation for e.g. testing.

ExampleProvider:
  (modelId: ExampleChatModelId, settings?: ExampleChatSettings): LanguageModelV1
    Creates a model for text generation.
  chatModel(modelId: ExampleChatModelId, settings?: ExampleChatSettings): LanguageModelV1
    Creates a chat model for text generation.
  completionModel(modelId: ExampleCompletionModelId, settings?: ExampleCompletionSettings): LanguageModelV1
    Creates a completion model for text generation.
  textEmbeddingModel(modelId: ExampleEmbeddingModelId, settings?: ExampleEmbeddingSettings): EmbeddingModelV2<string>
    Creates a text embedding model for text generation.
  imageModel(modelId: ExampleImageModelId, settings?: ExampleImageSettings): ImageModelV2
    Creates an image model for image generation.

createExample(options: ExampleProviderSettings = {}): ExampleProvider
  Factory function to create an instance of the ExampleProvider.
  Parameters:
    options: ExampleProviderSettings
      Configuration options for the provider, including API key, base URL, headers, query parameters, and custom fetch implementation.
  Returns:
    An instance of ExampleProvider configured with the provided options.

Example Usage:
  import { createExample } from './example-provider';

  const myProvider = createExample({
    apiKey: 'YOUR_API_KEY',
    baseURL: 'https://api.example.com/v1',
  });

  const chatModel = myProvider.chatModel('example/chat-model-1');
  const embeddingModel = myProvider.textEmbeddingModel('example/embedding-model');

  // Use chatModel and embeddingModel for AI operations.
```

### InferUITools Basic Usage Example

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/02-ai-sdk-ui/46-infer-ui-tools.mdx

Demonstrates how to use InferUITools with a sample tool set to infer input and output types for TypeScript.

```typescript
import { InferUITools } from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const tools = {
  weather: {
    description: 'Get the current weather',
    parameters: z.object({
      location: z.string().describe('The city and state'),
    }),
    execute: async ({ location }) => {
      return `The weather in ${location} is sunny.`;
    },
  },
  calculator: {
    description: 'Perform basic arithmetic',
    parameters: z.object({
      operation: z.enum(['add', 'subtract', 'multiply', 'divide']),
      a: z.number(),
      b: z.number(),
    }),
    execute: async ({ operation, a, b }) => {
      switch (operation) {
        case 'add':
          return a + b;
        case 'subtract':
          return a - b;
        case 'multiply':
          return a * b;
        case 'divide':
          return a / b;
      }
    },
  },
};

// Infer the types from the tool set
type MyUITools = InferUITools<typeof tools>;
// This creates a type with:
// {
//   weather: { input: { location: string }; output: string };
//   calculator: { input: { operation: 'add' | 'subtract' | 'multiply' | 'divide'; a: number; b: number }; output: number };
// }
```

### Reactive Class Arguments in Svelte

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/04-svelte.mdx

Demonstrates how to pass reactive arguments to a class constructor in Svelte by using a getter function to ensure the class instance always receives the latest value. This is crucial for properties that change over time.

```svelte
<script>
  import { Chat } from '@ai-sdk/svelte';

  let { id } = $props();

  // won't work; the class instance will be created once, `id` will be copied by value, and won't update when $props.id changes
  let chat = new Chat({ id });

  // will work; passes `id` by reference, so `Chat` always has the latest value
  let chat = new Chat({
    get id() {
      return id;
    },
  });
</script>
```

--------------------------------

### AI SDK streamText Configuration with stopWhen

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/01-rag-chatbot.mdx

Configures the AI SDK's `streamText` function to manage multi-step calls using the `stopWhen` parameter. This example demonstrates setting a stopping condition based on the number of steps and defining a tool for adding resources.

```tsx
import { createResource } from '@/lib/actions/resources';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import {
  convertToModelMessages,
  streamText,
  tool,
  UIMessage,
  stepCountIs,
} from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

// Allow streaming responses up to 30 seconds
export const maxDuration = 30;

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    system: `You are a helpful assistant. Check your knowledge base before answering any questions.
    Only respond to questions using information from tool calls.
    if no relevant information is found in the tool calls, respond, "Sorry, I don't know."`,
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
    stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
    tools: {
      addResource: tool({
        description: `add a resource to your knowledge base.
          If the user provides a random piece of knowledge unprompted, use this tool without asking for confirmation.`,
        inputSchema: z.object({
          content: z
            .string()
            .describe('the content or resource to add to the knowledge base'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ content }) => createResource({ content }),
      }),
    },
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### Next.js Route Handler for Chat API

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/25-r1.mdx

Defines a POST route handler for a chat endpoint in a Next.js application. It processes incoming messages, streams text from the DeepSeek model, and returns the response with optional reasoning.

```typescript
import { deepseek } from '@ai-sdk/deepseek';
import { convertToModelMessages, streamText, UIMessage } from 'ai';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: deepseek('deepseek-reasoner'),
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse({
    sendReasoning: true,
  });
}
```

### SQL Query Explanation Prompt

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/04-natural-language-postgres.mdx

This text prompt guides an AI model to explain SQL queries in plain English. It specifies the AI's role as a SQL expert, provides the database table schema, and instructs the model on how to break down a query into distinct, explainable sections.

```txt
You are a SQL (postgres) expert. Your job is to explain to the user write a SQL query you wrote to retrieve the data they asked for. The table schema is as follows:
unicorns (
  id SERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  company VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
  valuation DECIMAL(10, 2) NOT NULL,
  date_joined DATE,
  country VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
  city VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
  industry VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
  select_investors TEXT NOT NULL
);

When you explain you must take a section of the query, and then explain it. Each "section" should be unique. So in a query like: "SELECT * FROM unicorns limit 20", the sections could be "SELECT *", "FROM UNICORNS", "LIMIT 20".
If a section doesn't have any explanation, include it, but leave the explanation empty.
```

### Using System Messages with AI SDK

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-foundations/03-prompts.mdx

Illustrates how to use system messages to guide an AI assistant's behavior before user input. System messages are crucial for setting context, persona, or instructions for the AI. This example uses the `generateText` function with a `messages` array containing both system and user roles.

```ts
const result = await generateText({
  model: 'openai/gpt-4.1',
  messages: [
    { role: 'system', content: 'You help planning travel itineraries.' },
    {
      role: 'user',
      content:
        'I am planning a trip to Berlin for 3 days. Please suggest the best tourist activities for me to do.',
    },
  ],
});
```

### AI SDK RSC Usage and Limitations

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/01-navigating-the-library.mdx

Provides guidance on using AI SDK RSC, highlighting its experimental nature and recommending AI SDK UI for production. Details limitations related to cancellation, data transfer, and re-mounting issues during streaming, along with potential workarounds.

```APIDOC
AI SDK RSC (React Server Components):

Purpose: Utilities for streaming values and UI directly from server to client using React Server Components and Server Actions.

Recommendation: Use AI SDK UI for production applications. AI SDK RSC is experimental.

Limitations:
  - Cancellation: Cannot abort a stream using Server Actions. Future React/Next.js releases may improve this.
  - Increased Data Transfer: `createStreamableUI` can cause quadratic data transfer. Use `createStreamableValue` and client-side rendering to mitigate.
  - Re-mounting Issue: `createStreamableUI` can cause component re-mounting on `.done()`, leading to flickering. See issue #2232.

Related Functions:
  - createStreamableUI: For streaming UI components.
  - createStreamableValue: For streaming primitive values, recommended to avoid data transfer issues.
```

--------------------------------

### Update Frontend to Handle New Tool Output in Svelte

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/04-svelte.mdx

This Svelte component code updates the UI to correctly display output from the new 'convertFahrenheitToCelsius' tool. It modifies the message rendering logic to check for 'tool-convertFahrenheitToCelsius' part types and displays the tool's JSON output. This ensures users can see the results of tool calls in the chat interface.

```svelte
<script lang="ts">
  import { Chat } from '@ai-sdk/svelte';

  let input = '';
  const chat = new Chat({});

  function handleSubmit(event: SubmitEvent) {
    event.preventDefault();
    chat.sendMessage({ text: input });
    input = '';
  }
</script>

<main>
  <ul>
    {#each chat.messages as message, messageIndex (messageIndex)}
      <li>
        <div>{message.role}</div>
        <div>
          {#each message.parts as part, partIndex (partIndex)}
            {#if part.type === 'text'}
              <div>{part.text}</div>
            {:else if part.type === 'tool-weather' || part.type === 'tool-convertFahrenheitToCelsius'}
              <pre>{JSON.stringify(part, null, 2)}</pre>
            {/if}
          {/each}
        </div>
      </li>
    {/each}
  </ul>
  <form onsubmit={handleSubmit}>
    <input bind:value={input} />
    <button type="submit">Send</button>
  </form>
</main>
```

### Next.js Client Page with useChat Hook

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/22-gpt-4-5.mdx

A client-side React component for a Next.js application that utilizes the `useChat` hook from the AI SDK UI. It manages chat messages, user input, and submission, rendering the chat interface.

```tsx
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';

export default function Page() {
  const { messages, input, handleInputChange, handleSubmit, error } = useChat();

  return (
    <>
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id}>
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.content}
        </div>
      ))}
      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit}>
        <input name="prompt" value={input} onChange={handleInputChange} />
        <button type="submit">Submit</button>
      </form>
    </>
  );
}
```

### Generate Text with Crosshatch Context

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/03-community-providers/21-crosshatch.mdx

An example of using the Crosshatch provider with the `generateText` function to get AI-generated text. It showcases how to specify a model, provide a user access token, and inject personalized context from user data using the `replace` option.

```typescript
import { generateText } from 'ai';
import createCrosshatch from '@crosshatch/ai-provider';

const crosshatch = createCrosshatch();

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: crosshatch.languageModel("gpt-4o-mini", {
    token: 'YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN',
    replace: {
      restaurants: {
        select: ["entity_name", "entity_city", "entity_region"],
        from: "personalTimeline",
        where: [
          { field: "event", op: "=", value: "confirmed" },
          { field: "entity_subtype2", op: "=", value: "RESTAURANTS" }
        ],
        groupby: ["entity_name", "entity_city", "entity_region"],
        orderby: "count DESC",
        limit: 5
      }
    }
  }),
  system: `The user recently ate at these restaurants: {restaurants}`,
  messages: [{role: "user", content: "Where should I stay in Paris?"}]
});
```

### Next.js Route Handler for Chat

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/22-gpt-4-5.mdx

A server-side route handler for a Next.js application that processes chat messages. It uses the AI SDK to stream text responses from an OpenAI model, handling message conversion and streaming to the UI.

```tsx
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { convertToModelMessages, streamText, UIMessage } from 'ai';

// Allow responses up to 30 seconds
export const maxDuration = 30;

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-4.5-preview'),
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

--------------------------------

### Next.js Chat UI with useChat Hook

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/17-gemini-2-5.mdx

Client-side component (`app/page.tsx`) for a chat interface using the `useChat` hook from `@ai-sdk/react`. It manages user input, displays messages, and sends messages to the API route handler.

```tsx
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { useState } from 'react';

export default function Chat() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat();
  return (
    <div className="flex flex-col w-full max-w-md py-24 mx-auto stretch">
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id} className="whitespace-pre-wrap">
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'Gemini: '}
          {message.parts.map((part, i) => {
            switch (part.type) {
              case 'text':
                return <div key={`${message.id}-${i}`}>{part.text}</div>;
            }
          })}
        </div>
      ))}

      <form
        onSubmit={e => {
          e.preventDefault();
          sendMessage({ text: input });
          setInput('');
        }}
      >
        <input
          className="fixed dark:bg-zinc-900 bottom-0 w-full max-w-md p-2 mb-8 border border-zinc-300 dark:border-zinc-800 rounded shadow-xl"
          value={input}
          placeholder="Say something..."
          onChange={e => setInput(e.currentTarget.value)}
        />
      </form>
    </div>
  );
}
```

### Create Chat Route Handler with Next.js

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/24-o3.mdx

A Next.js route handler (`app/api/chat/route.ts`) that streams text responses from an AI model. It processes incoming chat messages, converts them for the AI SDK, and returns a UI message stream response.

```tsx
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { convertToModelMessages, streamText, UIMessage } from 'ai';

// Allow responses up to 5 minutes
export const maxDuration = 300;

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('o3-mini'),
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### Generate Structured Data with Zod Schema

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/24-o3.mdx

Demonstrates generating structured JSON data that conforms to a specified Zod schema using the `generateObject` function. This ensures type-safe outputs from the AI model, useful for data extraction or synthetic data generation.

```ts
import { generateObject } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { object } = await generateObject({
  model: openai('o3-mini'),
  schema: z.object({
    recipe: z.object({
      name: z.string(),
      ingredients: z.array(z.object({ name: z.string(), amount: z.string() })),
      steps: z.array(z.string()),
    }),
  }),
  prompt: 'Generate a lasagna recipe.',
});
```

### Use Tool Calling with OpenAI GPT-4.5 and AI SDK

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/22-gpt-4-5.mdx

This snippet illustrates how to enable GPT-4.5 to call external tools, allowing it to interact with APIs or perform specific tasks. It uses the 'generateText' function with a 'tools' parameter, defining a 'getWeather' tool with an input schema. This requires 'ai', '@ai-sdk/openai', and 'zod'.

```typescript
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-4.5-preview'),
  prompt: 'What is the weather like today in San Francisco?',
  tools: {
    getWeather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => ({
        location,
        temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10,
      }),
    }),
  },
});
```

### Generate Object with Disabled Structured Outputs

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/03-openai.mdx

Shows how to use `generateObject` to get structured data from OpenAI models. This example explicitly disables structured outputs using `providerOptions` and defines a Zod schema for the expected output. Requires `ai`, `@ai-sdk/openai`, and `zod`.

```ts
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { generateObject } from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const result = await generateObject({
  model: openai('gpt-4o-2024-08-06'),
  providerOptions: {
    openai: {
      structuredOutputs: false,
    },
  },
  schemaName: 'recipe',
  schemaDescription: 'A recipe for lasagna.',
  schema: z.object({
    name: z.string(),
    ingredients: z.array(
      z.object({
        name: z.string(),
        amount: z.string(),
      }),
    ),
    steps: z.array(z.string()),
  }),
  prompt: 'Generate a lasagna recipe.',
});

console.log(JSON.stringify(result.object, null, 2));
```

### Destructuring Class Properties in Svelte

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/04-svelte.mdx

Explains that destructuring class properties in Svelte, similar to vanilla JavaScript, copies them by value, disconnecting them from the original instance. This can lead to unexpected behavior when the class property is updated.

```javascript
const classInstance = new Whatever();
classInstance.foo = 'bar';
const { foo } = classInstance;
classInstance.foo = 'baz';

console.log(foo); // 'bar'
```

```svelte
<script>
  import { Chat } from '@ai-sdk/svelte';

  const chat = new Chat({});
  let { messages } = chat;

  chat.append({ content: 'Hello, world!', role: 'user' }).then(() => {
    console.log(messages); // []
    console.log(chat.messages); // [{ content: 'Hello, world!', role: 'user' }] (plus some other stuff)
  });
</script>
```

### Using Tools for LLM Extended Capabilities

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/21-llama-3_1.mdx

Illustrates how to integrate custom tools with LLMs to perform discrete tasks or interact with external systems. The `generateText` function combined with the `tool` utility allows the model to call defined functions, such as fetching weather data.

```typescript
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { deepinfra } from '@ai-sdk/deepinfra';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: deepinfra('meta-llama/Meta-Llama-3.1-70B-Instruct'),
  prompt: 'What is the weather like today?',
  tools: {
    getWeather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => ({
        location,
        temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10,
      }),
    }),
  },
});

// The model can now call the 'getWeather' tool to answer the prompt.
```

--------------------------------

### MCPClient API Methods

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/01-ai-sdk-core/23-create-mcp-client.mdx

Documentation for the MCPClient's core methods, including fetching tools and closing the connection. Covers method signatures, parameters, return types, and descriptions.

```APIDOC
MCPClient Methods:

tools(options?: { schemas?: TOOL_SCHEMAS }) => Promise<McpToolSet<TOOL_SCHEMAS>>
  - Gets the tools available from the MCP server.
  - Parameters:
    - options: Optional configuration for fetching tools.
      - schemas: Schema definitions for compile-time type checking. When not provided, schemas are inferred from the server.
  - Returns: A Promise that resolves to an McpToolSet containing the available tools.

close() => Promise<void>
  - Closes the connection to the MCP server and cleans up resources.
  - Returns: A Promise that resolves when the connection is closed.
```

### Define Weather Tool with AI Library

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/01-ai-sdk-core/20-tool.mdx

Demonstrates how to use the `tool()` helper function to define a tool for getting weather information. It specifies an input schema using Zod for the location and provides an `execute` method that simulates temperature retrieval. This setup ensures TypeScript can correctly infer the type of the `location` parameter within the `execute` function.

```typescript
import { tool } from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

export const weatherTool = tool({
  description: 'Get the weather in a location',
  inputSchema: z.object({
    location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
  }),
  // location below is inferred to be a string:
  execute: async ({ location }) => ({
    location,
    temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10,
  }),
});
```

### Generate Structured Data with Zod Schema

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/21-llama-3_1.mdx

Demonstrates how to generate structured JSON data that conforms to a specified Zod schema using the `generateObject` function. This ensures type-safe outputs from the LLM, useful for data extraction or synthetic data generation.

```typescript
import { generateObject } from 'ai';
import { deepinfra } from '@ai-sdk/deepinfra';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { object } = await generateObject({
  model: deepinfra('meta-llama/Meta-Llama-3.1-70B-Instruct'),
  schema: z.object({
    recipe: z.object({
      name: z.string(),
      ingredients: z.array(z.object({ name: z.string(), amount: z.string() })),
      steps: z.array(z.string()),
    }),
  }),
  prompt: 'Generate a lasagna recipe.',

// 'object' will be a type-safe representation of the generated recipe.
```
