### Connect and Use MCP Tools with AI SDK

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/05-node/54-mcp-tools.mdx

Demonstrates initializing MCP clients for `stdio`, `StreamableHTTP`, and `SSE` transports, retrieving tools, and integrating them with the AI SDK's `generateText` function. The example includes error handling and ensures clients are closed properly.

```ts
import { experimental_createMCPClient, generateText, stepCountIs } from 'ai';
import { Experimental_StdioMCPTransport } from 'ai/mcp-stdio';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { StdioClientTransport } from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/client/stdio';
import { SSEClientTransport } from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/client/sse';
import { StreamableHTTPClientTransport } from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/client/streamableHttp';

let clientOne;
let clientTwo;
let clientThree;

try {
  // Initialize an MCP client to connect to a `stdio` MCP server:
  const transport = new StdioClientTransport({
    command: 'node',
    args: ['src/stdio/dist/server.js'],
  });

  const clientOne = await experimental_createMCPClient({
    transport,
  });

  // You can also connect to StreamableHTTP MCP servers
  const httpTransport = new StreamableHTTPClientTransport(
    new URL('http://localhost:3000/mcp'),
  );
  const clientTwo = await experimental_createMCPClient({
    transport: httpTransport,
  });

  // Alternatively, you can connect to a Server-Sent Events (SSE) MCP server:
  const sseTransport = new SSEClientTransport(
    new URL('http://localhost:3000/sse'),
  );
  const clientThree = await experimental_createMCPClient({
    transport: sseTransport,
  });

  const toolSetOne = await clientOne.tools();
  const toolSetTwo = await clientTwo.tools();
  const toolSetThree = await clientThree.tools();
  const tools = {
    ...toolSetOne,
    ...toolSetTwo,
    ...toolSetThree, // note: this approach causes subsequent tool sets to override tools with the same name
  };

  const response = await generateText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    tools,
    stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
    messages: [
      {
        role: 'user',
        content: [{ type: 'text', text: 'Find products under $100' }],
      },
    ],
  });

  console.log(response.text);
} catch (error) {
  console.error(error);
} finally {
  await Promise.all([
    clientOne.close(),
    clientTwo.close(),
    clientThree.close(),
  ]);
}
```

--------------------------------

### Add Temperature Conversion Tool in TypeScript

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/06-nodejs.mdx

This TypeScript code snippet demonstrates adding a new tool to an AI chatbot. It defines a 'convertFahrenheitToCelsius' tool using Zod for schema validation and integrates it with the AI SDK's streaming text functionality. The example showcases how to handle multi-step tool execution within a conversational loop.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { ModelMessage, streamText, tool, stepCountIs } from 'ai';
import 'dotenv/config';
import { z } from 'zod';
import * as readline from 'node:readline/promises';

const terminal = readline.createInterface({
  input: process.stdin,
  output: process.stdout,
});

const messages: ModelMessage[] = [];

async function main() {
  while (true) {
    const userInput = await terminal.question('You: ');

    messages.push({ role: 'user', content: userInput });

    const result = streamText({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      messages,
      tools: {
        weather: tool({
          description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
          inputSchema: z.object({
            location: z
              .string()
              .describe('The location to get the weather for'),
          }),
          execute: async ({ location }) => {
            const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
            return {
              location,
              temperature,
            };
          },
        }),
        convertFahrenheitToCelsius: tool({
          description: 'Convert a temperature in fahrenheit to celsius',
          inputSchema: z.object({
            temperature: z
              .number()
              .describe('The temperature in fahrenheit to convert'),
          }),
          execute: async ({ temperature }) => {
            const celsius = Math.round((temperature - 32) * (5 / 9));
            return {
              celsius,
            };
          },
        }),
      },
      stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
      onStepFinish: async ({ toolResults }) => {
        if (toolResults.length) {
          console.log(JSON.stringify(toolResults, null, 2));
        }
      },
    });

    let fullResponse = '';
    process.stdout.write('\nAssistant: ');
    for await (const delta of result.textStream) {
      fullResponse += delta;
      process.stdout.write(delta);
    }
    process.stdout.write('\n\n');

    messages.push({ role: 'assistant', content: fullResponse });
  }
}

main().catch(console.error);

```

--------------------------------

### Frontend to Stream UI Components

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/21-llama-3_1.mdx

Provides a client-side component that triggers a Next.js Server Action (`streamComponent`) to fetch and display streamed UI elements. It uses `useState` to manage the dynamically rendered component, allowing users to initiate the streaming process with a button click.

```tsx
'use client';

import { useState } from 'react';
import { streamComponent } from './actions';

export default function Page() {
  const [component, setComponent] = useState<React.ReactNode>();

  return (
    <div>
      <form
        onSubmit={async e => {
          e.preventDefault();
          setComponent(await streamComponent());
        }}>
        <button>Stream Component</button>
      </form>
      <div>{component}</div>
    </div>
  );
}
```

### Add Fahrenheit to Celsius Tool in Chatbot Backend

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/04-svelte.mdx

This snippet demonstrates how to add a new tool, 'convertFahrenheitToCelsius', to an AI chat application's backend. It defines the tool's description, input schema using Zod, and the execution logic to perform the temperature conversion. This is integrated into the `streamText` function from '@ai-sdk/openai'.

```typescript
import {
  streamText,
  type UIMessage,
  convertToModelMessages,
  tool,
  stepCountIs,
} from 'ai';
import { createOpenAI } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

import { OPENAI_API_KEY } from '$env/static/private';

const openai = createOpenAI({
  apiKey: OPENAI_API_KEY,
});

export async function POST({ request }) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await request.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
    stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
    tools: {
      weather: tool({
        description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ location }) => {
          const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
          return {
            location,
            temperature,
          };
        },
      }),
      convertFahrenheitToCelsius: tool({
        description: 'Convert a temperature in fahrenheit to celsius',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          temperature: z
            .number()
            .describe('The temperature in fahrenheit to convert'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ temperature }) => {
          const celsius = Math.round((temperature - 32) * (5 / 9));
          return {
            celsius,
          };
        },
      }),
    },
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### Enable Claude 3.7 Sonnet Extended Thinking

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/20-sonnet-3-7.mdx

Shows how to activate Claude 3.7 Sonnet's extended thinking feature for complex reasoning tasks. It involves configuring the 'thinking' option within provider options and setting a token budget.

```ts
import { anthropic, AnthropicProviderOptions } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text, reasoning, reasoningDetails } = await generateText({
  model: anthropic('claude-3-7-sonnet-20250219'),
  prompt: 'How many people will live in the world in 2040?',
  providerOptions: {
    anthropic: {
      thinking: { type: 'enabled', budgetTokens: 12000 },
    } satisfies AnthropicProviderOptions,
  },
});

console.log(reasoning); // reasoning text
console.log(reasoningDetails); // reasoning details including redacted reasoning
console.log(text); // text response
```

### Agentic Control: prepareStep Example

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/01-announcing-ai-sdk-5-beta/index.mdx

Demonstrates the use of `prepareStep` within `generateText` to gain fine-grained control over agent steps. It shows how to dynamically change models, force tool selections, or limit available tools for a specific step.

```typescript
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const result = await generateText({
  // ... other parameters
  prepareStep: async ({ model, stepNumber, steps }) => {
    if (stepNumber === 0) {
      return {
        // use a different model for this step:
        model: modelForThisParticularStep,
        // force a tool choice for this step:
        toolChoice: { type: 'tool', toolName: 'tool1' },
        // limit the tools that are available for this step:
        activeTools: ['tool1'],
      };
    }
    // when nothing is returned, the default settings are used
  },
});
```

### customProvider Example

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/01-ai-sdk-core/42-custom-provider.mdx

Demonstrates how to create a custom provider with specific model settings and aliasing using the customProvider function.

```ts
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { customProvider } from 'ai';

// custom provider with different model settings:
export const myOpenAI = customProvider({
  languageModels: {
    // replacement model with custom settings:
    'gpt-4': wrapLanguageModel({
      model: openai('gpt-4'),
      middleware: defaultSettingsMiddleware({
        settings: {
          providerOptions: {
            openai: {
              reasoningEffort: 'high',
            },
          },
        },
      }),
    }),
    // alias model with custom settings:
    'gpt-4o-reasoning-high': wrapLanguageModel({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      middleware: defaultSettingsMiddleware({
        settings: {
          providerOptions: {
            openai: {
              reasoningEffort: 'high',
            },
          },
        },
      }),
    }),
  },
  fallbackProvider: openai,
});
```

### Implement Chat UI with useChat Hook (Next.js/React)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/18-claude-4.mdx

A React component for a Next.js application that uses the `useChat` hook from AI SDK UI to manage chat messages and send user input to the backend API. It displays messages and provides an input field for user interaction.

```tsx
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { DefaultChatTransport } from 'ai';
import { useState } from 'react';

export default function Page() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat({
    transport: new DefaultChatTransport({ api: '/api/chat' }),
  });

  const handleSubmit = (e: React.FormEvent) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    if (input.trim()) {
      sendMessage({ text: input });
      setInput('');
    }
  };

  return (
    <div className="flex flex-col h-screen max-w-2xl mx-auto p-4">
      <div className="flex-1 overflow-y-auto space-y-4 mb-4">
        {messages.map(message => (
          <div
            key={message.id}
            className={`p-3 rounded-lg ${ message.role === 'user' ? 'bg-blue-50 ml-auto' : 'bg-gray-50'}`}
          >
            <p className="font-semibold">
              {message.role === 'user' ? 'You' : 'Claude 4'}
            </p>
            {message.parts.map((part, index) => {
              if (part.type === 'text') {
                return (
                  <div key={index} className="mt-1">
                    {part.text}
                  </div>
                );
              }
              if (part.type === 'reasoning') {
                return (
                  <pre
                    key={index}
                    className="bg-gray-100 p-2 rounded mt-2 text-xs overflow-x-auto"
                  >
                    <details>
                      <summary className="cursor-pointer">
                        View reasoning
                      </summary>
                      {part.text}
                    </details>
                  </pre>
                );
              }
            })}
          </div>
        ))}
      </div>
      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit} className="flex gap-2">
        <input
          name="prompt"
          value={input}
          onChange={e => setInput(e.target.value)}
          className="flex-1 p-2 border rounded focus:outline-none focus:ring-2 focus:ring-blue-500"
          placeholder="Ask Claude 4 something..."
        />
        <button
          type="submit"
          className="bg-blue-500 text-white px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-blue-600"
        >
          Send
        </button>
      </form>
    </div>
  );
}
```

### Example Prompt with Temperature

```jsx
<InlinePrompt
  initialInput={`Create three slogans for a business with unique features.

Business: Bookstore with cats
Slogans: \"Purr-fect Pages\", \"Books and Whiskers\", \"Novels and Nuzzles\"
Business: Gym with rock climbing
Slogans: \"Peak Performance\", \"Reach New Heights\", \"Climb Your Way Fit\"
Business: Coffee shop with live music
Slogans:`}
showTemp={true}
initialTemperature={1}
/>
```

### Frontend Chat Interface with useChat Hook

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/21-llama-3_1.mdx

Implements a client-side chat interface using the `useChat` hook from AI SDK UI. This hook manages the chat state, including messages, user input, and submission handling. It makes requests to the backend API endpoint and displays the streamed AI responses in real-time.

```tsx
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';

export default function Page() {
  const { messages, input, handleInputChange, handleSubmit } = useChat();

  return (
    <>
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id}>
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.content}
        </div>
      ))}
      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit}>
        <input name="prompt" value={input} onChange={handleInputChange} />
        <button type="submit">Submit</button>
      </form>
    </>
  );
}
```

### Update Meal Log Interaction Example

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/06-advanced/09-multistep-interfaces.mdx

Illustrates a multistep interface scenario where a user first logs a meal and then requests an update. This example highlights the importance of application context, showing how the model uses previous actions to correctly identify and delete a meal based on user input.

```txt
User: Log a chicken shawarma for lunch.
Tool: log_meal("chicken shawarma", "250g", "12:00 PM")
Model: Chicken shawarma has been logged for lunch.
...
...
User: I skipped lunch today, can you update my log?
Tool: delete_meal("chicken shawarma")
Model: Chicken shawarma has been deleted from your log.
```

### Example Usage of createUIMessageStream

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/02-ai-sdk-ui/40-create-ui-message-stream.mdx

An example demonstrating how to use createUIMessageStream to write message chunks, merge other streams, and handle errors and finish callbacks.

```tsx
const existingMessages: UIMessage[] = [
  /* ... */
];

const stream = createUIMessageStream({
  async execute({ writer }) {
    // Write a message chunk
    writer.write({
      type: 'text-delta',
      textDelta: 'Hello',
    });

    // Merge another stream from streamText
    const result = streamText({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      prompt: 'Write a haiku about AI',
    });

    writer.merge(result.toUIMessageStream());
  },
  onError: error => `Custom error: ${error.message}`,
  originalMessages: existingMessages,
  onFinish: ({ messages, isContinuation, responseMessage }) => {
    console.log('Stream finished with messages:', messages);
  },
});
```

--------------------------------

### Chat API Endpoint with AI SDK Core

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/21-llama-3_1.mdx

Sets up a Next.js API route to handle chat requests. It uses AI SDK Core's `streamText` and `convertToModelMessages` to process user messages and stream responses from a specified model, like Llama 3.1 via DeepInfra. The `maxDuration` setting allows for extended streaming.

```tsx
import { deepinfra } from '@ai-sdk/deepinfra';
import { convertToModelMessages, streamText } from 'ai';

// Allow streaming responses up to 30 seconds
export const maxDuration = 30;

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: deepinfra('meta-llama/Meta-Llama-3.1-70B-Instruct'),
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### SQL Prompt for Database Query Generation with Schema and Rules

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/04-natural-language-postgres.mdx

This prompt guides an AI model to generate SQL queries for a 'unicorns' table. It includes schema details, specific SQL syntax rules (like ILIKE, LOWER), data interpretation guidelines (e.g., '10b' to 10.0), and output formatting requirements for chart-friendly data.

```Text
You are a SQL (postgres) and data visualization expert. Your job is to help the user write a SQL query to retrieve the data they need. The table schema is as follows:

unicorns (
  id SERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  company VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
  valuation DECIMAL(10, 2) NOT NULL,
  date_joined DATE,
  country VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
  city VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
  industry VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
  select_investors TEXT NOT NULL
);

Only retrieval queries are allowed.

For things like industry, company names and other string fields, use the ILIKE operator and convert both the search term and the field to lowercase using LOWER() function. For example: LOWER(industry) ILIKE LOWER('%search_term%').

Note: select_investors is a comma-separated list of investors. Trim whitespace to ensure you're grouping properly. Note, some fields may be null or have only one value.
When answering questions about a specific field, ensure you are selecting the identifying column (ie. what is Vercel's valuation would select company and valuation').

The industries available are:
- healthcare & life sciences
- consumer & retail
- financial services
- enterprise tech
- insurance
- media & entertainment
- industrials
- health

If the user asks for a category that is not in the list, infer based on the list above.

Note: valuation is in billions of dollars so 10b would be 10.0.
Note: if the user asks for a rate, return it as a decimal. For example, 0.1 would be 10%.

If the user asks for 'over time' data, return by year.

When searching for UK or USA, write out United Kingdom or United States respectively.

EVERY QUERY SHOULD RETURN QUANTITATIVE DATA THAT CAN BE PLOTTED ON A CHART! There should always be at least two columns. If the user asks for a single column, return the column and the count of the column. If the user asks for a rate, return the rate as a decimal. For example, 0.1 would be 10%.
```

```txt
User: What's the status of my wife's upcoming flight?
```

### Next.js Client Component with useChat Hook

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/20-sonnet-3-7.mdx

A client-side Next.js component (`app/page.tsx`) that utilizes the `useChat` hook from `@ai-sdk/react` to manage chat messages and send user input to the API. It displays messages and provides a form for user interaction, handling both text and reasoning parts.

```tsx
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { DefaultChatTransport } from 'ai';
import { useState } from 'react';

export default function Page() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat({
    transport: new DefaultChatTransport({ api: '/api/chat' }),
  });

  const handleSubmit = (e: React.FormEvent) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    if (input.trim()) {
      sendMessage({ text: input });
      setInput('');
    }
  };

  return (
    <>
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id}>
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.parts.map((part, index) => {
            // text parts:
            if (part.type === 'text') {
              return <div key={index}>{part.text}</div>;
            }
            // reasoning parts:
            if (part.type === 'reasoning') {
              return <pre key={index}>{part.text}</pre>;
            }
          })}
        </div>
      ))}
      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit}>
        <input
          name="prompt"
          value={input}
          onChange={e => setInput(e.target.value)}
        />
        <button type="submit">Send</button>
      </form>
    </>
  );
}
```

### Create Chat Endpoint Route Handler (Next.js/TypeScript)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/18-claude-4.mdx

A Next.js route handler for processing chat messages. It uses the AI SDK to stream text responses from the Anthropic Claude Sonnet 4 model, converting UI messages and handling provider-specific options like interleaved thinking.

```tsx
import { anthropic, AnthropicProviderOptions } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { streamText, convertToModelMessages, type UIMessage } from 'ai';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: anthropic('claude-sonnet-4-20250514'),
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
    headers: {
      'anthropic-beta': 'interleaved-thinking-2025-05-14',
    },
    providerOptions: {
      anthropic: {
        thinking: { type: 'enabled', budgetTokens: 15000 },
      } satisfies AnthropicProviderOptions,
    },
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse({
    sendReasoning: true,
  });
}
```

```ts
import { experimental_transcribe as transcribe } from 'ai';
import { gladia } from '@ai-sdk/gladia';
import { readFile } from 'fs/promises';

const result = await transcribe({
  model: gladia.transcription(),
  audio: await readFile('audio.mp3'),
  providerOptions: { gladia: { summarize: true } },
});
```

### streamToResponse Example Usage

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/04-stream-helpers/05-stream-to-response.mdx

Example demonstrating how to use streamToResponse to pipe a stream text result to a Node.js HTTP server response, including custom data streaming.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { StreamData, streamText, streamToResponse } from 'ai';
import { createServer } from 'http';

createServer(async (req, res) => {
  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-4.1'),
    prompt: 'What is the weather in San Francisco?',
  });

  // use stream data
  const data = new StreamData();

  data.append('initialized call');

  streamToResponse(
    result.toAIStream({
      onFinal() {
        data.append('call completed');
        data.close();
      },
    }),
    res,
    {},
    data,
  );
}).listen(8080);
```

### Next.js API Route for Chat with Anthropic

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/20-sonnet-3-7.mdx

A Next.js API route handler (`app/api/chat/route.ts`) that streams text responses from Anthropic's Claude 3.7 Sonnet model. It processes incoming chat messages, configures Anthropic provider options, and returns a UI message stream response, optionally including reasoning tokens.

```tsx
import { anthropic, AnthropicProviderOptions } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { streamText, convertToModelMessages, type UIMessage } from 'ai';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: anthropic('claude-3-7-sonnet-20250219'),
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
    providerOptions: {
      anthropic: {
        thinking: { type: 'enabled', budgetTokens: 12000 },
      } satisfies AnthropicProviderOptions,
    },
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse({
    sendReasoning: true,
  });
}
```

### experimental_createMCPClient API

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/01-ai-sdk-core/23-create-mcp-client.mdx

API documentation for the experimental_createMCPClient function, detailing its parameters and configuration options for connecting to MCP servers.

```APIDOC
experimental_createMCPClient(config: MCPClientConfig)
  Creates a lightweight Model Context Protocol (MCP) client that connects to an MCP server.
  This client is primarily used for tool conversion between MCP tools and AI SDK tools.

  Limitations:
  - Does not support accepting notifications from an MCP server.
  - Does not support custom configuration of the client.
  - This feature is experimental and may change or be removed in the future.

  Parameters:
    config: MCPClientConfig
      Configuration for the MCP client.
      Properties:
        transport: TransportConfig = MCPTransport | McpSSEServerConfig
          Configuration for the message transport layer.
          Can be either MCPTransport or McpSSEServerConfig.

          MCPTransport:
            A client transport instance, used explicitly for stdio or custom transports.
            Properties:
              start: () => Promise<void>
                A method that starts the transport.
              send: (message: JSONRPCMessage) => Promise<void>
                A method that sends a message through the transport.
              close: () => Promise<void>
                A method that closes the transport.
              onclose: () => void
                A method that is called when the transport is closed.
              onerror: (error: Error) => void
                A method that is called when the transport encounters an error.
              onmessage: (message: JSONRPCMessage) => void
                A method that is called when the transport receives a message.

          McpSSEServerConfig:
            Configuration for Server-Sent Events transport.
            Properties:
              type: 'sse'
                Use Server-Sent Events for communication.
              url: string
                URL of the MCP server.
              headers?: Record<string, string>
                Additional HTTP headers to be sent with requests.

        name?: string
          Client name. Defaults to "ai-sdk-mcp-client".

        onUncaughtError?: (error: unknown) => void
          Handler for uncaught errors.
```

### Create Dynamic Tool

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/01-ai-sdk-core/22-dynamic-tool.mdx

Example of creating a dynamic tool with an unknown input schema and execute function.

```ts
import { dynamicTool } from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

export const customTool = dynamicTool({
  description: 'Execute a custom user-defined function',
  inputSchema: z.object({}),
  // input is typed as 'unknown'
  execute: async input => {
    const { action, parameters } = input as any;

    // Execute your dynamic logic
    return {
      result: `Executed ${action} with ${JSON.stringify(parameters)}`,
    };
  },
});
```

### smoothStream() Chinese Chunking Example

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/01-ai-sdk-core/80-smooth-stream.mdx

Provides an example of using smoothStream with a custom regex for Chinese text chunking, accounting for the absence of space delimiters.

```tsx
import { smoothStream, streamText } from 'ai';

const result = streamText({
  model: 'openai/gpt-4.1',
  prompt: 'Your prompt here',
  experimental_transform: smoothStream({
    chunking: /[一-鿿]|S+s+/,
  }),
});
```

### Transcribe Audio with AssemblyAI Options

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/100-assemblyai.mdx

Shows how to transcribe audio using the 'ai' SDK, passing AssemblyAI-specific options via `providerOptions`. This example enables content safety filtering. It requires importing `experimental_transcribe` from 'ai' and `assemblyai` from '@ai-sdk/assemblyai'.

```ts
import { experimental_transcribe as transcribe } from 'ai';
import { assemblyai } from '@ai-sdk/assemblyai';
import { readFile } from 'fs/promises';

const result = await transcribe({
  model: assemblyai.transcription('best'),
  audio: await readFile('audio.mp3'),
  providerOptions: { assemblyai: { contentSafety: true } },
});
```

### Initialize AI SDK with Server Actions (TypeScript)

This file initializes the AI SDK using 'createAI' from '@ai-sdk/rsc'. It configures the AI with available server actions, including 'continueConversation', and sets up initial empty states for AI and UI. This setup is crucial for integrating the AI functionality into the application.

```typescript
import { createAI } from '@ai-sdk/rsc';
import { ServerMessage, ClientMessage, continueConversation } from './actions';

export const AI = createAI<ServerMessage[], ClientMessage[]>({
  actions: {
    continueConversation,
  },
  initialAIState: [],
  initialUIState: [],
});
```

```APIDOC
Adding New Codemods:
  1. Create the codemod in `src/codemods/`
  2. Add test fixtures in `src/test/__testfixtures__/`
  3. Create tests in `src/test/`
  4. Update the bundle in `src/lib/upgrade.ts`
```

### Multi-modal Tool Results with AI SDK

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-foundations/03-prompts.mdx

Demonstrates sending multi-part and multi-modal tool results to an AI model. It includes examples for models supporting multi-part content and those requiring a single output part. This requires the `generateText` function and potentially file system access for media.

```ts
const result = await generateText({
  model: 'openai/gpt-4.1',
  messages: [
    // ...
    {
      role: 'tool',
      content: [
        {
          type: 'tool-result',
          toolCallId: '12345', // needs to match the tool call id
          toolName: 'get-nutrition-data',
          // for models that do not support multi-part tool results,
          // you can include a regular output part:
          output: {
            type: 'json',
            value: {
              name: 'Cheese, roquefort',
              calories: 369,
              fat: 31,
              protein: 22,
            },
          },
        },
        {
          type: 'tool-result',
          toolCallId: '12345', // needs to match the tool call id
          toolName: 'get-nutrition-data',
          // for models that support multi-part tool results,
          // you can include a multi-part content part:
          output: {
            type: 'content',
            value: [
              {
                type: 'text',
                text: 'Here is an image of the nutrition data for the cheese:',
              },
              {
                type: 'media',
                data: fs
                  .readFileSync('./data/roquefort-nutrition-data.png')
                  .toString('base64'),
                mediaType: 'image/png',
              },
            ],
          },
        },
      ],
    },
  ],
});
```

### Create SQL Query Explanation Server Action

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/04-natural-language-postgres.mdx

This TypeScript server action, `explainQuery`, takes a user's natural language input and a generated SQL query. It leverages an AI model to break down the SQL query into sections and provide plain English explanations for each, returning an array of explanation objects. It utilizes the `generateObject` function with a defined schema and specifies the output format as an array.

```ts
// other imports
import { explanationSchema } from '@/lib/types';

/* ...rest of the file... */

export const explainQuery = async (input: string, sqlQuery: string) => {
  'use server';
  try {
    const result = await generateObject({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      system: `You are a SQL (postgres) expert. ...`, // SYSTEM PROMPT AS ABOVE - OMITTED FOR BREVITY
      prompt: `Explain the SQL query you generated to retrieve the data the user wanted. Assume the user is not an expert in SQL. Break down the query into steps. Be concise.

      User Query:
      ${input}

      Generated SQL Query:
      ${sqlQuery}`,
      schema: explanationSchema,
      output: 'array',
    });
    return result.object;
  } catch (e) {
    console.error(e);
    throw new Error('Failed to generate query');
  }
};
```

--------------------------------

### Codemod Generation Instructions

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/contributing/codemods.md

A list of instructions to guide an AI model in creating effective codemods. These cover file naming conventions, import strategies, return values, and testing procedures.

```markdown
- Start all input/output fixtures files with `// @ts-nocheck`. Make sure the comment remains in place in the output fixture file.
- Update `packages/codemod/src/lib/upgrade.ts`
- Use `import { createTransformer } from './lib/create-transformer';` for codemods. Do not import anything from `jscodeshift` directly.
- No need to cover imports that use `require()`
- The codemod should not return anything. It should set `context.hasChanges` to `true` instead.
- See files in `packages/codemod/src/codemods` for conventions
- Multiple input/output files can be used in case of import conflicts.
- Run tests to verify the change
- Run the codemod manually to verify that it's working
- If you need to create temporary files for testing, create them in `packages/codemod/`, and remove them when done.
```

### Update query-viewer.tsx with explainQuery Action

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/04-natural-language-postgres.mdx

This snippet demonstrates updating the `handleExplainQuery` function in `components/query-viewer.tsx` to call the `explainQuery` Server Action. It handles setting loading states and updating the component's state with the generated explanations.

```typescript
/* ...other imports... */
import { explainQuery } from '@/app/actions';

/* ...rest of the component... */

const handleExplainQuery = async () => {
  setQueryExpanded(true);
  setLoadingExplanation(true);

  const explanations = await explainQuery(inputValue, activeQuery);
  setQueryExplanations(explanations);

  setLoadingExplanation(false);
};

/* ...rest of the component... */
```

```ts
const qwen = createQwen({
  // optional settings, e.g.

  // headers: { 'X-Custom-Header': 'value' },
```

### Generate Image with Luma Photon

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/packages/luma/README.md

Example of generating an image using the Luma provider with the 'photon-1' model. It demonstrates how to call the `generateImage` function and save the resulting image to a file.

```ts
import { luma } from '@ai-sdk/luma';
import { experimental_generateImage as generateImage } from 'ai';
import fs from 'fs';

const { image } = await generateImage({
  model: luma.image('photon-1'),
  prompt: 'A serene mountain landscape at sunset',
});

const filename = `image-${Date.now()}.png`;
fs.writeFileSync(filename, image.uint8Array);
console.log(`Image saved to ${filename}`);
```

### Generate Text with Gemini CLI Provider (AI SDK v4 & v5-beta)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/03-community-providers/100-gemini-cli.mdx

Provides examples for generating text using the Gemini CLI provider with the `generateText` function from the AI SDK. It highlights the difference in accessing the generated text between AI SDK v4 and v5-beta.

```typescript
import { createGeminiProvider } from 'ai-sdk-provider-gemini-cli';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const gemini = createGeminiProvider({
  authType: 'oauth-personal',
});

// AI SDK v4
const { text } = await generateText({
  model: gemini('gemini-2.5-pro'),
  prompt: 'Write a vegetarian lasagna recipe for 4 people.',
});

// AI SDK v5-beta
const result = await generateText({
  model: gemini('gemini-2.5-pro'),
  prompt: 'Write a vegetarian lasagna recipe for 4 people.',
});
console.log(result.content[0].text);
```

### Use OpenAI Web Search Preview Tool

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/03-openai.mdx

Demonstrates how to use the `webSearchPreview` tool with the OpenAI SDK for web search functionality. It shows how to configure search context and user location, and how to force the tool's usage via `toolChoice`.

```ts
const result = await generateText({
  model: openai.responses('gpt-4o-mini'),
  prompt: 'What happened in San Francisco last week?',
  tools: {
    web_search_preview: openai.tools.webSearchPreview({
      // optional configuration:
      searchContextSize: 'high',
      userLocation: {
        type: 'approximate',
        city: 'San Francisco',
        region: 'California',
      },
    }),
  },
  // Force web search tool:
  toolChoice: { type: 'tool', toolName: 'web_search_preview' },
});

// URL sources
const sources = result.sources;
```

### Tool Usage for Text Generation

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/00-ai-gateway.mdx

Demonstrates how to enable tool usage within text generation. It defines a `getWeather` tool using Zod for schema validation and provides an example of its execution.

```ts
import { gateway } from '@ai-sdk/gateway';
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: gateway('meta/llama-3.3-70b'),
  prompt: 'What is the weather like in San Francisco?',
  tools: {
    getWeather: tool({
      description: 'Get the current weather for a location',
      parameters: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The location to get weather for'),
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => {
        // Your weather API call here
        return `It's sunny in ${location}`;
      },
    }),
  },
});
```

### Define and Call Tools

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/05-node/50-call-tools.mdx

Demonstrates how to define tools with descriptions and input schemas using the AI SDK and integrate them into a text generation request. It shows the basic setup for enabling tool use in language models.

```typescript
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const result = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-4.1'),
  tools: {
    weather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => ({
        location,
        temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10,
      }),
    }),
    cityAttractions: tool({
      inputSchema: z.object({ city: z.string() }),
    }),
  },
  prompt:
    'What is the weather in San Francisco and what attractions should I visit?',
});
```

--------------------------------

### Stream UI Message Response with Hono

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/15-api-servers/30-hono.mdx

Demonstrates creating a properly formatted streaming response for UI messages using the AI SDK and Hono. This method is suitable for chat-like interfaces where structured messages are expected.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { serve } from '@hono/node-server';
import { streamText } from 'ai';
import { Hono } from 'hono';

const app = new Hono();

app.post('/', async c => {
  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    prompt: 'Invent a new holiday and describe its traditions.',
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
});

serve({ fetch: app.fetch, port: 8080 });

```

--------------------------------

### Handle Assistant Thread Messages

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/03-slackbot.mdx

Handles `assistant_thread_started` events in Slack. It posts a welcome message to the new thread and sets up suggested prompts for users to interact with the AI assistant. It uses the Slack client for posting messages and setting prompts.

```typescript
import type { AssistantThreadStartedEvent } from '@slack/web-api';
import { client } from './slack-utils';

export async function assistantThreadMessage(
  event: AssistantThreadStartedEvent,
) {
  const { channel_id, thread_ts } = event.assistant_thread;
  console.log(`Thread started: ${channel_id} ${thread_ts}`);
  console.log(JSON.stringify(event));

  await client.chat.postMessage({
    channel: channel_id,
    thread_ts: thread_ts,
    text: "Hello, I'm an AI assistant built with the AI SDK by Vercel!",
  });

  await client.assistant.threads.setSuggestedPrompts({
    channel_id: channel_id,
    thread_ts: thread_ts,
    prompts: [
      {
        title: 'Get the weather',
        message: 'What is the current weather in London?',
      },
      {
        title: 'Get the news',
        message: 'What is the latest Premier League news from the BBC?',
      },
    ],
  });
}
```

### Configure Specific Search Sources

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/01-xai.mdx

Customize Live Search by specifying an array of 'SearchSource' objects in 'searchParameters'. This example configures web search with specific allowed websites and country.

```typescript
import { xai } from '@ai-sdk/xai';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const result = await generateText({
  model: xai('grok-3-latest'),
  prompt: 'Best ski resorts in Switzerland',
  providerOptions: {
    xai: {
      searchParameters: {
        mode: 'on',
        sources: [
          {
            type: 'web',
            country: 'CH', // ISO alpha-2 country code
            allowedWebsites: ['ski.com', 'snow-forecast.com'],
            safeSearch: true,
          },
        ],
      },
    },
  },
});
```

```ts
  openai
} from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import {
  embedMany
} from 'ai';

const {
  embeddings
} = await embedMany({
  model: openai.textEmbeddingModel('text-embedding-3-small'),
  values: [
    'sunny day at the beach',
    'rainy afternoon in the city',
    'snowy night in the mountains',
  ],
});
```

--------------------------------

### Prepare Step: Experimental to Stable

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/08-migration-guides/26-migration-guide-5-0.mdx

Highlights the promotion of the `prepareStep` option from experimental to stable, removing the `experimental_` prefix. This function allows dynamic configuration of generation steps, including model, active tools, and system messages.

```tsx
const result = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-4'),
  messages,
  tools: { weatherTool, locationTool },
  experimental_prepareStep: ({ steps, stepNumber, model }) => {
    console.log('Preparing step:', stepNumber);
    return {
      activeTools: ['weatherTool'],
      system: 'Be helpful and concise.',
    };
  },
});
```

```tsx
const result = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-4'),
  messages,
  tools: { weatherTool, locationTool },
  prepareStep: ({ steps, stepNumber, model }) => {
    console.log('Preparing step:', stepNumber);
    return {
      activeTools: ['weatherTool'],
      system: 'Be helpful and concise.',
      // Can also configure toolChoice, model, etc.
    };
  },
});
```

### OpenAI Compatible API Setup (Dedicated)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/03-community-providers/08-friendliai.mdx

Configures the `@ai-sdk/openai` package to interact with FriendliAI's dedicated endpoints. This setup is used when you have deployed custom models and need to access them via an OpenAI-compatible interface. Ensure the `baseURL` points to the dedicated endpoint path.

```ts
import { createOpenAI } from '@ai-sdk/openai';

const friendli = createOpenAI({
  baseURL: 'https://api.friendli.ai/dedicated/v1',
  apiKey: process.env.FRIENDLI_TOKEN,
});
```

### Implement Enhanced Tool Streaming Callbacks

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/01-announcing-ai-sdk-5-beta/index.mdx

Demonstrates how to use fine-grained streaming callbacks for tools, including `onInputStart`, `onInputDelta`, and `onInputAvailable`. These allow for real-time feedback during tool input processing.

```tsx
const weatherTool = tool({
  inputSchema: z.object({ city: z.string() }),
  onInputStart: ({ toolCallId }) => {
    console.log('Tool input streaming started:', toolCallId);
  },
  onInputDelta: ({ inputTextDelta, toolCallId }) => {
    console.log('Tool input delta:', inputTextDelta);
  },
  onInputAvailable: ({ input, toolCallId }) => {
    console.log('Tool input ready:', input);
  },
  execute: async ({ city }) => {
    return `Weather in ${city}: sunny, 72°F`;
  }
});
```

### wrapLanguageModel Usage Example

Demonstrates how to import and use the `wrapLanguageModel` function to wrap a language model with middleware. It shows the basic structure for applying custom middleware to a model.

```ts
import { wrapLanguageModel } from 'ai';

const wrappedLanguageModel = wrapLanguageModel({
  model: 'openai/gpt-4.1',
  middleware: yourLanguageModelMiddleware,
});
```

--------------------------------

### Agentic Control: stopWhen Examples

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/01-announcing-ai-sdk-5-beta/index.mdx

Provides examples of using the `stopWhen` parameter in `generateText` to define custom stopping conditions for an agent. This includes stopping after a certain number of steps, when a specific tool is called, or based on other custom criteria.

```typescript
import { generateText, stepCountIs, hasToolCall, maxTotalTokens } from 'ai';

// stop loop at 5 steps
const result1 = generateText({
  // ...
  stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
});

// stop loop when weather tool called
const result2 = generateText({
  // ...
  stopWhen: hasToolCall('weather'),
});

// stop loop at your own custom condition (e.g., max tokens)
const result3 = generateText({
  // ...
  stopWhen: maxTotalTokens(20000),
});
```

--------------------------------

### AI SDK Setup with RSC

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/20-rsc/60-save-messages-to-database.mdx

Initializes the AI instance using createAI from the AI SDK. It configures available actions, defines handlers for state updates (onSetAIState) and retrieval (onGetUIState), and integrates server-side logic for saving chat history and rendering UI components.

```ts
import { createAI } from '@ai-sdk/rsc';
import { ServerMessage, ClientMessage, continueConversation } from './actions';

export const AI = createAI<ServerMessage[], ClientMessage[]>({
  actions: {
    continueConversation,
  },
  onSetAIState: async ({ state, done }) => {
    'use server';

    if (done) {
      saveChat(state);
    }
  },
  onGetUIState: async () => {
    'use server';

    const history: ServerMessage[] = getAIState();

    return history.map(({ role, content }) => ({
      id: generateId(),
      role,
      display:
        role === 'function' ? <Stock {...JSON.parse(content)} /> : content,
    }));
  },
});

```

### React useObject Hook Example

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/02-ai-sdk-ui/03-use-object.mdx

Demonstrates the usage of the `experimental_useObject` hook in a React client component. It shows how to initialize the hook with an API endpoint and schema, submit input to trigger the stream, and display the parsed object content.

```tsx
'use client';

import { experimental_useObject as useObject } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { z } from 'zod';

export default function Page() {
  const { object, submit } = useObject({
    api: '/api/use-object',
    schema: z.object({ content: z.string() }),
  });

  return (
    <div>
      <button onClick={() => submit('example input')}>Generate</button>
      {object?.content && <p>{object.content}</p>}
    </div>
  );
}
```

### Setup Patronus OTEL Exporter with @vercel/otel

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/05-observability/patronus.mdx

Configures the OpenTelemetry SDK in a Node.js application using `@vercel/otel`. It sets up an OTLP trace exporter pointing to the Patronus endpoint and includes the API key in the headers for authentication. This enables automatic conversion of LLM spans into prompt/response records within Patronus.

```typescript
import { registerOTel } from '@vercel/otel';
import { OTLPTraceExporter } from '@opentelemetry/exporter-trace-otlp-http';
import { BatchSpanProcessor } from '@opentelemetry/sdk-trace-node';

export function register() {
  registerOTel({
    serviceName: 'next-app',
    additionalSpanProcessors: [
      new BatchSpanProcessor(
        new OTLPTraceExporter({
          url: process.env.OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT,
          headers: {
            'x-api-key': process.env.PATRONUS_API_KEY!,
          },
        }),
      ),
    ],
  });
}
```

### Intercepting Fetch Requests Example

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/03-community-providers/96-sambanova.mdx

Shows how to intercept fetch requests made by the SambaNova provider by providing a custom `fetch` implementation during instance creation. This allows logging or modifying requests/responses.

```typescript
import { createSambaNova } from 'sambanova-ai-provider';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const sambanovaProvider = createSambaNova({
  apiKey: 'YOUR_API_KEY',
  fetch: async (url, options) => {
    console.log('URL', url);
    console.log('Headers', JSON.stringify(options.headers, null, 2));
    console.log(`Body ${JSON.stringify(JSON.parse(options.body), null, 2)}`);
    return await fetch(url, options);
  },
});

const model = sambanovaProvider('Meta-Llama-3.1-70B-Instruct');

const { text } = await generateText({
  model,
  prompt: 'Hello, nice to meet you.',
});
```

### Use Groq Model with Reasoning Format

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/09-groq.mdx

Generate text using a Groq model, configuring provider-specific options like `reasoningFormat`, `parallelToolCalls`, and `user` identifier. This example demonstrates using a reasoning model.

```ts
import { groq } from '@ai-sdk/groq';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const result = await generateText({
  model: groq('qwen1.5-72b-chat'),
  providerOptions: {
    groq: {
      reasoningFormat: 'parsed',
      parallelToolCalls: true, // Enable parallel function calling (default: true)
      user: 'user-123', // Unique identifier for end-user (optional)
    }
  },
  prompt: 'How many "r"s are in the word "strawberry"?',
});
```

### Response with Citations

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/01-xai.mdx

Shows how to retrieve citations along with the generated text when search is enabled and `returnCitations` is set to true. The example demonstrates accessing the `sources` array from the response.

```typescript
const { text, sources } = await generateText({
  model: xai('grok-3-latest'),
  prompt: 'What are the latest developments in AI?',
  providerOptions: {
    xai: {
      searchParameters: {
        mode: 'auto',
        returnCitations: true,
      },
    },
  },
});

// Access the sources used
for (const source of sources) {
  if (source.sourceType === 'url') {
    console.log('Source:', source.url);
  }
}
```

### Configure Multi-Step Tool Calls with stopWhen in TypeScript

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/06-nodejs.mdx

This snippet demonstrates how to enable multi-step tool calls by configuring the `stopWhen` option with `stepCountIs(5)`. It also includes an `onStepFinish` callback to log tool results, allowing the model to use this information for subsequent generations until the stopping condition is met.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { ModelMessage, streamText, tool, stepCountIs } from 'ai';
import 'dotenv/config';
import { z } from 'zod';
import * as readline from 'node:readline/promises';

const terminal = readline.createInterface({
  input: process.stdin,
  output: process.stdout,
});

const messages: ModelMessage[] = [];

async function main() {
  while (true) {
    const userInput = await terminal.question('You: ');

    messages.push({ role: 'user', content: userInput });

    const result = streamText({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      messages,
      tools: {
        weather: tool({
          description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
          inputSchema: z.object({
            location: z
              .string()
              .describe('The location to get the weather for'),
          }),
          execute: async ({ location }) => {
            const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
            return {
              location,
              temperature,
            };
          },
        }),
      },
      stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
      onStepFinish: async ({ toolResults }) => {
        if (toolResults.length) {
          console.log(JSON.stringify(toolResults, null, 2));
        }
      },
    });

    let fullResponse = '';
    process.stdout.write('\nAssistant: ');
    for await (const delta of result.textStream) {
      fullResponse += delta;
      process.stdout.write(delta);
    }
    process.stdout.write('\n\n');

    messages.push({ role: 'assistant', content: fullResponse });
  }
}

main().catch(console.error);

```

### Assistant Message: File Content with AI SDK

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-foundations/03-prompts.mdx

Provides an example of an assistant message containing file content, such as a generated image. This feature is supported by specific models and allows the AI to output files directly.

```ts
const result = await generateText({
  model: 'openai/gpt-4.1',
  messages: [
    { role: 'user', content: 'Generate an image of a roquefort cheese!' },
    {
      role: 'assistant',
      content: [
        {
          type: 'file',
          mediaType: 'image/png',
          data: fs.readFileSync('./data/roquefort.jpg'),
        },
      ],
    },
  ],
});
```

### Basic Usage Example

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/02-ai-sdk-ui/47-infer-ui-tool.mdx

Demonstrates how to use InferUITool to infer the input and output types of a Zod-defined weather tool. The inferred types are then assigned to a TypeScript type alias.

```typescript
import { InferUITool } from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const weatherTool = {
  description: 'Get the current weather',
  parameters: z.object({
    location: z.string().describe('The city and state'),
  }),
  execute: async ({ location }) => {
    return `The weather in ${location} is sunny.`;
  },
};

// Infer the types from the tool
type WeatherUITool = InferUITool<typeof weatherTool>;
// This creates a type with:
// {
//   input: { location: string };
//   output: string;
// }
```

Command to start the local development server for the AI agent application using the pnpm package manager. This command is essential for running the application locally and testing the implemented file upload functionality.

### Implement Sequential Generations in TypeScript

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/06-advanced/09-sequential-generations.mdx

Demonstrates creating a sequence of AI generations using the AI SDK. The example shows how to generate blog post ideas, select the best idea, and then create an outline based on the chosen idea. Each step's output is fed as input to the subsequent generation, illustrating a common AI workflow pattern.

```typescript
import {
  openai
} from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import {
  generateText
} from 'ai';

async function sequentialActions() {
  // Generate blog post ideas
  const ideasGeneration = await generateText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    prompt: 'Generate 10 ideas for a blog post about making spaghetti.',
  });

  console.log('Generated Ideas:\n', ideasGeneration);

  // Pick the best idea
  const bestIdeaGeneration = await generateText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    prompt: `Here are some blog post ideas about making spaghetti:
${ideasGeneration}

Pick the best idea from the list above and explain why it's the best.`, 
  });

  console.log('\nBest Idea:\n', bestIdeaGeneration);

  // Generate an outline
  const outlineGeneration = await generateText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    prompt: `We've chosen the following blog post idea about making spaghetti:
${bestIdeaGeneration}

Create a detailed outline for a blog post based on this idea.`, 
  });

  console.log('\nBlog Post Outline:\n', outlineGeneration);
}

sequentialActions().catch(console.error);
```

### Route Handler with AI SDK Core and OpenAI Provider

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/08-migration-guides/39-migration-guide-3-1.mdx

Example of a Next.js Route Handler refactored to use AI SDK Core and the '@ai-sdk/openai' provider. It demonstrates a unified API for querying LLMs and returning a UI-compatible stream response.

```tsx
import { streamText } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages } = await req.json();

  const result = await streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-4.1'),
    messages,
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### Customize Headers for Provider Authentication

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/packages/openai-compatible/README.md

```typescript
import { createOpenAICompatible } from '@ai-sdk/openai-compatible';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: createOpenAICompatible({
    baseURL: 'https://api.example.com/v1',
```

### Example Usage of createUIMessageStreamResponse

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/02-ai-sdk-ui/41-create-ui-message-stream-response.mdx

Demonstrates how to use createUIMessageStreamResponse to create a streaming UI response, including writing custom data, text, source information, and merging with LLM streams.

```tsx
import { createUIMessageStream, createUIMessageStreamResponse } from 'ai';

const response = createUIMessageStreamResponse({
  status: 200,
  statusText: 'OK',
  headers: {
    'Custom-Header': 'value',
  },
  stream: createUIMessageStream({
    execute({ writer }) {
      // Write custom data
      writer.write({
        type: 'data',
        value: { message: 'Hello' },
      });

      // Write text content
      writer.write({
        type: 'text',
        value: 'Hello, world!',
      });

      // Write source information
      writer.write({
        type: 'source-url',
        value: {
          type: 'source',
          id: 'source-1',
          url: 'https://example.com',
          title: 'Example Source',
        },
      });

      // Merge with LLM stream
      const result = streamText({
        model: openai('gpt-4'),
        prompt: 'Say hello',
      });

      writer.merge(result.toUIMessageStream());
    },
  }),
});
```

### Transcribe Audio with Fal AI (TypeScript)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/10-fal.mdx

Shows a complete example of transcribing an audio file using the Fal AI SDK. It requires the 'ai' and '@ai-sdk/fal' packages, and 'fs/promises' for file reading. The input is an audio file path and model configuration, and the output is the transcription result. It supports passing provider-specific options to customize the transcription process.

```typescript
import { experimental_transcribe as transcribe } from 'ai';
import { fal } from '@ai-sdk/fal';
import { readFile } from 'fs/promises';

const result = await transcribe({
  model: fal.transcription('wizper'),
  audio: await readFile('audio.mp3'),
  providerOptions: { fal: { batchSize: 10 } },
});
```

```typescript
await addMemories(messages, {
```

### Define Chart Configuration Schema (TypeScript)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/04-natural-language-postgres.mdx

Defines the TypeScript schema for chart configurations using Zod. This schema includes properties for chart type, axis mappings, styling, and descriptive fields to guide AI model generation.

```typescript
/* ...rest of the file... */

export const configSchema = z
  .object({
    description: z
      .string()
      .describe(
        'Describe the chart. What is it showing? What is interesting about the way the data is displayed?',
      ),
    takeaway: z.string().describe('What is the main takeaway from the chart?'),
    type: z.enum(['bar', 'line', 'area', 'pie']).describe('Type of chart'),
    title: z.string(),
    xKey: z.string().describe('Key for x-axis or category'),
    yKeys: z
      .array(z.string())
      .describe(
        'Key(s) for y-axis values this is typically the quantitative column',
      ),
    multipleLines: z
      .boolean()
      .describe(
        'For line charts only: whether the chart is comparing groups of data.',
      )
      .optional(),
    measurementColumn: z
      .string()
      .describe(
        'For line charts only: key for quantitative y-axis column to measure against (eg. values, counts etc.)',
      )
      .optional(),
    lineCategories: z
      .array(z.string())
      .describe(
        'For line charts only: Categories used to compare different lines or data series. Each category represents a distinct line in the chart.',
      )
      .optional(),
    colors: z
      .record(
        z.string().describe('Any of the yKeys'),
        z.string().describe('Color value in CSS format (e.g., hex, rgb, hsl)'),
      )
      .describe('Mapping of data keys to color values for chart elements')
      .optional(),
    legend: z.boolean().describe('Whether to show legend'),
  })
  .describe('Chart configuration object');

export type Config = z.infer<typeof configSchema>;
```

--------------------------------

### Create Resource Server Action (Initial)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/01-rag-chatbot.mdx

This Server Action in Next.js is responsible for creating a new resource in the database. It parses input using a Zod schema and returns a success message or an error.

```tsx
'use server';

import {
  NewResourceParams,
  insertResourceSchema,
  resources,
} from '@/lib/db/schema/resources';
import { db } from '../db';

export const createResource = async (input: NewResourceParams) => {
  try {
    const { content } = insertResourceSchema.parse(input);

    const [resource] = await db
      .insert(resources)
      .values({ content })
      .returning();

    return 'Resource successfully created.';
  } catch (e) {
    if (e instanceof Error)
      return e.message.length > 0 ? e.message : 'Error, please try again.';
  }
};
```

### Flight Booking Workflow

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/06-advanced/09-multistep-interfaces.mdx

Demonstrates a typical flight booking process using tool composition. It shows the sequence of user interactions and corresponding tool calls (searchFlights, lookupFlight, bookFlight) to find, verify, and book a flight, including handling passenger details.

```txt
User: I want to book a flight from New York to London.
Tool: searchFlights("New York", "London")
Model: Here are the available flights from New York to London.
User: I want to book flight number BA123 on 12th December for myself and my wife.
Tool: lookupFlight("BA123") -> "4 seats available"
Model: Sure, there are seats available! Can you provide the names of the passengers?
User: John Doe and Jane Doe.
Tool: bookFlight("BA123", "12th December", ["John Doe", "Jane Doe"])
Model: Your flight has been booked!
```

### Create AI Chat API Route (TypeScript)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/05-nuxt.mdx

Sets up a server-side API route using TypeScript to handle chat messages. It initializes an OpenAI provider and streams text responses from a specified model.

```typescript
import { streamText, UIMessage, convertToModelMessages } from 'ai';
import { createOpenAI } from '@ai-sdk/openai';

export default defineLazyEventHandler(async () => {
  const apiKey = useRuntimeConfig().openaiApiKey;
  if (!apiKey) throw new Error('Missing OpenAI API key');
  const openai = createOpenAI({
    apiKey: apiKey,
  });

  return defineEventHandler(async (event: any) => {
    const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await readBody(event);

    const result = streamText({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
    });

    return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
  });
});
```

```javascript
  model: openrouter.chat('meta-llama/llama-3.1-405b-instruct'),
```

### smoothStream() Regex Chunking Examples

Demonstrates how to configure smoothStream with regular expressions for custom text chunking, such as splitting on underscores.

```ts
// To split on underscores:
smoothStream({
  chunking: /_+/,
});

// Also can do it like this, same behavior
smoothStream({
  chunking: /[^_]*_/,
});
```

--------------------------------

### AI SDK Core Concepts: Tool and StopWhen

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/05-nuxt.mdx

This section outlines key functionalities within the AI SDK for managing tool usage and generation stopping conditions. `tool` is used to define custom tools with descriptions and input schemas, while `stopWhen` controls the generation process based on specific criteria like step count.

```APIDOC
streamText(options)
  - Streams text output from a language model.
  - Parameters:
    - model: The language model to use (e.g., openai('gpt-4o')).
    - messages: An array of messages representing the conversation history.
    - stopWhen: A condition to stop generation. Defaults to stepCountIs(1).
    - tools: An object defining available tools for the model.

tool(toolDefinition)
  - Defines a single tool for the AI model.
  - Parameters:
    - description: A natural language description of what the tool does.
    - inputSchema: A Zod schema defining the expected input parameters for the tool.
    - execute: An async function that performs the tool's action.

stepCountIs(count)
  - A stopping condition that halts generation after a specified number of steps.
  - Parameters:
    - count: The maximum number of generation steps allowed.
```

--------------------------------

### Generate Text with OpenAI Reasoning Models

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/03-openai.mdx

Demonstrates using `generateText` with OpenAI's reasoning models like `o3-mini`. It shows how to configure `reasoningEffort` via `providerOptions` and access `reasoningTokens` from `providerMetadata`. Requires `@ai-sdk/openai` and `ai` packages.

```ts
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text, usage, providerMetadata } = await generateText({
  model: openai('o3-mini'),
  prompt: 'Invent a new holiday and describe its traditions.',
  providerOptions: {
    openai: {
      reasoningEffort: 'low',
    },
  },
});

console.log(text);
console.log('Usage:', {
  ...usage,
  reasoningTokens: providerMetadata?.openai?.reasoningTokens,
});
```

### POST Route Handler with System Prompt

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/01-rag-chatbot.mdx

Enhances the Next.js API route handler by incorporating a system prompt. This prompt guides the AI model's behavior, instructing it to use only tool call information and to respond with a specific phrase if no relevant data is found.

```tsx
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { convertToModelMessages, streamText, UIMessage } from 'ai';

// Allow streaming responses up to 30 seconds
export const maxDuration = 30;

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    system: `You are a helpful assistant. Check your knowledge base before answering any questions.
    Only respond to questions using information from tool calls.
    if no relevant information is found in the tool calls, respond, "Sorry, I don't know."`,
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### Call Tools with Image Prompt using AI SDK and Node.js

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/05-node/52-call-tools-with-image-prompt.mdx

Demonstrates how to use the AI SDK with Node.js to call tools when provided with an image as part of the user prompt. This example utilizes multimodal input capabilities, specifically passing an image URL to the `generateText` function.

```typescript
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const result = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-4.1'),
  messages: [
    {
      role: 'user',
      content: [
        { type: 'text', text: 'can you log this meal for me?' },
        {
          type: 'image',
          image: new URL(
            'https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Cheeseburger_%2817237580619%29.jpg/640px-Cheeseburger_%2817237580619%29.jpg',
          ),
        },
      ],
    },
  ],
  tools: {
    logFood: tool({
      description: 'Log a food item',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        name: z.string(),
        calories: z.number(),
      }),
      execute({ name, calories }) {
        storeInDatabase({ name, calories }); // your implementation here
      },
    }),
  },
});

```

### Create Server Action for Chart Generation (JavaScript/TypeScript)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/04-natural-language-postgres.mdx

Implements a Next.js Server Action that takes query results and a user query to generate a chart configuration. It uses an AI model (GPT-4o) and the defined Zod schema, then applies theme colors.

```javascript
/* ...other imports... */
import { Config, configSchema, explanationsSchema, Result } from '@/lib/types';

/* ...rest of the file... */

export const generateChartConfig = async (
  results: Result[],
  userQuery: string,
) => {
  'use server';

  try {
    const { object: config } = await generateObject({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      system: 'You are a data visualization expert.',
      prompt: `Given the following data from a SQL query result, generate the chart config that best visualises the data and answers the users query.
      For multiple groups use multi-lines.

      Here is an example complete config:
      export const chartConfig = {
        type: "pie",
        xKey: "month",
        yKeys: ["sales", "profit", "expenses"],
        colors: {
          sales: "#4CAF50",    // Green for sales
          profit: "#2196F3",   // Blue for profit
          expenses: "#F44336"  // Red for expenses
        },
        legend: true
      }

      User Query:
      ${userQuery}

      Data:
      ${JSON.stringify(results, null, 2)}`,
      schema: configSchema,
    });

    // Override with shadcn theme colors
    const colors: Record<string, string> = {};
    config.yKeys.forEach((key, index) => {
      colors[key] = `hsl(var(--chart-${index + 1}))`;
    });

    const updatedConfig = { ...config, colors };
    return { config: updatedConfig };
  } catch (e) {
    console.error(e);
    throw new Error('Failed to generate chart suggestion');
  }
};
```

### TextStreamPart: Tool Call Streaming Start

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/01-ai-sdk-core/02-stream-text.mdx

Indicates the beginning of a streaming sequence for a tool call. This is relevant when tool call arguments are streamed incrementally.

```APIDOC
TextStreamPart:
  type: 'tool-call-streaming-start'
  toolCallId: string
    - The unique identifier for the tool call.
  toolName: string
    - The name of the tool.

```

--------------------------------

### Complete Chat Example with Data Part Handling

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/04-ai-sdk-ui/20-streaming-data.mdx

A full example of a chat component using `useChat`. It includes sending user messages, handling the `onData` callback for transient notifications, and rendering different types of persistent data parts (weather, text) within the message history.

```tsx
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { useState } from 'react';
import { MyUIMessage } from '@/ai/types';

export default function Chat() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');

  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat<MyUIMessage>({
    api: '/api/chat',
    onData: dataPart => {
      // Handle transient notifications
      if (dataPart.type === 'data-notification') {
        console.log('Notification:', dataPart.data.message);
      }
    },
  });

  const handleSubmit = (e: React.FormEvent) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    sendMessage({ text: input });
    setInput('');
  };

  return (
    <>
      {messages?.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id}>
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}

          {/* Render weather data */}
          {message.parts
            .filter(part => part.type === 'data-weather')
            .map((part, index) => (
              <span key={index} className="weather-update">
                {part.data.status === 'loading' ? (
                  <>Getting weather for {part.data.city}...</>
                ) : (
                  <>
                    Weather in {part.data.city}: {part.data.weather}
                  </>
                )}
              </span>
            ))}

          {/* Render text content */}
          {message.parts
            .filter(part => part.type === 'text')
            .map((part, index) => (
              <div key={index}>{part.text}</div>
            ))}
        </div>
      ))}

      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit}>
        <input
          value={input}
          onChange={e => setInput(e.target.value)}
          placeholder="Ask about the weather..."
        />
        <button type="submit">Send</button>
      </form>
    </>
  );
}
```

### Valibot Schema Conversion Example

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/01-ai-sdk-core/27-valibot-schema.mdx

Demonstrates how to use the `valibotSchema` helper function to convert a Valibot schema definition into a JSON schema compatible with the AI SDK. This is useful for structured data generation and tool integration.

```typescript
import {
  valibotSchema
} from '@ai-sdk/valibot';
import {
  object,
  string,
  array
} from 'valibot';

const recipeSchema = valibotSchema(
  object({
    name: string(),
    ingredients: array(
      object({
        name: string(),
        amount: string(),
      }),
    ),
    steps: array(string()),
  }),
);
```

### Computer Tool API Documentation

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/05-anthropic.mdx

API reference for the Computer Tool, outlining supported actions, required parameters like coordinates and text, and how to map tool results for LLM consumption.

```APIDOC
ComputerTool:
  Constructor Parameters:
    displayWidthPx (number): Width of the display in pixels.
    displayHeightPx (number): Height of the display in pixels.
    displayNumber (number, optional): Display number, typically for X11 environments.
  execute(params):
    Parameters:
      action (string): The action to perform. Allowed values: 'key', 'type', 'mouse_move', 'left_click', 'left_click_drag', 'right_click', 'middle_click', 'double_click', 'screenshot', 'cursor_position'.
      coordinate (number[], optional): Required for 'mouse_move' and 'left_click_drag'. Specifies the (x, y) coordinates.
      text (string, optional): Required for 'type' and 'key' actions.
    Returns: The result of the action, which can be text or image data.
  toModelOutput(result):
    Maps the tool's execution result to a format consumable by the LLM, supporting text and image types.
```

```typescript
  },
```

### Configure Perplexity Provider Options

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/70-perplexity.mdx

Customize Perplexity provider behavior by passing `providerOptions`. This example shows how to enable image responses by setting `return_images: true`, which is available for Tier-2 Perplexity users and above. Metadata like usage statistics and image URLs are included in `providerMetadata`.

```ts
import { perplexity } from '@ai-sdk/perplexity';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const result = await generateText({
  model: perplexity('sonar-pro'),
  prompt: 'What are the latest developments in quantum computing?',
  providerOptions: {
    perplexity: {
      return_images: true, // Enable image responses (Tier-2 Perplexity users only)
    },
  },
});

console.log(result.providerMetadata);
// Example output:
// {
//   perplexity: {
//     usage: { citationTokens: 5286, numSearchQueries: 1 },
//     images: [
//       { imageUrl: "https://example.com/image1.jpg", originUrl: "https://elsewhere.com/page1", height: 1280, width: 720 },
//       { imageUrl: "https://example.com/image2.jpg", originUrl: "https://elsewhere.com/page2", height: 1280, width: 720 }
//     ]
//   },
// }
```

### Call Tools in Multiple Steps with AI SDK (Node.js)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/05-node/53-call-tools-multiple-steps.mdx

Demonstrates how to enable multi-step tool calls in the AI SDK for Node.js. It uses `generateText` with `stopWhen: stepCountIs(5)` to limit the number of tool call steps. The example includes defining a tool for fetching weather information with a Zod schema for input validation.

```typescript
import {
  generateText,
  tool,
  stepCountIs
} from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { text, steps } = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-4.1'),
  stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
  tools: {
    weather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }: { location: string }) => ({
        location,
        temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10,
      }),
    }),
  },
  prompt: 'What is the weather in San Francisco?',
});

```
