### Create Google Vertex AI Embedding Model

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/16-google-vertex.mdx

Shows how to instantiate an embedding model using the Google Vertex AI provider with the `.textEmbedding()` factory method. It includes an example of passing provider-specific options like `outputDimensionality`.

```ts
import { vertex } from '@ai-sdk/google-vertex';
import { embed } from 'ai';

const model = vertex.textEmbedding('text-embedding-004');

const { embedding } = await embed({
  model,
  value: 'sunny day at the beach',
  providerOptions: {
    google: {
      outputDimensionality: 512, // optional, number of dimensions for the embedding
    },
  },
});
```

### Stream Text with Mock Language Model

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/03-ai-sdk-core/55-testing.mdx

Illustrates simulating a streaming text response using `MockLanguageModelV2` and `simulateReadableStream` with the `streamText` function. This example defines a sequence of chunks, including text deltas and a final finish signal, to mimic a real-time stream for testing.

```typescript
import { streamText, simulateReadableStream } from 'ai';
import { MockLanguageModelV2 } from 'ai/test';

const result = streamText({
  model: new MockLanguageModelV2({
    doStream: async () => ({
      stream: simulateReadableStream({
        chunks: [
          { type: 'text-start', id: 'text-1' },
          { type: 'text-delta', id: 'text-1', delta: 'Hello' },
          { type: 'text-delta', id: 'text-1', delta: ', ' },
          { type: 'text-delta', id: 'text-1', delta: 'world!' },
          { type: 'text-end', id: 'text-1' },
          {
            type: 'finish',
            finishReason: 'stop',
            logprobs: undefined,
            usage: { inputTokens: 3, outputTokens: 10, totalTokens: 13 },
          },
        ],
      }),
    }),
  }),
  prompt: 'Hello, test!',
});
```

### Generate Text with Mock Language Model

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/03-ai-sdk-core/55-testing.mdx

Demonstrates using `MockLanguageModelV2` with the `generateText` function. This example shows how to configure the mock model to return a predefined text response and usage statistics, allowing for deterministic testing of text generation logic.

```typescript
import { generateText } from 'ai';
import { MockLanguageModelV2 } from 'ai/test';

const result = await generateText({
  model: new MockLanguageModelV2({
    doGenerate: async () => ({
      finishReason: 'stop',
      usage: { inputTokens: 10, outputTokens: 20, totalTokens: 30 },
      content: [{ type: 'text', text: `Hello, world!` }],
      warnings: [],
    }),
  }),
  prompt: 'Hello, test!',
});
```

### Streaming UI Components with createStreamableUI

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/06-advanced/07-rendering-ui-with-language-models.mdx

This example shows how to use the `createStreamableUI` function from `@ai-sdk/rsc` to stream React components from the server. It integrates with a language model's tool execution to render a `WeatherCard` component and stream it to the client.

```typescript
import { createStreamableUI } from '@ai-sdk/rsc'

const uiStream = createStreamableUI();

const text = generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-3.5-turbo'),
  system: 'you are a friendly assistant'
  prompt: 'what is the weather in SF?'
  tools: {
    getWeather: {
      description: 'Get the weather for a location',
      parameters: z.object({
        city: z.string().describe('The city to get the weather for'),
        unit: z
          .enum(['C', 'F'])
          .describe('The unit to display the temperature in')
      }),
      execute: async ({ city, unit }) => {
        const weather = getWeather({ city, unit })
        const { temperature, unit, description, forecast } = weather

        uiStream.done(
          <WeatherCard
            weather={{
              temperature: 47,
              unit: 'F',
              description: 'sunny'
              forecast,
            }}
          />
        )
      }
    }
  }
})

return {
  display: uiStream.value
}
```

### Example Usage: @built-in-ai/core

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/03-community-providers/100-built-in-ai.mdx

Demonstrates streaming text generation using the `@built-in-ai/core` provider with the AI SDK. It calls `streamText` with the `builtInAI` model and logs the streamed output.

```typescript
import { streamText } from 'ai';
import { builtInAI } from '@built-in-ai/core';

const result = streamText({
  model: builtInAI(), // will default to the specific browser model
  prompt: 'Hello, how are you',
});

for await (const chunk of result.textStream) {
  console.log(chunk);
}
```

### Use StreamUI with Initial Loading Indicator in TSX

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/05-ai-sdk-rsc/10-migrating-to-ui.mdx

Shows how to implement loading indicators in AI SDK RSC using the `initial` parameter of `streamUI`. This example defines a component to display while the generation is in progress, demonstrating a common pattern for user feedback during asynchronous operations.

```tsx
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { streamUI } from '@ai-sdk/rsc';

const { value: stream } = await streamUI({
  model: openai('gpt-4o'),
  system: 'you are a friendly assistant!',
  messages,
  initial: <div>Loading...</div>,
  text: async function* ({ content, done }) {
    // process text
  },
  tools: {
    // tool definitions
  },
});

return stream;
```

### Use Tools for Agentic Behavior

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/19-openai-responses.mdx

Illustrates how to enable agentic behavior by allowing the AI model to call external tools. This example uses a `getWeather` tool and the `stopWhen` parameter to manage multi-step LLM calls. It requires importing `generateText`, `tool`, and `stepCountIs` from 'ai', the OpenAI provider, and Zod for tool input schema. The output is text, but the process involves tool execution.

```typescript
import { generateText, tool, stepCountIs } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: openai.responses('gpt-4o'),
  prompt: 'What is the weather like today in San Francisco?',
  tools: {
    getWeather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => ({
        location,
        temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10,
      }),
    }),
  },
  stopWhen: stepCountIs(5), // enable multi-step 'agentic' LLM calls
});
```

### APIDOC: AI SDK Tool Definition and Usage

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/03-slackbot.mdx

Defines the structure for creating and integrating tools with the AI SDK. It includes the `tool` function for defining tool capabilities, input schemas using Zod, and execution logic. Also details the `generateText` function's parameters for model interaction and tool invocation.

```APIDOC
AI SDK Tool Integration:

This section documents the core components for defining and using tools within the AI SDK, enabling AI agents to perform external actions.

1.  `tool` Function:
    - Purpose: Factory function to define a tool for the AI model.
    - Signature: `tool({ description: string, inputSchema: ZodSchema, execute: (params: any) => Promise<any> })`
    - Parameters:
        - `description`: A human-readable description of what the tool does. This is crucial for the AI model to understand when to use the tool.
        - `inputSchema`: A Zod schema defining the expected input parameters for the tool. This ensures type safety and provides structure for the AI model's output.
        - `execute`: An asynchronous function that performs the tool's action. It receives the validated input parameters and returns the result.
    - Example Tool Definition (`getWeather`):
      ```typescript
      getWeather: tool({
        description: 'Get the current weather at a location',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          latitude: z.number(),
          longitude: z.number(),
          city: z.string(),
        }),
        execute: async ({ latitude, longitude, city }) => {
          // ... fetch weather data ...
          return { temperature: 25, weatherCode: 0, humidity: 60, city: 'London' };
        },
      })
      ```

2.  `generateText` Function:
    - Purpose: Orchestrates AI model interaction, including tool calls.
    - Signature: `generateText({ model: Model, system?: string, messages: ModelMessage[], stopWhen?: StopCondition, tools?: { [toolName: string]: ToolDefinition } })`
    - Parameters:
        - `model`: The AI model to use (e.g., `openai('gpt-4o')`).
        - `system`: A system prompt to guide the AI's behavior and context.
        - `messages`: An array of messages representing the conversation history.
        - `stopWhen`: Defines conditions under which the generation process should stop (e.g., `stepCountIs(10)` for multi-step conversations).
        - `tools`: An object where keys are tool names and values are `ToolDefinition` objects created using the `tool` function. This enables the AI to discover and invoke available tools.
    - Return Value: An object containing the generated `text` and potentially other metadata.

3.  `stepCountIs` Function:
    - Purpose: A helper function to create a `StopCondition` that stops generation after a specified number of steps (tool calls + responses).
    - Signature: `stepCountIs(count: number)`
    - Usage: `stopWhen: stepCountIs(10)` allows for up to 10 turns in the agent's execution flow.

4.  `exa.searchAndContents` (External Tool Example):
    - Purpose: Searches the web and retrieves content snippets using the Exa API.
    - Signature: `exa.searchAndContents(query: string, options?: { livecrawl: 'always' | 'never' | 'once', numResults: number, includeDomains?: string[] })`
    - Parameters:
        - `query`: The search query string.
        - `options`: Configuration for the search, including crawl behavior, number of results, and specific domains to include.
    - Return Value: An object containing an array of `results`, where each result has `title`, `url`, and `snippet` properties.

Example Usage within `generateResponse`:

The `generateResponse` function orchestrates these components. It calls `generateText` with a model, system prompt, messages, a stopping condition, and a dictionary of defined tools (`getWeather`, `searchWeb`). The AI model then decides which tool to call based on the user's input and the provided tool descriptions and schemas. The `execute` function of the chosen tool is invoked, and its result is fed back to the model for further processing or final response generation.
```

### Use streamUI function with OpenAI provider

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/08-migration-guides/39-migration-guide-3-1.mdx

Illustrates the usage of the new `streamUI` function from the AI SDK RSC API, allowing integration with any compatible AI provider. This example uses the OpenAI provider and defines tools with a `generate` key for returning React Server Components.

```typescript
import { streamUI } from '@ai-sdk/rsc';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';
import { Spinner, Weather } from '@/components';
import { getWeather } from '@/utils';

async function submitMessage(userInput = 'What is the weather in SF?') {
  'use server';

  const result = await streamUI({
    model: openai('gpt-4.1'),
    system: 'You are a helpful assistant',
    messages: [{ role: 'user', content: userInput }],
    text: ({ content }) => <p>{content}</p>,
    tools: {
      get_city_weather: {
        description: 'Get the current weather for a city',
        parameters: z
          .object({
            city: z.string().describe('Name of the city'),
          })
          .required(),
        generate: async function* ({ city }) {
          yield <Spinner />;
          const weather = await getWeather(city);
          return <Weather info={weather} />;
        },
      },
    },
  });

  return result.value;
}
```

--------------------------------

### Streaming System - Stream Parts

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/03-community-providers/01-custom-providers.mdx

Details the typed events used in the Vercel AI SDK's streaming system. Covers lifecycle events like stream start, response metadata, and finish, as well as content events for incremental updates.

```APIDOC
Streaming System Events:

1. Stream Lifecycle Events:
   - `stream-start`:
     - Description: Initial event indicating the start of a stream. May include warnings about unsupported features.
     - Example:
       ```ts
       { type: 'stream-start', warnings: [] }
       ```
   - `response-metadata`:
     - Description: Provides model information and response headers.
     - Example:
       ```ts
       { type: 'response-metadata', modelId: 'gpt-4.1', ... }
       ```
   - `finish`:
     - Description: Final event containing usage statistics and the reason for stream termination.
     - Example:
       ```ts
       { type: 'finish', usage: { inputTokens: 10, outputTokens: 20 }, finishReason: 'stop' }
       ```
   - `error`:
     - Description: Events indicating errors that can occur at any point during the stream.

2. Content Events:
   - All content types (`text`, `file`, `reasoning`, `source`, `tool-call`) stream directly.
   - `tool-call-delta`:
     - Description: Provides incremental updates for tool call arguments.
   - `reasoning-part-finish`:
     - Description: An explicit marker for the completion of a reasoning section.

Example Stream Sequence:
```ts
{
  type: 'stream-start',
  warnings: []
}
{
  type: 'text',
  text: 'Hello'
}
{
  type: 'text',
  text: ' world'
}
{
  type: 'tool-call',
  toolCallId: '1',
  toolName: 'search',
  args: {...}
}
{
  type: 'response-metadata',
  modelId: 'gpt-4.1',
  ...
}
{
  type: 'finish',
  usage: { inputTokens: 10, outputTokens: 20 },
  finishReason: 'stop'
}
```
```

--------------------------------

### Tool Input Start Event

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/04-ai-sdk-ui/50-stream-protocol.mdx

Indicates the beginning of tool input streaming. This SSE part includes a JSON object with the event type 'tool-input-start', the tool call identifier, and the name of the tool.

```APIDOC
data: {"type":"tool-input-start","toolCallId":"call_fJdQDqnXeGxTmr4E3YPSR7Ar","toolName":"getWeatherInformation"}
```

--------------------------------

### Create Chat API Route

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/07-expo.mdx

Defines a serverless API route handler for POST requests at `/api/chat`. This route processes incoming chat messages, streams responses using the AI SDK's `streamText` function with the OpenAI model, and returns a streamed response to the client.

```tsx
import {
  openai
} from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import {
  streamText,
  UIMessage,
  convertToModelMessages
} from 'ai';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse({
    headers: {
      'Content-Type': 'application/octet-stream',
      'Content-Encoding': 'none',
    },
  });
}
```

--------------------------------

### Route Handler with Legacy OpenAI SDK

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/08-migration-guides/39-migration-guide-3-1.mdx

Example of a Next.js Route Handler using the legacy OpenAI SDK to query a model and stream the response. It utilizes OpenAIStream and StreamingTextResponse from the 'ai' package.

```tsx
import OpenAI from 'openai';
import { OpenAIStream, StreamingTextResponse } from 'ai';

const openai = new OpenAI({
  apiKey: process.env.OPENAI_API_KEY!,
});

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages } = await req.json();

  const response = await openai.chat.completions.create({
    model: 'gpt-4.1',
    stream: true,
    messages,
  });

  const stream = OpenAIStream(response);

  return new StreamingTextResponse(stream);
}
```

### Create Custom Fal Provider Instance

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/10-fal.mdx

```ts
import { createFal } from '@ai-sdk/fal';

const fal = createFal({
  apiKey: 'your-api-key', // optional, defaults to FAL_API_KEY environment variable, falling back to FAL_KEY
  baseURL: 'custom-url', // optional
  headers: {
    /* custom headers */
  }, // optional
});
```

### streamText() Function Example

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/01-ai-sdk-core/02-stream-text.mdx

Demonstrates how to use the streamText function to generate text from a language model and stream it. It's suitable for real-time applications like chatbots.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { streamText } from 'ai';

const { textStream } = streamText({
  model: openai('gpt-4o'),
  prompt: 'Invent a new holiday and describe its traditions.',
});

for await (const textPart of textStream) {
  process.stdout.write(textPart);
}
```

### Create AI Context with createAI

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/05-ai-sdk-rsc/03-generative-ui-state.mdx

Initializes the AI context using the `createAI` function from the SDK. It requires defining the AI state and UI state types, providing initial states, and listing allowed server actions.

```ts
import { createAI } from '@ai-sdk/rsc';
import { ClientMessage, ServerMessage, sendMessage } from './actions';

export type AIState = ServerMessage[];
export type UIState = ClientMessage[];

export const AI = createAI<AIState, UIState>({
  initialAIState: [],
  initialUIState: [],
  actions: {
    sendMessage,
  },
});
```

### Convert LlamaIndex ChatEngine Stream

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/04-stream-helpers/16-llamaindex-adapter.mdx

Example demonstrating how to use the `toDataStreamResponse` function to convert a LlamaIndex ChatEngine stream into an HTTP response.

```tsx
import { OpenAI, SimpleChatEngine } from 'llamaindex';
import { toDataStreamResponse } from '@ai-sdk/llamaindex';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { prompt } = await req.json();

  const llm = new OpenAI({ model: 'gpt-4o' });
  const chatEngine = new SimpleChatEngine({ llm });

  const stream = await chatEngine.chat({
    message: prompt,
    stream: true,
  });

  return toDataStreamResponse(stream);
}
```

### Simulate Streaming with Non-Streaming Model

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/01-ai-sdk-core/67-simulate-streaming-middleware.mdx

Demonstrates how to integrate simulateStreamingMiddleware into a language model wrapper. This setup allows you to use a consistent streaming API, even when interacting with models that return complete responses.

```ts
import { streamText } from 'ai';
import { wrapLanguageModel } from 'ai';
import { simulateStreamingMiddleware } from 'ai';

// Example with a non-streaming model
const result = streamText({
  model: wrapLanguageModel({
    model: nonStreamingModel,
    middleware: simulateStreamingMiddleware(),
  }),
  prompt: 'Your prompt here',
});

// Now you can use the streaming interface
for await (const chunk of result.fullStream) {
  // Process streaming chunks
}
```

### Generate Object with Schema

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/01-ai-sdk-core/03-generate-object.mdx

Generates a typed, structured object using a Zod schema for a given prompt and language model. This example demonstrates creating a recipe object.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { generateObject } from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { object } = await generateObject({
  model: openai('gpt-4.1'),
  schema: z.object({
    recipe: z.object({
      name: z.string(),
      ingredients: z.array(z.string()),
      steps: z.array(z.string()),
    }),
  }),
  prompt: 'Generate a lasagna recipe.',
});

console.log(JSON.stringify(object, null, 2));
```

### Generate Image with LangDB

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/03-community-providers/94-langdb.mdx

Utilize the `experimental_generateImage` function with a LangDB image model. This example demonstrates generating an image and saving it to a file.

```tsx
import { createLangDB } from '@langdb/vercel-provider';
import { experimental_generateImage as generateImage } from 'ai';
import fs from 'fs';
import path from 'path';

const langdb = createLangDB({
  apiKey: process.env.LANGDB_API_KEY,
  projectId: 'your-project-id',
});

export async function generateImageExample() {
  const { images } = await generateImage({
    model: langdb.image('openai/dall-e-3'),
    prompt: 'A delighted resplendent quetzal mid-flight amidst raindrops',
  });

  const imagePath = path.join(__dirname, 'generated-image.png');
  fs.writeFileSync(imagePath, images[0].uint8Array);
  console.log(`Image saved to: ${imagePath}`);
}
```

### smoothStream() Custom Callback Chunking Example

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/01-ai-sdk-core/80-smooth-stream.mdx

Shows how to provide a custom callback function to smoothStream for advanced chunking logic, allowing precise control over text segmentation.

```ts
smoothStream({
  chunking: text => {
    const findString = 'some string';
    const index = text.indexOf(findString);

    if (index === -1) {
      return null;
    }

    return text.slice(0, index) + findString;
  },
});
```

### TypeScript: Force Tool Call with generateText

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/03-ai-sdk-core/15-tools-and-tool-calling.mdx

Example demonstrating how to use the `toolChoice: 'required'` option with `generateText` to ensure the model invokes a tool.

```ts
import { z } from 'zod';
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';

const result = await generateText({
  model: 'openai/gpt-4o',
  tools: {
    weather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => ({
        location,
        temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10,
      }),
    }),
  },
  toolChoice: 'required', // force the model to call a tool
  prompt: 'What is the weather in San Francisco?',
});
```

### smoothStream() Japanese Chunking Example

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/01-ai-sdk-core/80-smooth-stream.mdx

Illustrates how to use smoothStream with a custom regex for effective word chunking in Japanese text, addressing its lack of space delimiters.

```tsx
import { smoothStream, streamText } from 'ai';

const result = streamText({
  model: 'openai/gpt-4.1',
  prompt: 'Your prompt here',
  experimental_transform: smoothStream({
    chunking: /[぀-ゟ゠-ヿ]|S+s+/,
  }),
});
```

### Computer Tool Initialization and Execution

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/08-amazon-bedrock.mdx

Initializes the Computer Tool for controlling keyboard and mouse actions. It requires display dimensions and an execute function to handle actions like screenshots, typing, and clicks. The toModelOutput function maps tool results for LLM consumption.

```ts
const computerTool = anthropic.tools.computer_20241022({
  displayWidthPx: 1920,
  displayHeightPx: 1080,
  displayNumber: 0, // Optional, for X11 environments

  execute: async ({ action, coordinate, text }) => {
    // Implement your computer control logic here
    // Return the result of the action

    // Example code:
    switch (action) {
      case 'screenshot': {
        // multipart result:
        return {
          type: 'image',
          data: fs
            .readFileSync('./data/screenshot-editor.png')
            .toString('base64'),
        };
      }
      default: {
        console.log('Action:', action);
        console.log('Coordinate:', coordinate);
        console.log('Text:', text);
        return `executed ${action}`;
      }
    }
  },

  // map to tool result content for LLM consumption:
  toModelOutput(result) {
    return typeof result === 'string'
      ? [{ type: 'text', text: result }]
      : [{ type: 'image', data: result.data, mediaType: 'image/png' }];
  },
});
```

### Implement Chat UI with useChat Hook in React Native

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/07-expo.mdx

This code sets up a basic chat interface in a React Native application using the `@ai-sdk/react` library's `useChat` hook. It displays messages, handles user input, and sends messages to a backend API. Dependencies include `@ai-sdk/react` and `expo/fetch` for streaming. It takes user input and displays LLM responses.

```tsx
import { generateAPIUrl } from '@/utils';
import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { DefaultChatTransport } from 'ai';
import { fetch as expoFetch } from 'expo/fetch';
import { useState } from 'react';
import { View, TextInput, ScrollView, Text, SafeAreaView } from 'react-native';

export default function App() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, error, sendMessage } = useChat({
    transport: new DefaultChatTransport({
      fetch: expoFetch as unknown as typeof globalThis.fetch,
      api: generateAPIUrl('/api/chat'),
    }),
    onError: error => console.error(error, 'ERROR'),
  });

  if (error) return <Text>{error.message}</Text>;

  return (
    <SafeAreaView style={{ height: '100%' }}>
      <View
        style={{
          height: '95%',
          display: 'flex',
          flexDirection: 'column',
          paddingHorizontal: 8,
        }}
      >
        <ScrollView style={{ flex: 1 }}>
          {messages.map(m => (
            <View key={m.id} style={{ marginVertical: 8 }}>
              <View>
                <Text style={{ fontWeight: 700 }}>{m.role}</Text>
                {m.parts.map((part, i) => {
                  switch (part.type) {
                    case 'text':
                      return <Text key={`${m.id}-${i}`}>{part.text}</Text>;
                  }
                })}
              </View>
            </View>
          ))}
        </ScrollView>

        <View style={{ marginTop: 8 }}>
          <TextInput
            style={{ backgroundColor: 'white', padding: 8 }}
            placeholder="Say something..."
            value={input}
            onChange={e => setInput(e.nativeEvent.text)}
            onSubmitEditing={e => {
              e.preventDefault();
              sendMessage({ text: input });
              setInput('');
            }}
            autoFocus={true}
          />
        </View>
      </View>
    </SafeAreaView>
  );
}

```

--------------------------------

### AI SDK Codemod CLI Usage

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/packages/codemod/README.md

This section details how to use the AI SDK codemod CLI tool. It covers the main command structure, available commands for applying codemods, global options for controlling execution, and practical examples.

```APIDOC
CLI Usage:
  npx @ai-sdk/codemod@beta <command> [options]

Available Commands:
  upgrade          Apply all codemods (v4 + v5)
  v4               Apply v4 codemods (v3 → v4 migration)
  v5               Apply v5 codemods (v4 → v5 migration)
  <codemod-name> <path>  Apply specific codemod

Global Options:
  --dry            Preview changes without applying them
  --print          Print transformed code to stdout
  --verbose        Show detailed transformation logs

Examples:
  # Preview all changes without applying
  npx @ai-sdk/codemod@beta --dry upgrade

  # Preview v4 changes only
  npx @ai-sdk/codemod@beta --dry v4

  # Preview v5 changes only
  npx @ai-sdk/codemod@beta --dry v5

  # Show verbose output for specific codemod
  npx @ai-sdk/codemod@beta --verbose v4/remove-experimental-ai-fn-exports src/

  # Print transformed code for specific codemod
  npx @ai-sdk/codemod@beta --print v4/replace-baseurl src/config.ts
```

### Google Vertex Anthropic Provider Setup

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/16-google-vertex.mdx

Explains how to set up and use the Google Vertex Anthropic provider for accessing Anthropic's Claude models. It covers importing default instances and creating custom configurations.

```ts
import { vertexAnthropic } from '@ai-sdk/google-vertex/anthropic';
```

```ts
import { createVertexAnthropic } from '@ai-sdk/google-vertex/anthropic';

const vertexAnthropic = createVertexAnthropic({
  project: 'my-project', // optional
  location: 'us-central1', // optional
});
```

Provides an example of how to catch and handle the specific `AI_NoImageGeneratedError` that occurs when image generation fails. It shows how to access error details like `cause` and `responses` for debugging.

```ts
import { generateImage, NoImageGeneratedError } from 'ai';

try {
  await generateImage({ model, prompt });
} catch (error) {
  if (NoImageGeneratedError.isInstance(error)) {
    console.log('NoImageGeneratedError');
    console.log('Cause:', error.cause);
    console.log('Responses:', error.responses);
  }
}
```

### AI SDK Tool Definitions and Execution

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/01-next/72-call-tools-multiple-steps.mdx

Defines tools for interacting with language models, including schemas for input parameters and execution logic. This section details the `getLocation` and `getWeather` tools, their Zod schemas, and how they are integrated into the AI SDK for multi-step execution.

```APIDOC
Tool Definitions:

  getLocation: Tool
    description: Get the location of the user
    inputSchema: z.object({})
    execute: async () => { ... }
      - Returns: string (e.g., "Your location is at latitude 37.7749 and longitude -122.4194")

  getWeather: Tool
    description: Get the weather for a location
    inputSchema: z.object({
      city: z.string().describe('The city to get the weather for'),
      unit: z.enum(['C', 'F']).describe('The unit to display the temperature in')
    })
    execute: async ({ city, unit }) => { ... }
      - Returns: string (e.g., "It is currently 24°C and Sunny in San Francisco!")

AI SDK Functions:

  streamText(options)
    - Generates a text stream from a language model.
    - Parameters:
      - model: The language model to use (e.g., openai('gpt-4o')).
      - system: System prompt for the assistant.
      - messages: Array of chat messages.
      - stopWhen: Condition to stop generation (e.g., stepCountIs(5)).
      - tools: ToolSet object containing defined tools.
    - Returns: StreamTextResult object.

  stepCountIs(count: number): StopCondition
    - Creates a stop condition that halts generation after a specified number of tool call steps.

  tool(options): Tool
    - Defines a tool with description, input schema, and execution logic.

  convertToModelMessages(messages: UIMessage[]): ModelMessage[]
    - Converts UI messages to the format expected by the model.

Type Definitions:

  ChatMessage = UIMessage<never, UIDataTypes, ChatTools>
    - Represents a chat message with support for tool calls.

  ChatTools = InferUITools<typeof tools>
    - Infers the tool types from the ToolSet definition.

```

--------------------------------

### Chat Route Handler using AI SDK

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/02-nextjs-app-router.mdx

Implements a POST request handler for a chat API. It processes incoming messages, calls the AI SDK's streamText function with a specified model (OpenAI GPT-4o), and returns the AI's response as a UI-compatible stream.

```tsx
import {
  openai
} from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import {
  streamText,
  UIMessage,
  convertToModelMessages
} from 'ai';

// Allow streaming responses up to 30 seconds
export const maxDuration = 30;

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### Example Usage of useStreamableValue

Demonstrates how to use the useStreamableValue hook within a React component to consume a streamable value. It handles loading, error, and data display states.

```tsx
function MyComponent({ streamableValue }) {
  const [data, error, pending] = useStreamableValue(streamableValue);

  if (pending) return <div>Loading...</div>;
  if (error) return <div>Error: {error.message}</div>;

  return <div>Data: {data}</div>;
}
```

const result = await generateText({

    {

### Generate AI Response with SDK

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/03-slackbot.mdx

Generates a response using the AI SDK, specifically targeting OpenAI models like GPT-4o-mini. It takes conversation history and an optional status updater, formats a system prompt, and processes the AI's text output, converting markdown to Slack's mrkdwn format. Dependencies include the AI SDK and OpenAI integration.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { generateText, ModelMessage } from 'ai';

export const generateResponse = async (
  messages: ModelMessage[],
  updateStatus?: (status: string) => void,
) => {
  const { text } = await generateText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o-mini'),
    system: `You are a Slack bot assistant. Keep your responses concise and to the point.
    - Do not tag users.
    - Current date is: ${new Date().toISOString().split('T')[0]}`, 
    messages,
  });

  // Convert markdown to Slack mrkdwn format
  return text.replace(/[(.*?)](.*?[\s]*)/g, '<$2|$1>').replace(/\*\*/g, '*');
};
```

### Generate Object with Mock Language Model

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/03-ai-sdk-core/55-testing.mdx

Shows how to use `MockLanguageModelV2` with `generateObject` to simulate the generation of structured data. This example configures the mock model to return a JSON string that conforms to a Zod schema, enabling testing of object parsing and generation logic.

```typescript
import { generateObject } from 'ai';
import { MockLanguageModelV2 } from 'ai/test';
import { z } from 'zod';

const result = await generateObject({
  model: new MockLanguageModelV2({
    doGenerate: async () => ({
      finishReason: 'stop',
      usage: { inputTokens: 10, outputTokens: 20, totalTokens: 30 },
      content: [{ type: 'text', text: `{"content":"Hello, world!"}` }],
      warnings: [],
    }),
  }),
  schema: z.object({ content: z.string() }),
  prompt: 'Hello, test!',
});
```

### Frontend Integration: Calling Server Action

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/04-natural-language-postgres.mdx

Updates the frontend `handleSubmit` function to call the `generateQuery` Server Action with the user's input. It then passes the generated SQL query to another action (`runGeneratedSQLQuery`) and updates the UI with results.

```typescript
/* ...other imports... */
import { runGeneratedSQLQuery, generateQuery } from './actions';

/* ...rest of the file... */

const handleSubmit = async (suggestion?: string) => {
  clearExistingData();

  const question = suggestion ?? inputValue;
  if (inputValue.length === 0 && !suggestion) return;

  if (question.trim()) {
    setSubmitted(true);
  }

  setLoading(true);
  setLoadingStep(1);
  setActiveQuery('');

  try {
    const query = await generateQuery(question);

    if (query === undefined) {
      toast.error('An error occurred. Please try again.');
      setLoading(false);
      return;
    }

    setActiveQuery(query);
    setLoadingStep(2);

    const companies = await runGeneratedSQLQuery(query);
    const columns = companies.length > 0 ? Object.keys(companies[0]) : [];
    setResults(companies);
    setColumns(columns);

    setLoading(false);
  } catch (e) {
    toast.error('An error occurred. Please try again.');
    setLoading(false);
  }
};

/* ...rest of the file... */
```

### Configure xAI Provider Options for Models

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/01-xai.mdx

import { xai } from '@ai-sdk/xai';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const model = xai('grok-3-mini');

await generateText({
  model,
  providerOptions: {
    xai: {
      reasoningEffort: 'high',
    },
  },
});

Set `with_timestamps` to `true` in `providerOptions` to include start and end timestamps for each word or token in the transcription output. The default value is `false`.

  sarvam: {

Demonstrates how to initialize the web search tool with parameters like maximum uses, allowed/blocked domains, and user location for geographically relevant results. This configuration is then passed to a text generation function.

```ts
const webSearchTool = anthropic.tools.webSearch_20250305({
  maxUses: 3,
  allowedDomains: ['techcrunch.com', 'wired.com'],
  blockedDomains: ['example-spam-site.com'],
  userLocation: {
    type: 'approximate',
    country: 'US',
    region: 'California',
    city: 'San Francisco',
    timezone: 'America/Los_Angeles',
  },
});

const result = await generateText({
  model: anthropic('claude-opus-4-20250514'),

    web_search: webSearchTool,
  },
});

### Generate Text with Experimental Output Schema

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/03-openai.mdx

Illustrates using `generateText` with the `experimental_output` option to guide the model towards a specific output format using a Zod schema. This is useful for simpler structured outputs within text generation.

```typescript
import { generateText, Output } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import z from 'zod';

const result = await generateText({
  model: openai.responses('gpt-4.1'),
  prompt: 'How do I make a pizza?',
  experimental_output: Output.object({
    schema: z.object({
      ingredients: z.array(z.string()),
      steps: z.array(z.string()),
    }),
  }),
});

// result.text will contain the generated text, potentially including structured data if the model adheres to the schema
```

### Rename maxTokens to maxOutputTokens

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/08-migration-guides/26-migration-guide-5-0.mdx

Example showing the change in the `maxTokens` parameter to `maxOutputTokens` for controlling the maximum number of tokens in `generateText` calls.

```tsx
const result = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-4.1'),
  maxTokens: 1024,
  prompt: 'Hello, world!',
});
```

```tsx
const result = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-4.1'),
  maxOutputTokens: 1024,
  prompt: 'Hello, world!',
});
```

### Deterministic Function Execution with Language Models

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/06-advanced/08-model-as-router.mdx

Demonstrates how to use language models to execute specific functions based on user prompts, ensuring deterministic outputs. The example uses a hypothetical `generateText` function with tool definitions, showing how the model can select the appropriate function (e.g., `getWeather`) or refrain from executing any if the query is out of scope.

```tsx
const sendMessage = (prompt: string) =>
  generateText({
    model: 'gpt-3.5-turbo',
    system: 'you are a friendly weather assistant!',
    prompt,
    tools: {
      getWeather: {
        description: 'Get the weather in a location',
        parameters: z.object({
          location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ location }: { location: string }) => ({
          location,
          temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10,
        }),
      },
    },
  });

sendMessage('What is the weather in San Francisco?'); // getWeather is called
sendMessage('What is the weather in New York?'); // getWeather is called
sendMessage('What events are happening in London?'); // No function is called
```

--------------------------------

### AI Chatbot API Route with Weather Tool (TypeScript)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/07-expo.mdx

Defines a POST API route for a chatbot using the AI SDK. It integrates a weather tool that allows the LLM to fetch simulated weather data based on location input. The tool uses Zod for input schema validation and an async execute function for data retrieval.

```typescript
import {
  openai
} from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import {
  streamText,
  UIMessage,
  convertToModelMessages,
  tool
} from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
    tools: {
      weather: tool({
        description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ location }) => {
          const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
          return {
            location,
            temperature,
          };
        },
      }),
    },
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse({
    headers: {
      'Content-Type': 'application/octet-stream',
      'Content-Encoding': 'none',
    },
  });
}
```

### Send Custom Data Stream with Hono

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/15-api-servers/30-hono.mdx

Illustrates using `createDataStream` to send custom data alongside AI-generated content. This allows for more complex client-server communication, including initialization messages and error handling.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { serve } from '@hono/node-server';
import { createDataStream, streamText } from 'ai';
import { Hono } from 'hono';
import { stream } from 'hono/streaming';

const app = new Hono();

app.post('/stream-data', async c => {
  // immediately start streaming the response
  const dataStream = createDataStream({
    execute: async dataStreamWriter => {
      dataStreamWriter.writeData('initialized call');

      const result = streamText({
        model: openai('gpt-4o'),
        prompt: 'Invent a new holiday and describe its traditions.',
      });

      result.mergeIntoDataStream(dataStreamWriter);
    },
    onError: error => {
      // Error messages are masked by default for security reasons.
      // If you want to expose the error message to the client, you can do so here:
      return error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error);
    },
  });

  // Mark the response as a v1 data stream:
  c.header('X-Vercel-AI-Data-Stream', 'v1');
  c.header('Content-Type', 'text/plain; charset=utf-8');

  return stream(c, stream =>
    stream.pipe(dataStream.pipeThrough(new TextEncoderStream()))
  );
});

serve({ fetch: app.fetch, port: 8080 });

```

--------------------------------

### TypeScript: AI Response Generation with Tools

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/03-slackbot.mdx

Generates AI responses using the Vercel AI SDK, integrating custom tools for actions like fetching weather or searching the web. This function enables multi-step conversations by defining stopping conditions and tool execution.

```TypeScript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { generateText, tool, ModelMessage, stepCountIs } from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';
import { exa } from './utils';

export const generateResponse = async (
  messages: ModelMessage[],
  updateStatus?: (status: string) => void,
) => {
  const { text } = await generateText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    system: `You are a Slack bot assistant. Keep your responses concise and to the point.
    - Do not tag users.
    - Current date is: ${new Date().toISOString().split('T')[0]}
    - Always include sources in your final response if you use web search.`, // Note: Date formatting might need adjustment for specific locales
    messages,
    stopWhen: stepCountIs(10),
    tools: {
      getWeather: tool({
        description: 'Get the current weather at a location',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          latitude: z.number(),
          longitude: z.number(),
          city: z.string(),
        }),
        execute: async ({ latitude, longitude, city }) => {
          updateStatus?.(`is getting weather for ${city}...`);

          const response = await fetch(
            `https://api.open-meteo.com/v1/forecast?latitude=${latitude}&longitude=${longitude}&current=temperature_2m,weathercode,relativehumidity_2m&timezone=auto`,
          );

          const weatherData = await response.json();
          return {
            temperature: weatherData.current.temperature_2m,
            weatherCode: weatherData.current.weathercode,
            humidity: weatherData.current.relativehumidity_2m,
            city,
          };
        },
      }),
      searchWeb: tool({
        description: 'Use this to search the web for information',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          query: z.string(),
          specificDomain: z
            .string()
            .nullable()
            .describe(
              'a domain to search if the user specifies e.g. bbc.com. Should be only the domain name without the protocol',
            ),
        }),
        execute: async ({ query, specificDomain }) => {
          updateStatus?.(`is searching the web for ${query}...`);
          const { results } = await exa.searchAndContents(query, {
            livecrawl: 'always',
            numResults: 3,
            includeDomains: specificDomain ? [specificDomain] : undefined,
          });

          return {
            results: results.map(result => ({
              title: result.title,
              url: result.url,
              snippet: result.text.slice(0, 1000),
            })),
          };
        },
      }),
    },
  });

  // Convert markdown to Slack mrkdwn format
  return text.replace(/\[(.*?)\\]\((.*?)\)/g, '<$2|$1>').replace(/\*\*/g, '*');
};

```

--------------------------------

### Wire up Chat UI with useChat Hook (Vue)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/05-nuxt.mdx

Integrates a chat interface into a Vue.js application using the `useChat` hook from the AI SDK. It handles displaying messages and sending user input to the API.

```vue
<script setup lang="ts">
import { Chat } from "@ai-sdk/vue";
import { ref } from "vue";

const input = ref("");
const chat = new Chat({});

const handleSubmit = (e: Event) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    chat.sendMessage({ text: input.value });
    input.value = "";
};
</script>

<template>
    <div>
        <div v-for="(m, index) in chat.messages" :key="m.id ? m.id : index">
            {{ m.role === "user" ? "User: " : "AI: " }}
            <div
                v-for="(part, index) in m.parts"
                :key="`${m.id}-${part.type}-${index}`"
            >
                <div v-if="part.type === 'text'">{{ part.text }}</div>
            </div>
        </div>

        <form @submit="handleSubmit">
            <input v-model="input" placeholder="Say something..." />
        </form>
    </div>
</template>
```

export default function RootLayout({
  children,

### Integrate Laminar with @vercel/otel

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/05-observability/laminar.mdx

Configures Laminar to coexist with `@vercel/otel` for tracing. This setup ensures regular Next.js traces are sent via `@vercel/otel`, while AI SDK and LLM traces are sent via Laminar.

```javascript
import { registerOTel } from '@vercel/otel';

export async function register() {
  registerOTel('my-service-name');
  if (process.env.NEXT_RUNTIME === 'nodejs') {
    const { Laminar } = await import('@lmnr-ai/lmnr');
    // Make sure to initialize Laminar **after** `@registerOTel`
    Laminar.initialize({
      projectApiKey: process.env.LMNR_PROJECT_API_KEY,
    });
  }
}
```

import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';

const model = openai.completion('gpt-3.5-turbo-instruct');

### Create API Route for MCP Tools with AI SDK (TypeScript)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/01-next/73-mcp-tools.mdx

Sets up a Next.js API route to handle text generation using the AI SDK and Model Context Protocol (MCP). It demonstrates connecting to MCP servers via different transports (stdio, HTTP, SSE) and streaming responses. Requires installation of `@modelcontextprotocol/sdk`.

```ts
import { experimental_createMCPClient, streamText } from 'ai';
import { Experimental_StdioMCPTransport } from 'ai/mcp-stdio';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { StdioClientTransport } from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/client/stdio';
import { SSEClientTransport } from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/client/sse';
import { StreamableHTTPClientTransport } from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/client/streamableHttp';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { prompt }: { prompt: string } = await req.json();

  try {
    // Initialize an MCP client to connect to a `stdio` MCP server:
    const transport = new StdioClientTransport({
      command: 'node',
      args: ['src/stdio/dist/server.js'],
    });

    const stdioClient = await experimental_createMCPClient({
      transport,
    });

    // You can also connect to StreamableHTTP MCP servers
    const httpTransport = new StreamableHTTPClientTransport(
      new URL('http://localhost:3000/mcp'),
    );
    const httpClient = await experimental_createMCPClient({
      transport: httpTransport,
    });

    // Alternatively, you can connect to a Server-Sent Events (SSE) MCP server:
    const sseTransport = new SSEClientTransport(
      new URL('http://localhost:3000/sse'),
    );
    const sseClient = await experimental_createMCPClient({
      transport: sseTransport,
    });

    const toolSetOne = await stdioClient.tools();
    const toolSetTwo = await httpClient.tools();
    const toolSetThree = await sseClient.tools();
    const tools = {
      ...toolSetOne,
      ...toolSetTwo,
      ...toolSetThree, // note: this approach causes subsequent tool sets to override tools with the same name
    };

    const response = await streamText({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      tools,
      prompt,
      // When streaming, the client should be closed after the response is finished:
      onFinish: async () => {
        await stdioClient.close();
        await httpClient.close();
        await sseClient.close();
      },
      // Closing clients onError is optional
      // - Closing: Immediately frees resources, prevents hanging connections
      // - Not closing: Keeps connection open for retries
      onError: async error => {
        await stdioClient.close();
        await httpClient.close();
        await sseClient.close();
      },
    });

    return response.toDataStreamResponse();
  } catch (error) {
    return new Response('Internal Server Error', { status: 500 });
  }
}
```

### Custom Provider: Limit Models & Settings

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/03-ai-sdk-core/45-provider-management.mdx

Create a custom provider to restrict available models and apply specific settings, such as 'reasoningEffort', across different providers. This example limits models and configures OpenAI settings.

```ts
import { anthropic } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import {
  customProvider,
  defaultSettingsMiddleware,
  wrapLanguageModel,
} from 'ai';

export const myProvider = customProvider({
  languageModels: {
    'text-medium': anthropic('claude-3-5-sonnet-20240620'),
    'text-small': openai('gpt-4o-mini'),
    'reasoning-medium': wrapLanguageModel({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      middleware: defaultSettingsMiddleware({
        settings: {
          providerOptions: {
            openai: {
              reasoningEffort: 'high',
            },
          },
        },
      }),
    }),
    'reasoning-fast': wrapLanguageModel({
      model: openai('gpt-4o-mini'),
      middleware: defaultSettingsMiddleware({
        settings: {
          providerOptions: {
            openai: {
              reasoningEffort: 'high',
            },
          },
        },
      }),
    }),
  },
  embeddingModels: {
    embedding: openai.textEmbeddingModel('text-embedding-3-small'),
  },
  // no fallback provider
});
```

### Simulate UI Message Stream Responses in Next.js

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/03-ai-sdk-core/55-testing.mdx

This example demonstrates simulating UI Message Stream responses in a Next.js application using the 'ai' SDK. It configures a ReadableStream with initial and chunk delays, providing sample data chunks that mimic a streaming chat interface. This is useful for testing and debugging purposes.

```typescript
import { simulateReadableStream } from 'ai';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  return new Response(
    simulateReadableStream({
      initialDelayInMs: 1000, // Delay before the first chunk
      chunkDelayInMs: 300, // Delay between chunks
      chunks: [
        `data: {"type":"start","messageId":"msg-123"}\n\n`,
        `data: {"type":"text-start","id":"text-1"}\n\n`,
        `data: {"type":"text-delta","id":"text-1","delta":"This"}\n\n`,
        `data: {"type":"text-delta","id":"text-1","delta":" is an"}\n\n`,
        `data: {"type":"text-delta","id":"text-1","delta":" example."}\n\n`,
        `data: {"type":"text-end","id":"text-1"}\n\n`,
        `data: {"type":"finish"}\n\n`,
        `data: [DONE]\n\n`,
      ],
    }).pipeThrough(new TextEncoderStream()),
    {
      status: 200,
      headers: {
        'Content-Type': 'text/event-stream',
        'Cache-Control': 'no-cache',
        'Connection': 'keep-alive',
        'x-vercel-ai-ui-message-stream': 'v1',
      },
    },
  );
}
```

### Client-Side Chatbot with useChat Hook and Tool Calls

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/04-ai-sdk-ui/03-chatbot-tool-usage.mdx

This example showcases the `useChat` hook for building a client-side chatbot with real-time message streaming. It details how to handle client-side tool execution via the `onToolCall` callback and automatically send messages when tool results are available using `sendAutomaticallyWhen`. The code also illustrates rendering tool-specific message parts in the UI.

```tsx
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import {
  DefaultChatTransport,
  lastAssistantMessageIsCompleteWithToolCalls,
} from 'ai';
import { useState } from 'react';

export default function Chat() {
  const { messages, sendMessage, addToolResult } = useChat({
    transport: new DefaultChatTransport({
      api: '/api/chat',
    }),

    sendAutomaticallyWhen: lastAssistantMessageIsCompleteWithToolCalls,

    // run client-side tools that are automatically executed:
    async onToolCall({ toolCall }) {
      if (toolCall.toolName === 'getLocation') {
        const cities = ['New York', 'Los Angeles', 'Chicago', 'San Francisco'];

        // No await - avoids potential deadlocks
        addToolResult({
          tool: 'getLocation',
          toolCallId: toolCall.toolCallId,
          output: cities[Math.floor(Math.random() * cities.length)],
        });
      }
    },
  });
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');

  return (
    <>
      {messages?.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id}>
          <strong>{`${message.role}: `}</strong>
          {message.parts.map(part => {
            switch (part.type) {
              // render text parts as simple text:
              case 'text':
                return part.text;

              // for tool parts, use the typed tool part names:
              case 'tool-askForConfirmation': {
                const callId = part.toolCallId;

                switch (part.state) {
                  case 'input-streaming':
                    return (
                      <div key={callId}>Loading confirmation request...</div>
                    );
                  case 'input-available':
                    return (
                      <div key={callId}>
                        {part.input.message}
                        <div>
                          <button
                            onClick={() =>
                              addToolResult({
                                tool: 'askForConfirmation',
                                toolCallId: callId,
                                output: 'Yes, confirmed.',
                              })
                            }
                          >
                            Yes
                          </button>
                          <button
                            onClick={() =>
                              addToolResult({
                                tool: 'askForConfirmation',
                                toolCallId: callId,
                                output: 'No, denied',
                              })
                            }
                          >
                            No
                          </button>
                        </div>
                      </div>
                    );
                  case 'output-available':
                    return (
                      <div key={callId}>
                        Location access allowed: {part.output}
                      </div>
                    );
                  case 'output-error':
                    return <div key={callId}>Error: {part.errorText}</div>;
                }
                break;
              }

              case 'tool-getLocation': {
                const callId = part.toolCallId;

                switch (part.state) {
                  case 'input-streaming':
                    return (
                      <div key={callId}>Preparing location request...</div>
                    );
                  case 'input-available':
                    return <div key={callId}>Getting location...</div>;
                  case 'output-available':

```

### Implement Manual Agent Loop in TypeScript

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/05-node/55-manual-agent-loop.mdx

Demonstrates a complete manual agent loop in TypeScript, allowing full control over tool execution, message history updates, and loop termination. This example uses the AI SDK to stream responses and handle tool calls explicitly.

```ts
import {
  openai
} from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import {
  ModelMessage,
  streamText,
  tool
} from 'ai';
import 'dotenv/config';
import z from 'zod';

const getWeather = async ({ location }: { location: string }) => {
  return `The weather in ${location} is ${Math.floor(Math.random() * 100)} degrees.`;
};

const messages: ModelMessage[] = [
  {
    role: 'user',
    content: 'Get the weather in New York and San Francisco',
  },
];

async function main() {
  while (true) {
    const result = streamText({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      messages,
      tools: {
        getWeather: tool({
          description: 'Get the current weather in a given location',
          inputSchema: z.object({
            location: z.string(),
          }),
        }),
        // add more tools here, omitting the execute function so you handle it yourself
      },
    });

    // Stream the response (only necessary for providing updates to the user)
    for await (const chunk of result.fullStream) {
      if (chunk.type === 'text-delta') {
        process.stdout.write(chunk.text);
      }

      if (chunk.type === 'tool-call') {
        console.log('\nCalling tool:', chunk.toolName);
      }
    }

    // Add LLM generated messages to the message history
    const responseMessages = (await result.response).messages;
    messages.push(...responseMessages);

    const finishReason = await result.finishReason;

    if (finishReason === 'tool-calls') {
      const toolCalls = await result.toolCalls;

      // Handle all tool call execution here
      for (const toolCall of toolCalls) {
        if (toolCall.toolName === 'getWeather') {
          const toolOutput = await getWeather(toolCall.input);
          messages.push({
            role: 'tool',
            content: [
              {
                toolName: toolCall.toolName,
                toolCallId: toolCall.toolCallId,
                type: 'tool-result',
                output: { type: 'text', value: toolOutput }, // update depending on the tool's output format
              },
            ],
          });
        }
        // Handle other tool calls
      }
    } else {
      // Exit the loop when the model doesn't request to use any more tools
      console.log('\n\nFinal message history:');
      console.dir(messages, { depth: null });
      break;
    }
  }
}

main().catch(console.error);

```

### Create Resource Server Action with Embeddings

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/01-rag-chatbot.mdx

This updated Server Action creates a resource and then generates and stores embeddings for its content using a separate `generateEmbeddings` function and the database. It handles potential errors during the process.

```tsx
'use server';

import {
  NewResourceParams,
  insertResourceSchema,
  resources,
} from '@/lib/db/schema/resources';
import { db } from '../db';
import { generateEmbeddings } from '../ai/embedding';
import { embeddings as embeddingsTable } from '../db/schema/embeddings';

export const createResource = async (input: NewResourceParams) => {
  try {
    const { content } = insertResourceSchema.parse(input);

    const [resource] = await db
      .insert(resources)
      .values({ content })
      .returning();

    const embeddings = await generateEmbeddings(content);
    await db.insert(embeddingsTable).values(
      embeddings.map(embedding => ({
        resourceId: resource.id,
        ...embedding,
      })),
    );

    return 'Resource successfully created and embedded.';
  } catch (error) {
    return error instanceof Error && error.message.length > 0
      ? error.message
      : 'Error, please try again.';
  }
};
```

### Send Image URL in Messages

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-foundations/03-prompts.mdx

```ts
const result = await generateText({
  model: 'openai/gpt-4.1',
  messages: [
    {
      role: 'user',
      content: [
        { type: 'text', text: 'Describe the image in detail.' },
        {
          type: 'image',
          image:
            'https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/main/examples/ai-core/data/comic-cat.png?raw=true',
        },
      ],
    },
  ],
});
```

### Create Baseten Provider Instance

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/02-openai-compatible-providers/40-baseten.mdx

Create a custom provider instance for Baseten using the `createOpenAICompatible` function. This requires specifying the model's environment URL and setting the authorization header with your Baseten API key.

```ts
import { createOpenAICompatible } from '@ai-sdk/openai-compatible';

const BASETEN_MODEL_ID = '<model-id>'; // e.g. 5q3z8xcw
const BASETEN_MODEL_URL = `https://model-${BASETEN_MODEL_ID}.api.baseten.co/environments/production/sync/v1`;

const baseten = createOpenAICompatible({
  name: 'baseten',
  baseURL: BASETEN_MODEL_URL,
  headers: {
    Authorization: `Bearer ${process.env.BASETEN_API_KEY ?? ''}`,
  },
});
```

### AI-Powered SQL Query Generation Server Action

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/04-natural-language-postgres.mdx

Implements the `generateQuery` Server Action using the AI SDK's `generateObject` function. It leverages OpenAI's model to generate a SQL query based on user input, constrained to a Zod schema for structured output.

```typescript
/* ...other imports... */
import { generateObject } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

/* ...rest of the file... */

export const generateQuery = async (input: string) => {
  'use server';
  try {
    const result = await generateObject({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      system: `You are a SQL (postgres) ...`, // SYSTEM PROMPT AS ABOVE - OMITTED FOR BREVITY
      prompt: `Generate the query necessary to retrieve the data the user wants: ${input}`,
      schema: z.object({
        query: z.string(),
      }),
    });
    return result.object.query;
  } catch (e) {
    console.error(e);
    throw new Error('Failed to generate query');
  }
};
```

### Provide Custom Tracer

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/05-observability/signoz.mdx

Demonstrates how to provide a custom OpenTelemetry Tracer to the `generateText` function. This allows for integration with custom TracerProviders, enabling detailed telemetry collection for AI SDK operations. The example initializes a `NodeTracerProvider` and retrieves a tracer instance to be passed via the `experimental_telemetry` option.

```javascript
const tracerProvider = new NodeTracerProvider();
const result = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-4-turbo'),
  prompt: 'Write a short story about a cat.',
  experimental_telemetry: {
    isEnabled: true,
    tracer: tracerProvider.getTracer('ai'),
  },
});
```

### Generate Image with Replicate (Basic)

```typescript
import { replicate } from '@ai-sdk/replicate';

  model: replicate.image('black-forest-labs/flux-schnell'),
  prompt: 'The Loch Ness Monster getting a manicure',
  aspectRatio: '16:9',

### Define Tool with Output Schema using AI SDK

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/01-announcing-ai-sdk-5-beta/index.mdx

Demonstrates defining a tool with an input and output schema using the `tool` function from the 'ai' library. This enhances type inference and validation for tool execution.

```tsx
import { tool } from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const weatherTool = tool({
  description: 'Get weather information',
  inputSchema: z.object({
    city: z.string()
  }),
  outputSchema: z.object({
    temperature: z.number(),
    conditions: z.string()
  }),
  execute: async ({ city }) => ({
    temperature: 72,
    conditions: 'sunny'
  })
});
```

### Generate Object with ChromeAI

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/03-community-providers/04-chrome-ai.mdx

Use the `generateObject` function with the `chromeai` provider and a Zod schema to generate structured JSON output. This example demonstrates generating a lasagna recipe.

```javascript
import { generateObject } from 'ai';
import { chromeai } from 'chrome-ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { object } = await generateObject({
  model: chromeai('text'),
  schema: z.object({
    recipe: z.object({
      name: z.string(),
      ingredients: z.array(
        z.object({
          name: z.string(),
          amount: z.string(),
        }),
      ),
      steps: z.array(z.string()),
    }),
  }),
  prompt: 'Generate a lasagna recipe.',
});

console.log(object); // { recipe: {...} }
```

### TextStreamPart API Documentation

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/01-ai-sdk-core/02-stream-text.mdx

Defines the structure for various parts of a text stream from an AI model. This includes information about tool execution returns, the start of a processing step, and the completion of a step, along with associated metadata and usage details.

```APIDOC
TextStreamPart:
  # Represents the return type of a tool execution.
  # This part contains the result after a tool has completed its execution.
  # The specific type of the result is inferred from the tool's execute function return type.
  - type: 'tool execution return type'
    parameters:
      - name: 'name'
        type: 'string'
        description: 'The name of the tool execution result.'
      - name: 'type'
        type: 'string'
        description: 'The type of the tool execution return, e.g., "tool execution return type".'
      - name: 'description'
        type: 'string'
        description: 'A description of the tool execution result.'

  # Represents the initiation of a new step in the AI processing stream.
  # This part includes metadata about the request sent to the language model provider.
  - type: 'start-step'
    parameters:
      - name: 'type'
        type: "'start-step'"
        description: 'Indicates the start of a new step in the stream.'
      - name: 'request'
        type: 'LanguageModelRequestMetadata'
        description: 'Information about the request that was sent to the language model provider.'
        properties:
          - type: 'LanguageModelRequestMetadata'
            parameters:
              - name: 'body'
                type: 'string'
                description: 'Raw request HTTP body that was sent to the provider API as a string.'
      - name: 'warnings'
        type: 'CallWarning[]'
        description: 'Warnings from the model provider (e.g. unsupported settings).'

  # Represents the completion of a step in the AI processing stream.
  # This part contains response metadata, usage statistics, and the reason for finishing.
  - type: 'finish-step'
    parameters:
      - name: 'type'
        type: "'finish-step'"
        description: 'Indicates the end of the current step in the stream.'
      - name: 'response'
        type: 'LanguageModelResponseMetadata'
        description: 'Response metadata from the language model provider.'
        properties:
          - type: 'LanguageModelResponseMetadata'
            parameters:
              - name: 'id'
                type: 'string'
                description: 'The response identifier. The AI SDK uses the ID from the provider response when available, and generates an ID otherwise.'
              - name: 'model'
                type: 'string'
                description: 'The model that was used to generate the response. The AI SDK uses the response model from the provider response when available, and the model from the function call otherwise.'
              - name: 'timestamp'
                type: 'Date'
                description: 'The timestamp of the response. The AI SDK uses the response timestamp from the provider response when available, and creates a timestamp otherwise.'
              - name: 'headers'
                type: 'Record<string, string>'
                description: 'The response headers.'
      - name: 'usage'
        type: 'LanguageModelUsage'
        description: 'The token usage of the generated text.'
        properties:
          - type: 'LanguageModelUsage'
            parameters:
              - name: 'inputTokens'
                type: 'number'
                description: 'The total number of tokens in the prompt.'
              - name: 'outputTokens'
                type: 'number'
                description: 'The total number of tokens in the completion.'
              - name: 'totalTokens'
                type: 'number'
                description: 'The total number of tokens generated.'
      - name: 'finishReason'
        type: "'stop' | 'length' | 'content-filter' | 'tool-calls' | 'error' | 'other' | 'unknown'"
        description: 'The reason the model finished generating the text.'
      - name: 'providerMetadata'
        type: 'ProviderMetadata | undefined'
        isOptional: true
        description: 'Optional metadata from the provider. The outer key is the provider name. The inner values are the metadata. Details depend on the provider.'

```

### AI SDK UI Functions Compatibility

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/01-navigating-the-library.mdx

Details the compatibility of AI SDK UI functions across React, Svelte, and Vue.js frameworks. Lists functions like useChat, useCompletion, and useObject, indicating their support status. Contributions for missing framework support are encouraged.

```APIDOC
AI SDK UI Functions:

useChat:
  Description: Enables chat functionality.
  Framework Support:
    React: Supported
    Svelte: Supported
    Vue.js: Supported

useChat (tool calling):
  Description: Enables chat functionality with tool calling capabilities.
  Framework Support:
    React: Supported
    Svelte: Supported
    Vue.js: Not Supported

useCompletion:
  Description: Enables completion functionality.
  Framework Support:
    React: Supported
    Svelte: Supported
    Vue.js: Supported

useObject:
  Description: Enables object retrieval functionality.
  Framework Support:
    React: Supported
    Svelte: Not Supported
    Vue.js: Not Supported
```

--------------------------------

### Prepare Step Function Return Options

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/08-migration-guides/26-migration-guide-5-0.mdx

Details the possible return values for the `prepareStep` function, which can dynamically configure aspects of a generation step. These include selecting a different model, specifying active tools, defining tool choice strategies, setting system messages, or using default settings.

```tsx
The `prepareStep` function receives `{ steps, stepNumber, model }` and can return:

- `model`: Different model for this step
- `activeTools`: Which tools to make available
- `toolChoice`: Tool selection strategy
- `system`: System message for this step
- `undefined`: Use default settings
```

### Stream Text Response with Hono

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/15-api-servers/30-hono.mdx

Shows how to extract a plain text stream from the AI SDK result and pipe it directly to the Hono response. This is useful for streaming raw text content without additional formatting.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { serve } from '@hono/node-server';
import { streamText } from 'ai';
import { Hono } from 'hono';
import { stream } from 'hono/streaming';

const app = new Hono();

app.post('/', async c => {
  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    prompt: 'Invent a new holiday and describe its traditions.',
  });

  c.header('Content-Type', 'text/plain; charset=utf-8');

  return stream(c, stream => stream.pipe(result.textStream));
});

serve({ fetch: app.fetch, port: 8080 });

```

### AI SDK generateObject Function

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/04-natural-language-postgres.mdx

The `generateObject` function from the AI SDK facilitates structured output from language models. It takes a model, system prompt, user prompt, and a Zod schema to constrain the output to a specific format.

```APIDOC
generateObject(options: {
  model: Model;
  system?: string;
  prompt: string;
  schema: z.ZodSchema<T>;
  temperature?: number;
  maxTokens?: number;
  // ... other options
}): Promise<{ object: T; text: string }>;

// Parameters:
// - model: The AI model to use (e.g., openai('gpt-4o')).
// - system: An optional system prompt to guide the model's behavior.
// - prompt: The user's natural language query or instruction.
// - schema: A Zod schema defining the expected structure of the model's output.
// - temperature: Controls randomness; lower values make output more deterministic.
// - maxTokens: The maximum number of tokens to generate.

// Returns:
// - An object containing:
//   - object: The parsed output conforming to the provided Zod schema.
//   - text: The raw text output from the model.

// Example Usage:
// const result = await generateObject({
//   model: openai('gpt-4o'),
//   system: 'You are a helpful assistant.',
//   prompt: 'Tell me a joke.',
//   schema: z.object({ joke: z.string() }),
// });
// console.log(result.object.joke);
```

--------------------------------

### APIDOC: Prepare Step Configuration

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/07-reference/01-ai-sdk-core/02-stream-text.mdx

Defines functions for configuring AI steps. `PrepareStepFunction` allows modification of model, tool choices, active tools, system prompt, and input messages for a step. `PrepareStepResult` specifies the return structure to modify these settings.

```APIDOC
PrepareStepFunction<TOOLS>:
  Parameters:
    options: object
      type: PrepareStepOptions
      description: The options for the step.
      parameters:
        steps: Array<StepResult<TOOLS>>
          description: The steps that have been executed so far.
        stepNumber: number
          description: The number of the step that is being executed.
        model: LanguageModel
          description: The model that is being used.
        messages: Array<ModelMessage>
          description: The messages that will be sent to the model for the current step.

PrepareStepResult<TOOLS>:
  description: Return value that can modify settings for the current step.
  parameters:
    model?: LanguageModel
      description: Change the model for this step.
    toolChoice?: ToolChoice<TOOLS>
      description: Change the tool choice strategy for this step.
    activeTools?: Array<keyof TOOLS>
      description: Change which tools are active for this step.
    system?: string
      description: Change the system prompt for this step.
    messages?: Array<ModelMessage>
      description: Modify the input messages for this step.
```

        { type: 'text', text: 'Describe the image in detail.' },
