### Update UI for Weather Tool Display

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/07-expo.mdx

This code snippet updates the `app/(tabs)/index.tsx` file to render weather tool invocations. It modifies the message mapping to display `tool-weather` parts as JSON, alongside standard text parts. Dependencies include `@ai-sdk/react` and `expo/fetch`.

```tsx
import { generateAPIUrl } from '@/utils';
import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { DefaultChatTransport } from 'ai';
import { fetch as expoFetch } from 'expo/fetch';
import { useState } from 'react';
import { View, TextInput, ScrollView, Text, SafeAreaView } from 'react-native';

export default function App() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, error, sendMessage } = useChat({
    transport: new DefaultChatTransport({
      fetch: expoFetch as unknown as typeof globalThis.fetch,
      api: generateAPIUrl('/api/chat'),
    }),
    onError: error => console.error(error, 'ERROR'),
  });

  if (error) return <Text>{error.message}</Text>;

  return (
    <SafeAreaView style={{ height: '100%' }}>
      <View
        style={{
          height: '95%',
          display: 'flex',
          flexDirection: 'column',
          paddingHorizontal: 8,
        }}
      >
        <ScrollView style={{ flex: 1 }}>
          {messages.map(m => (
            <View key={m.id} style={{ marginVertical: 8 }}>
              <View>
                <Text style={{ fontWeight: 700 }}>{m.role}</Text>
                {m.parts.map((part, i) => {
                  switch (part.type) {
                    case 'text':
                      return <Text key={`${m.id}-${i}`}>{part.text}</Text>;
                    case 'tool-weather':
                      return (
                        <Text key={`${m.id}-${i}`}>
                          {JSON.stringify(part, null, 2)}
                        </Text>
                      );
                  }
                })}
              </View>
            </View>
          ))}
        </ScrollView>

        <View style={{ marginTop: 8 }}>
          <TextInput
            style={{ backgroundColor: 'white', padding: 8 }}
            placeholder="Say something..."
            value={input}
            onChange={e => setInput(e.nativeEvent.text)}
            onSubmitEditing={e => {
              e.preventDefault();
              sendMessage({ text: input });
              setInput('');
            }}
            autoFocus={true}
          />
        </View>
      </View>
    </SafeAreaView>
  );
}
```

### RAG Middleware (TypeScript)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/03-ai-sdk-core/40-middleware.mdx

Shows how to integrate Retrieval Augmented Generation (RAG) as middleware. This example modifies the prompt by adding relevant context fetched from external sources (simulated by helper functions) to the last user message.

```typescript
import type { LanguageModelV2Middleware } from '@ai-sdk/provider';

export const yourRagMiddleware: LanguageModelV2Middleware = {
  transformParams: async ({ params }) => {
    const lastUserMessageText = getLastUserMessageText({
      prompt: params.prompt,
    });

    if (lastUserMessageText == null) {
      return params; // do not use RAG (send unmodified parameters)
    }

    const instruction =
      'Use the following information to answer the question:\n' +
      findSources({ text: lastUserMessageText })
        .map(chunk => JSON.stringify(chunk))
        .join('\n');

    return addToLastUserMessage({ params, text: instruction });
  },
};

```

### Add Weather Tool to AI Chat Route Handler (TypeScript)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/02-nextjs-app-router.mdx

This snippet demonstrates how to define a server-side route handler for an AI chatbot. It integrates a 'weather' tool using `@ai-sdk` and `zod` for input schema validation, allowing the AI to fetch simulated weather data based on user location. The tool's execution logic runs on the server.

```tsx
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { streamText, UIMessage, convertToModelMessages, tool } from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

export const maxDuration = 30;

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
    tools: {
      weather: tool({
        description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ location }) => {
          const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
          return {
            location,
            temperature,
          };
        },
      }),
    },
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### V2 Prompt Format - Prompt Parts

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/03-community-providers/01-custom-providers.mdx

Describes the building blocks for messages in the Vercel AI SDK's V2 prompt structure. Covers text, reasoning, file, tool call, and tool result parts with their respective properties.

```APIDOC
LanguageModelV2Prompt Parts:

- Text Part:
  - Type: 'text'
  - Properties:
    - text: string (plain text content)
    - providerOptions?: SharedV2ProviderOptions (optional provider-specific options)
  - Description: The most basic prompt part, containing plain text.
  - Example:
    ```ts
    interface LanguageModelV2TextPart {
      type: 'text';
      text: string;
      providerOptions?: SharedV2ProviderOptions;
    }
    ```

- Reasoning Part:
  - Type: 'reasoning'
  - Properties:
    - text: string (reasoning process content)
    - providerOptions?: SharedV2ProviderOptions (optional provider-specific options)
  - Description: Used in assistant messages to capture the model's reasoning process.
  - Example:
    ```ts
    interface LanguageModelV2ReasoningPart {
      type: 'reasoning';
      text: string;
      providerOptions?: SharedV2ProviderOptions;
    }
    ```

- File Part:
  - Type: 'file'
  - Properties:
    - filename?: string (optional file name)
    - data: LanguageModelV2DataContent (binary data, base64 string, or URL)
    - mediaType: string (MIME type of the file)
    - providerOptions?: SharedV2ProviderOptions (optional provider-specific options)
  - Description: Enables multimodal inputs by including files in prompts.
  - Example:
    ```ts
    interface LanguageModelV2FilePart {
      type: 'file';
      filename?: string;
      data: LanguageModelV2DataContent;
      mediaType: string;
      providerOptions?: SharedV2ProviderOptions;
    }
    ```
  - Data Field Flexibility:
    - Uint8Array: Direct binary data.
    - string: Base64-encoded data.
    - URL: Reference to external content (provider dependent).

- Tool Call Part:
  - Type: 'tool-call'
  - Properties:
    - toolCallId: string (unique identifier for the tool call)
    - toolName: string (name of the tool being called)
    - args: unknown (arguments for the tool call)
    - providerOptions?: SharedV2ProviderOptions (optional provider-specific options)
  - Description: Represents tool calls made by the assistant.
  - Example:
    ```ts
    interface LanguageModelV2ToolCallPart {
      type: 'tool-call';
      toolCallId: string;
      toolName: string;
      args: unknown;
      providerOptions?: SharedV2ProviderOptions;
    }
    ```

- Tool Result Part:
  - Type: 'tool-result'
  - Properties:
    - toolCallId: string (ID of the tool call being reported)
    - toolName: string (name of the tool that was executed)
    - result: unknown (the result of the tool execution)
    - isError?: boolean (flag indicating if the tool execution resulted in an error)
    - content?: Array<{ type: 'text' | 'image'; text?: string; data?: string; mediaType?: string; }>
    - providerOptions?: SharedV2ProviderOptions (optional provider-specific options)
  - Description: Contains the results of executed tool calls, optionally including rich content like images.
  - Example:
    ```ts
    interface LanguageModelV2ToolResultPart {
      type: 'tool-result';
      toolCallId: string;
      toolName: string;
      result: unknown;
      isError?: boolean;
      content?: Array<{ type: 'text' | 'image'; text?: string; data?: string; mediaType?: string; }>;
      providerOptions?: SharedV2ProviderOptions;
    }
    ```
```

--------------------------------

### Custom Provider: Override Settings

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/03-ai-sdk-core/45-provider-management.mdx

Create a custom provider to override default model settings or provide model name aliases with pre-configured options. This example demonstrates setting 'reasoningEffort' for OpenAI models.

```ts
import { openai as originalOpenAI } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import {
  customProvider,
  defaultSettingsMiddleware,
  wrapLanguageModel,
} from 'ai';

// custom provider with different provider options:
export const openai = customProvider({
  languageModels: {
    // replacement model with custom provider options:
    'gpt-4o': wrapLanguageModel({
      model: originalOpenAI('gpt-4o'),
      middleware: defaultSettingsMiddleware({
        settings: {
          providerOptions: {
            openai: {
              reasoningEffort: 'high',
            },
          },
        },
      }),
    }),
    // alias model with custom provider options:
    'gpt-4o-mini-high-reasoning': wrapLanguageModel({
      model: originalOpenAI('gpt-4o-mini'),
      middleware: defaultSettingsMiddleware({
        settings: {
          providerOptions: {
            openai: {
              reasoningEffort: 'high',
            },
          },
        },
      }),
    }),
  },
  fallbackProvider: originalOpenAI,
});
```

### Combining Hook and Request Level Options

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/09-troubleshooting/11-use-chat-custom-request-options.mdx

Explains how request-level options override or add to hook-level configurations, demonstrating precedence with examples for headers and body fields.

```tsx
// Hook-level default configuration
const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat({
  transport: new DefaultChatTransport({
    api: '/api/chat',
    headers: {
      'X-API-Version': 'v1',
    },
    body: {
      model: 'gpt-4o',
    },
  }),
});

// Override or add options per request
sendMessage(
  { text: input },
  {
    headers: {
      'X-API-Version': 'v2', // This overrides the hook-level header
      'X-Request-ID': '123', // This is added
    },
    body: {
      model: 'gpt-4o-mini', // This overrides the hook-level body field
      temperature: 0.5, // This is added
    },
  },
);
```

### Slackbot Event Handler API Route

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/03-slackbot.mdx

Handles incoming POST requests from Slack for event callbacks. It verifies requests, identifies event types (url_verification, app_mention, assistant_thread_started, message), and dispatches them to appropriate handler functions using Vercel's waitUntil for background processing.

```typescript
import type { SlackEvent } from '@slack/web-api';
import {
  assistantThreadMessage,
  handleNewAssistantMessage,
} from '../lib/handle-messages';
import { waitUntil } from '@vercel/functions';
import { handleNewAppMention } from '../lib/handle-app-mention';
import { verifyRequest, getBotId } from '../lib/slack-utils';

export async function POST(request: Request) {
  const rawBody = await request.text();
  const payload = JSON.parse(rawBody);
  const requestType = payload.type as 'url_verification' | 'event_callback';

  // See https://api.slack.com/events/url_verification
  if (requestType === 'url_verification') {
    return new Response(payload.challenge, { status: 200 });
  }

  await verifyRequest({ requestType, request, rawBody });

  try {
    const botUserId = await getBotId();

    const event = payload.event as SlackEvent;

    if (event.type === 'app_mention') {
      waitUntil(handleNewAppMention(event, botUserId));
    }

    if (event.type === 'assistant_thread_started') {
      waitUntil(assistantThreadMessage(event));
    }

    if (
      event.type === 'message' &&
      !event.subtype &&
      event.channel_type === 'im' &&
      !event.bot_id &&
      !event.bot_profile &&
      event.bot_id !== botUserId
    ) {
      waitUntil(handleNewAssistantMessage(event, botUserId));
    }

    return new Response('Success!', { status: 200 });
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Error generating response', error);
    return new Response('Error generating response', { status: 500 });
  }
}
```

--------------------------------

### Secure Server Action with Token Authentication

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/05-ai-sdk-rsc/09-authentication.mdx

This example shows how to protect a Next.js Server Action by verifying a user's authentication token stored in cookies. It demonstrates returning an error for unauthenticated requests and updating a streamable UI with skeleton and final content upon successful authentication.

```tsx
'use server';

import { cookies } from 'next/headers';
import { createStreamableUI } from '@ai-sdk/rsc';
import { validateToken } from '../utils/auth';

export const getWeather = async () => {
  const token = cookies().get('token');

  if (!token || !validateToken(token)) {
    return {
      error: 'This action requires authentication',
    };
  }
  const streamableDisplay = createStreamableUI(null);

  streamableDisplay.update(<Skeleton />);
  streamableDisplay.done(<Weather />);

  return {
    display: streamableDisplay.value,
  };
}
```

### Implement GET Handler for Resumable Streams

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/04-ai-sdk-ui/03-chatbot-message-persistence.mdx

Provides the server-side implementation for the `/api/chat` GET endpoint. This handler reads the `chatId` from query parameters, loads associated stream IDs, identifies the most recent one, and returns it via `streamContext.resumableStream()` to resume the stream. It includes error handling for missing IDs and falls back to an empty stream if necessary.

```ts
import { loadStreams } from '@util/chat-store';
import { createUIMessageStream, JsonToSseTransformStream } from 'ai';
import { after } from 'next/server';
import { createResumableStreamContext } from 'resumable-stream';

export async function GET(request: Request) {
  const streamContext = createResumableStreamContext({
    waitUntil: after,
  });

  const { searchParams } = new URL(request.url);
  const chatId = searchParams.get('chatId');

  if (!chatId) {
    return new Response('id is required', { status: 400 });
  }

  const streamIds = await loadStreams(chatId);

  if (!streamIds.length) {
    return new Response('No streams found', { status: 404 });
  }

  const recentStreamId = streamIds.at(-1);

  if (!recentStreamId) {
    return new Response('No recent stream found', { status: 404 });
  }

  const emptyDataStream = createUIMessageStream({
    execute: () => {},
  });

  return new Response(
    await streamContext.resumableStream(recentStreamId, () =>
      emptyDataStream.pipeThrough(new JsonToSseTransformStream()),
    ),
  );
}
```

### Build Chatbot UI with AI SDK UI and Next.js (Client Component)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/23-o1.mdx

Example of a client-side React component using the `useChat` hook from AI SDK UI to manage chat messages, user input, and form submission. It displays messages and provides an input field for user interaction.

```tsx
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';

export default function Page() {
  const { messages, input, handleInputChange, handleSubmit, error } = useChat();

  return (
    <>
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id}>
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.content}
        </div>
      ))}
      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit}>
        <input name="prompt" value={input} onChange={handleInputChange} />
        <button type="submit">Submit</button>
      </form>
    </>
  );
}

```

### Implicit Caching for Cost Savings

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/15-google-generative-ai.mdx

Illustrates how to leverage implicit caching by structuring prompts with consistent prefixes to achieve token cost savings. It provides examples of prompt design for maximizing cache hits and checking cached token usage in provider metadata.

```typescript
import { google } from '@ai-sdk/google';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

// Structure prompts with consistent content at the beginning
const baseContext =
  'You are a cooking assistant with expertise in Italian cuisine. Here are 1000 lasagna recipes for reference...';

const { text: veggieLasagna } = await generateText({
  model: google('gemini-2.5-pro'),
  prompt: `${baseContext}\n\nWrite a vegetarian lasagna recipe for 4 people.`, // Minimum token requirements apply for cache hits
});

// Second request with same prefix - eligible for cache hit
const { text: meatLasagna, providerMetadata } = await generateText({
  model: google('gemini-2.5-pro'),
  prompt: `${baseContext}\n\nWrite a meat lasagna recipe for 12 people.`, // Minimum token requirements apply for cache hits
});

// Check cached token count in usage metadata
console.log('Cached tokens:', providerMetadata.google?.usageMetadata);
// e.g.
// {
//   groundingMetadata: null,
//   safetyRatings: null,
//   usageMetadata: {
//     cachedContentTokenCount: 2027,
//     thoughtsTokenCount: 702,
//     promptTokenCount: 2152,
//     candidatesTokenCount: 710,
//     totalTokenCount: 3564
//   }
// }
```

### Remove `init` option from `pipeDataStreamToResponse` (AI SDK 3.4 vs 4.0)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/08-migration-guides/29-migration-guide-4-0.mdx

The `init` option, previously used for setting headers in `pipeDataStreamToResponse` and `toDataStreamResponse`, has been removed. Users should now directly place these options within the main `options` object.

```typescript
const result = await streamText({
  // ...
});

result.toUIMessageStreamResponse(response, {
  init: {
    headers: {
      'X-Custom-Header': 'value',
    },
  },
  // ...
});
```

```typescript
const result = streamText({
  // ...
});

result.toUIMessageStreamResponse(response, {
  headers: {
    'X-Custom-Header': 'value',
  },
  // ...
});
```

### Stream UI Function Usage

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/05-ai-sdk-rsc/02-streaming-react-components.mdx

Demonstrates calling the `streamUI` function with an OpenAI model, a prompt, a text handler for plain text responses, and an empty tools object. This example shows how to stream the model's response as a React component.

```tsx
const result = await streamUI({
  model: openai('gpt-4o'),
  prompt: 'Get the weather for San Francisco',
  text: ({ content }) => <div>{content}</div>,
  tools: {},
});
```

### Implement Chat UI with useChat Hook

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/02-nextjs-app-router.mdx

This React component utilizes the useChat hook from the AI SDK to manage chat messages and user input. It displays messages from both the user and AI, and provides an input field for sending new messages. The component handles form submission to send user input to the chat API and clears the input field upon sending.

```tsx
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { useState } from 'react';

export default function Chat() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat();
  return (
    <div className="flex flex-col w-full max-w-md py-24 mx-auto stretch">
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id} className="whitespace-pre-wrap">
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.parts.map((part, i) => {
            switch (part.type) {
              case 'text':
                return <div key={`${message.id}-${i}`}>{part.text}</div>;
            }
          })}
        </div>
      ))}

      <form
        onSubmit={e => {
          e.preventDefault();
          sendMessage({ text: input });
          setInput('');
        }}
      >
        <input
          className="fixed dark:bg-zinc-900 bottom-0 w-full max-w-md p-2 mb-8 border border-zinc-300 dark:border-zinc-800 rounded shadow-xl"
          value={input}
          placeholder="Say something..."
          onChange={e => setInput(e.currentTarget.value)}
        />
      </form>
    </div>
  );
}
```

### Guardrails Middleware (TypeScript)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/03-ai-sdk-core/40-middleware.mdx

Demonstrates using guardrails as middleware to ensure generated text is safe and appropriate. This example shows a filtering approach to replace sensitive content, like 'badword', with a placeholder.

```typescript
import type { LanguageModelV2Middleware } from '@ai-sdk/provider';

export const yourGuardrailMiddleware: LanguageModelV2Middleware = {
  wrapGenerate: async ({ doGenerate }) => {
    const { text, ...rest } = await doGenerate();

    // filtering approach, e.g. for PII or other sensitive information:
    const cleanedText = text?.replace(/badword/g, '<REDACTED>');

    return { text: cleanedText, ...rest };
  },

  // here you would implement the guardrail logic for streaming
  // Note: streaming guardrails are difficult to implement, because
  // you do not know the full content of the stream until it's finished.
};

```

### Enable OpenAI Reasoning Summaries (Streaming)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/03-openai.mdx

Shows how to enable detailed reasoning summaries for streaming text generation with OpenAI models like `o4-mini`. It demonstrates accessing the `reasoning` part from the stream output by setting `reasoningSummary: 'detailed'` or `'auto'`.

```ts
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { streamText } from 'ai';

const result = streamText({
  model: openai.responses('o4-mini'),
  prompt: 'Tell me about the Mission burrito debate in San Francisco.',
  providerOptions: {
    openai: {
      reasoningSummary: 'detailed', // 'auto' for condensed or 'detailed' for comprehensive
    },
  },
});

for await (const part of result.fullStream) {
  if (part.type === 'reasoning') {
    console.log(`Reasoning: ${part.textDelta}`);
  } else if (part.type === 'text-delta') {
    process.stdout.write(part.textDelta);
  }
}
```

### Send Binary Image in Messages

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-foundations/03-prompts.mdx

Shows how to include an image part in a user message using binary data, specifically a Node.js `Buffer`. The `image` property accepts `Buffer`, `ArrayBuffer`, `Uint8Array`, or `URL` objects. This example uses `fs.readFileSync` to load an image file.

```ts
const result = await generateText({
  model,
  messages: [
    {
      role: 'user',
      content: [
        { type: 'text', text: 'Describe the image in detail.' },
        {
          type: 'image',
          image: fs.readFileSync('./data/comic-cat.png'),
        },
      ],
    },
  ],
});
```

### Generate Image with Replicate

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/packages/replicate/README.md

Demonstrates basic image generation using the Replicate provider with the AI SDK. It shows how to import the necessary functions, call `generateImage` with a Replicate model, and save the resulting image.

```typescript
import { replicate } from '@ai-sdk/replicate';
import { experimental_generateImage as generateImage } from 'ai';

const { image } = await generateImage({
  model: replicate.image('black-forest-labs/flux-schnell'),
  prompt: 'The Loch Ness Monster getting a manicure',
});

const filename = `image-${Date.now()}.png`;
fs.writeFileSync(filename, image.uint8Array);
console.log(`Image saved to ${filename}`);
```

### Generate Image with Image Reference (TypeScript)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/80-luma.mdx

Use up to 4 reference images to guide your generation. The `weight` parameter (0-1) controls the influence of reference images on the output. This is useful for creating variations or visualizing complex concepts.

```typescript
await generateImage({
  model: luma.image('photon-1'),
  prompt: 'A salamander at dusk in a forest pond, in the style of ukiyo-e',
  providerOptions: {
    luma: {
      image_ref: [
        {
          url: 'https://example.com/reference.jpg',
          weight: 0.85,
        },
      ],
    },
  },
});
```

### Generate Text with Cloudflare Workers AI

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/03-community-providers/11-cloudflare-workers-ai.mdx

Example of using the `generateText` function from the AI SDK with a Cloudflare Workers AI model. It takes a model instance and a prompt to generate text output.

```typescript
import { createWorkersAI } from 'workers-ai-provider';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

type Env = {
  AI: Ai;
};

export default {
  async fetch(_: Request, env: Env) {
    const workersai = createWorkersAI({ binding: env.AI });
    const result = await generateText({
      model: workersai('@cf/meta/llama-2-7b-chat-int8'),
      prompt: 'Write a 50-word essay about hello world.',
    });

    return new Response(result.text);
  },
};
```

--------------------------------

### AI SDK Streaming: Tool Input Handling (v5)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/08-migration-guides/26-migration-guide-5-0.mdx

Demonstrates the new streaming pattern for tool inputs in AI SDK v5. Tool inputs are now streamed using `tool-input-start`, `tool-input-delta`, and `tool-input-end` events, allowing for real-time updates of JSON inputs before the final `tool-call`.

```tsx
for await (const chunk of result.fullStream) {
  switch (chunk.type) {
    case 'tool-input-start': {
      console.log(`Starting tool input for ${chunk.toolName}: ${chunk.id}`);
      break;
    }
    case 'tool-input-delta': {
      // Stream the JSON input as it's being generated
      process.stdout.write(chunk.delta);
      break;
    }
    case 'tool-input-end': {
      console.log(`Completed tool input: ${chunk.id}`);
      break;
    }
    case 'tool-call': {
      // Final tool call with complete input
      console.log('Tool call:', chunk.toolName, chunk.input);
      break;
    }
  }
}
```

--------------------------------

### Update Frontend with AI Tool Rendering

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/02-nextjs-app-router.mdx

Updates the `app/page.tsx` file to handle and display AI tool outputs, specifically `tool-weather` and `tool-convertFahrenheitToCelsius` parts. It uses the `@ai-sdk/react` hook to manage chat messages and render tool calls within a React component, showing the model's interaction with external tools.

```tsx
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { useState } from 'react';

export default function Chat() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat();
  return (
    <div className="flex flex-col w-full max-w-md py-24 mx-auto stretch">
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id} className="whitespace-pre-wrap">
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.parts.map((part, i) => {
            switch (part.type) {
              case 'text':
                return <div key={`${message.id}-${i}`}>{part.text}</div>;
              case 'tool-weather':
              case 'tool-convertFahrenheitToCelsius':
                return (
                  <pre key={`${message.id}-${i}`}>
                    {JSON.stringify(part, null, 2)}
                  </pre>
                );
            }
          })}
        </div>
      ))}

      <form
        onSubmit={e => {
          e.preventDefault();
          sendMessage({ text: input });
          setInput('');
        }}
      >
        <input
          className="fixed dark:bg-zinc-900 bottom-0 w-full max-w-md p-2 mb-8 border border-zinc-300 dark:border-zinc-800 rounded shadow-xl"
          value={input}
          placeholder="Say something..."
          onChange={e => setInput(e.currentTarget.value)}
        />
      </form>
    </div>
  );
}

```

### Integrate Weather Tool in TypeScript Chatbot

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/06-nodejs.mdx

This snippet shows how to add a weather tool to an AI chatbot. It defines a tool with a descriptive string and a Zod schema for its input, including a location parameter. The tool's execution logic simulates fetching weather data, returning a random temperature. The code streams the AI's response and logs any tool calls or results.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { ModelMessage, streamText, tool } from 'ai';
import 'dotenv/config';
import { z } from 'zod';
import * as readline from 'node:readline/promises';

const terminal = readline.createInterface({
  input: process.stdin,
  output: process.stdout,
});

const messages: ModelMessage[] = [];

async function main() {
  while (true) {
    const userInput = await terminal.question('You: ');

    messages.push({ role: 'user', content: userInput });

    const result = streamText({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      messages,
      tools: {
        weather: tool({
          description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
          inputSchema: z.object({
            location: z
              .string()
              .describe('The location to get the weather for'),
          }),
          execute: async ({ location }) => {
            const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
            return {
              location,
              temperature,
            };
          },
        }),
      },
    });

    let fullResponse = '';
    process.stdout.write('\nAssistant: ');
    for await (const delta of result.textStream) {
      fullResponse += delta;
      process.stdout.write(delta);
    }
    process.stdout.write('\n\n');

    console.log(await result.toolCalls);
    console.log(await result.toolResults);
    messages.push({ role: 'assistant', content: fullResponse });
  }
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

### Enable Live Search with xAI Models

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/providers/01-ai-sdk-providers/01-xai.mdx

Enable Live Search functionality for xAI models by configuring 'searchParameters' within 'providerOptions'. This allows models to query real-time data and include citations.

```typescript
import { xai } from '@ai-sdk/xai';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text, sources } = await generateText({
  model: xai('grok-3-latest'),
  prompt: 'What are the latest developments in AI?',
  providerOptions: {
    xai: {
      searchParameters: {
        mode: 'auto', // 'auto', 'on', or 'off'
        returnCitations: true,
        maxSearchResults: 5,
      },
    },
  },
});

console.log(text);
console.log('Sources:', sources);
```

### Create AI Chat Tool with Information Retrieval in TypeScript

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/01-rag-chatbot.mdx

This snippet shows how to integrate a knowledge retrieval tool into an AI chat application using the 'ai' SDK. It defines two tools: 'addResource' for adding content and 'getInformation' for querying the knowledge base, leveraging Zod for schema validation and custom logic for execution.

```ts
import { createResource } from '@/lib/actions/resources';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import {
  convertToModelMessages,
  streamText,
  tool,
  UIMessage,
  stepCountIs,
} from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';
import { findRelevantContent } from '@/lib/ai/embedding';

// Allow streaming responses up to 30 seconds
export const maxDuration = 30;

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
    stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
    system: `You are a helpful assistant. Check your knowledge base before answering any questions.
    Only respond to questions using information from tool calls.
    if no relevant information is found in the tool calls, respond, "Sorry, I don't know."
    `,
    tools: {
      addResource: tool({
        description: `add a resource to your knowledge base.
          If the user provides a random piece of knowledge unprompted, use this tool without asking for confirmation.`, 
        inputSchema: z.object({
          content: z
            .string()
            .describe('the content or resource to add to the knowledge base'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ content }) => createResource({ content }),
      }),
      getInformation: tool({
        description: `get information from your knowledge base to answer questions.`, 
        inputSchema: z.object({
          question: z.string().describe('the users question'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ question }) => findRelevantContent(question),
      }),
    },
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

--------------------------------

### Client-side Chat Interface with useChat Hook (TypeScript)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/01-next/25-markdown-chatbot-with-memoization.mdx

This snippet demonstrates setting up a client-side chat interface using the `useChat` hook from `@ai-sdk/react`. It manages chat messages, handles user input submission, and utilizes a `MemoizedMarkdown` component for rendering message content. The example shows how to share a `Chat` instance across components for synchronized state management.

```typescript
"use client";

import { Chat, useChat } from "@ai-sdk/react";
import { DefaultChatTransport } from "ai";
import { useState } from "react";
import { MemoizedMarkdown } from "@/components/memoized-markdown";

const chat = new Chat({
  transport: new DefaultChatTransport({
    api: "/api/chat",
  }),
});

export default function Page() {
  const { messages } = useChat({ chat, experimental_throttle: 50 });

  return (
    <div className="flex flex-col w-full max-w-xl py-24 mx-auto stretch">
      <div className="space-y-8 mb-4">
        {messages.map((message) => (
          <div key={message.id}>
            <div className="font-bold mb-2">
              {message.role === "user" ? "You" : "Assistant"}
            </div>
            <div className="prose space-y-2">
              {message.parts.map((part) => {
                if (part.type === "text") {
                  return (
                    <MemoizedMarkdown
                      key={`${message.id}-text`}
                      id={message.id}
                      content={part.text}
                    />
                  );
                }
              })}
            </div>
          </div>
        ))}
      </div>

      <MessageInput />
    </div>
  );
}

const MessageInput = () => {
  const [input, setInput] = useState("");
  const { sendMessage } = useChat({ chat });

  return (
    <form
      onSubmit={(event) => {
        event.preventDefault();
        sendMessage({
          text: input,
        });
        setInput("");
      }}
    >
      <input
        className="fixed bottom-0 w-full max-w-xl p-2 mb-8 dark:bg-zinc-900 border border-zinc-300 dark:border-zinc-800 rounded shadow-xl"
        placeholder="Say something..."
        value={input}
        onChange={(event) => {
          setInput(event.target.value);
        }}
      />
    </form>
  );
};

```

--------------------------------

### Enable Multi-Step Tool Calls in API Route

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/02-getting-started/05-nuxt.mdx

This code updates a server-side API route (`server/api/chat.ts`) to enable multi-step tool calls for an AI model. By setting `stopWhen: stepCountIs(5)`, the model can perform up to five steps, allowing it to use tool results to refine its answers. It utilizes `ai` SDK, `zod` for schema validation, and `@ai-sdk/openai` for model integration.

```typescript
import {
  streamText,
  UIMessage,
  convertToModelMessages,
  tool,
  stepCountIs,
} from 'ai';
import { createOpenAI } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

export default defineLazyEventHandler(async () => {
  const apiKey = useRuntimeConfig().openaiApiKey;
  if (!apiKey) throw new Error('Missing OpenAI API key');
  const openai = createOpenAI({
    apiKey: apiKey,
  });

  return defineEventHandler(async (event: any) => {
    const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await readBody(event);

    const result = streamText({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
      stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
      tools: {
        weather: tool({
          description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
          inputSchema: z.object({
            location: z
              .string()
              .describe('The location to get the weather for'),
          }),
          execute: async ({ location }) => {
            const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
            return {
              location,
              temperature,
            };
          },
        }),
      },
    });

    return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
  });
});
```

### Slack Event Subscription URL

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/cookbook/00-guides/03-slackbot.mdx

Specifies the URL that Slack will use to send events to the deployed application. This URL, typically ending in '/api/events', needs to be configured in the Slack app's Event Subscriptions settings.

```bash
https://your-vercel-url.vercel.app/api/events
```

### UI Framework Support Expansion

Source: https://github.com/vercel/ai/blob/ai_5_0_0/content/docs/08-migration-guides/37-migration-guide-3-3.mdx

Details on expanded support for UI frameworks like SolidJS, Vue.js, and Svelte, including feature parity and new hooks.

```APIDOC
SolidJS:
  Description: Updated `useChat` and `useCompletion` hooks.
  Features:
    - Achieved feature parity with React implementations.

Vue.js:
  Description: Introduction of new hooks and updates.
  Features:
    - Introduced `useAssistant` hook.

Vue.js / Nuxt:
  Description: Updated examples showcasing latest features.
  Reference:
    - [Nuxt OpenAI examples](https://github.com/vercel/ai/tree/main/examples/nuxt-openai)

Svelte:
  Description: Added tool calling support to `useChat` hook.
```
